The Minimum of Plural: Three or More? The Hanafi Rule and its Proof
Ruling and proof for plural minimum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on the minimum of plural, apply it to a given expression to determine coverage, and explain the proof from linguistic consensus.

Core Idea
Plural in Arabic must cover at least three, proven by the distinct forms of singular, dual, and plural.

How do we know that words like 'slaves' or 'men' require at least three individuals? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi usul rule that plural applies to three or more inclusively—not probabilistically. We'll walk through the ruling, clarify a common misunderstanding, and examine the proof from the consensus of Arabic linguists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Plural Application
Read the passage and extract the core ruling: plural words (e.g., 'rijal', 'qawm') apply to three or more individuals. Note that 'from three to infinity' does not mean probabilistic; it means inclusive of all individuals of whatever number is intended.
The passage uses the example of freeing slaves to illustrate inclusive application.
2
Distinguish Inclusive vs. Probabilistic Application
The text explicitly rejects a probabilistic reading. Understand that when a plural word is used, it covers every individual of the targeted count, not a range. This is key to generality (umum).
If a man says 'my slaves are free' and has exactly three, all three are freed; if ten, all ten—not a random subset.
3
Analyze the Proof from Linguistic Consensus
The proof is ijma: Arabic linguists agree that the forms of singular, dual, and plural are distinct. For these forms to be distinct, the plural must cover a number different from one (singular) and two (dual). Hence, the minimum plural is three.
This proof is based on the structure of Arabic, not on a specific text. It illustrates how usul al-fiqh uses linguistic principles to derive rules.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفاظ عموم کا حکم فالجمع و مافی معتاہ:۔ یہاں سے سب کا حکم بیان فرمارہے ہیں۔ کہ جمع (رجال) اور جو جمع کے معنی میں ہو (رحط قوم) ان کا اطلاق کم از کم تین افراد پر ہو گا اور تین سے لیکر الی مالا تھا یہ تک ان کا اطلاق درست ہے۔ اور اس اطلاق کا مطلب یہ نہیں ہے کہ تین سے لیکر والی مالا تھا یہ پر اطلاق کا احتمال رکھتا ہے کہ تین پر بھی اطلاق کر سکتے ہیں اور تین سے زائد پر بھی اطلاق کر سکتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ عموم کے منافی ہے بلکہ اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ اس جمع کا اطلاق جس عدد معین پر کریں گے تو یہ اس کے تمام افراد کو شامل ہوگا۔ مثلاً کوئی آدمی یہ کہے کہ عبیدی احرار اور اس کے پاس تین غلام ہیں تو یہ عبیدی ان تینوں کو شامل ہوگا اور تینوں آزاد ہو جائیں گے اور اگر اس کے پس دس غلام ہیں تو دس کے دس آزاد ہو جائیں گے۔ لان اقل الجمع :۔ یہاں سے دلیل دے رہے ہیں کہ جمع کا اطلاق کم از کم تین افراد پر ہوتا ہے اور وہ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمع کا کم از کم درجہ تین ہے کیونکہ اصل لغت نے اس بات پر اجماع کیا ہے کہ واحد ، تثنیہ اور جمع کے صیغے سارے ایک دوسرے سے مختلف ہیں اور یہ ختلاف تب ہو سکتا ہے جب جمع کا کم از کم درجہ تین ہو کیونکہ اس کے نیچے ایک پر واحد کا صیغہ دلالت کرتا ہے اور دو پر
The Ruling on Words of Generality: So the plural (rijal) and what is in its meaning (raht, qawm) – these are applied to at least three individuals, and from three to infinity their application is correct. And the meaning of this application is not that it probabilistically means from three to infinity (i.e., that it can apply to three or more), because that would contradict generality. Rather, the meaning is that whatever specific number this plural is applied to, it includes all individuals of that number. For example, if a person says 'my slaves are free' and he has three slaves, then 'my slaves' includes all three and they all become free; if he has ten slaves, all ten become free. The minimum of plural: Here he provides the proof that plural applies to at least three individuals, and the proof is that the minimum level of plural is three, because the original language has consensus that the forms of singular, dual, and plural are all different from each other, and this difference can only occur when the minimum of plural is three, because below three: one is indicated by the singular form, and two by...
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (hukm) about the application of plural words (jama') in Hanafi usul. The commentator states that words like 'rijal' (plural form) and words in the meaning of plural like 'raht' and 'qawm' are applied to three or more individuals. The phrase 'from three to infinity' is clarified: it does not mean that the word probabilistically can mean three or more; rather, it means that whatever number is intended (three, four, etc.), the plural inclusively covers all individuals of that number. For example, if one says 'my slaves are free' and has three slaves, all three are freed; if ten, all ten are freed. The proof (dalil) given is the consensus (ijma) of Arabic linguists that the forms of singular (wahid), dual (tathniyah), and plural (jama') are distinct. For these forms to be distinct, the minimum plural must be three, because singular covers one, dual covers two, so plural must cover three or more. The text cuts off mid-sentence, but the argument is clear.

Key Terms
جمع (jama'): A plural form or word in the meaning of plural, applied to three or more.
اقل الجمع (aqall al-jama'): The minimum number for plural: three, proven by linguistic consensus.
اطلاق (itlaq): The application or usage of a word to its referents; here, the plural is inclusive of all individuals of the intended number.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the plural form necessarily implies a minimum of three individuals, proven by the linguistic consensus on distinct singular, dual, and plural forms.

The Minimum Number for Plural in General Terms
Explaining the ruling on the minimum number for plural and the dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the minimum number for plural and apply it to determine the scope of a general term.

Core Idea
Plural in Arabic general terms minimally indicates three individuals, not two, unless specified otherwise by context.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding the scope of general terms (umum) is foundational. This lesson explores a key rule: a plural form (jam') like 'رجال' or 'قوم' applies to at least three individuals. While this may seem purely linguistic, it has direct implications for how we interpret commands and prohibitions in the Qur'an and Hadith. We'll examine the linguistic evidence, consider an opposing view that allows plural to apply to two, and see how the Hanafi school defends its position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Rule
State the ruling: in general terms, a plural word minimally applies to three individuals. This is based on the linguistic distinction between singular (one), dual (two), and plural (three or more).
This is a default rule; context can specify a different number.
2
Understand the Linguistic Proof
The Arabic language has distinct forms for singular, dual, and plural. Since singular indicates one and dual indicates two, plural must begin at three. This is a consensus of grammarians.
The proof is dalil 'aqli based on language structure.
3
Examine the Opposing View
Some scholars argue plural can apply to two, citing four specific evidences: (1) the inheritance verse using 'ikhwah' (brothers) for two, (2) the verse 'qulubukuma' (your hearts) using plural for two, (3) hadith 'al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah', and (4) the pronoun 'na' in past tense referring to two.
These are specific contexts (inheritance, grammar) not general linguistic rule.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi school refutes by noting that those examples are restricted to their specific contexts (inheritance, bequest, grammar). There is no dispute in those rulings, but the general linguistic principle remains: plural's default is three. General terms retain their scope unless a specific context reduces it.
The key is distinguishing between general rule and specific application.
5
Apply to a Concrete Example
If someone says 'my slaves are free' (عبیدی احرار) and they have three slaves, the statement includes all three. If they have ten, all ten are freed. This shows the plural covers every individual from three upward.
This demonstrates 'umum: the plural includes all individuals of the intended group.

Source Text

الترويج لحل التوضيح والتلويج

الفاظ عموم کا حکم
فالجمع و مافی معناہ:۔ یہاں سے سب کا حکم بیان فرمارہے ہیں۔ کہ جمع (رجال) اور جو جمع کے معنی میں ہو (رہط قوم) ان کا اطلاق کم از کم تین افراد پر ہو گا اور تین سے لے آلی مالا نہایتہ تک ان کا اطلاق درست ہے۔ اور اس اطلاق کا مطلب یہ نہیں ہے کہ تین سے لے کر والی مالا نہایتہ پر اطلاق کا احتمال رکھتا ہے کہ تین پر بھی اطلاق کر سکتے ہیں اور تین سے زائد پر بھی اطلاق کر سکتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ عموم کے منافی ہے بلکہ اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ اس جمع کا اطلاق جس عدد معین پر کریں گے تو یہ اس کے تمام افراد کو شامل ہوگا۔ مثلاً کوئی آدمی یہ کہے کہ عبیدی احرار اور اس کے پاس تین غلام ہیں تو یہ عبیدی ان تینوں کو شامل ہوگا اور تینوں آزاد ہو جائیں گے اور اگر اس کے پاس دس غلام ہیں تو دس کے دس آزاد ہو جائیں گے۔

لان اقل الجمع:۔ یہاں سے دلیل دے رہے ہیں کہ جمع کا اطلاق کم از کم تین افراد پر ہوتا ہے اور وہ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمع کا کم از کم درجہ تین ہے کیونکہ اصل لغت نے اس بات پر اجماع کیا ہے کہ واحد، تثنیہ اور جمع کے صیغے سارے ایک دوسرے سے مختلف ہیں اور یہ اختلاف تب ہو سکتا ہے جب جمع کا کم از کم درجہ تین ہو کیونکہ اس کے نیچے ایک پر واحد کا صیغہ دلالت کرتا ہے اور دو پر تثنیہ کا صیغہ دلالت کرتا ہے تو جمع کی حد تین سے ہی شروع ہوگی۔

جمع کے بارے میں بعض کا مذہب اور ان کے دلائل

و عند البعض اثنان لقولہ:۔ یہاں سے یہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ مذکورہ بالا مذہب جمہور کا تھا کہ جمع کا اطلاق کم از کم تین افراد پر ہوگا۔ بعض حضرات یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جمع کا اطلاق دو پر بھی ہو سکتا ہے تو ان کے نزدیک جمع کا کم از کم درجہ دو ہے۔ اور اس پر وہ چار دلائل پیش کرتے ہیں۔ دلیل (۱) قرآن پاک میں ارشاد ہے فان كان له اخوة فلامه السدس، کہ اگر بہت سے بھائی ہوں تو اس کی ماں کو سدس ملے گا ویسے ماں کا حصہ ثلث ہے لیکن بھائی اس کیلئے حاجب بن جاتے ہیں اس کے حصے کو ثلث سے سدس میں بدل دیتے ہیں۔ اور یہ حجب نقصان جس طرح کئی بھائیوں سے ہوتا ہے اسی طرح دو بھائیوں سے بھی ہو جاتا ہے اب آیت میں اخوة جمع کا صیغہ ہے تو اگر جمع کا اطلاق کم از کم تین پر ہوتا دو پر نہ ہو سکتا تو حجب کیلئے تین بھائیوں کا ہونا ضروری ہوتا دو سے حجب نہ ہوتا۔ حالانکہ دو سے بھی حجب ہوتا ہے تو اخوة سے مراد کم از کم دو بھائی ہوئے لہٰذا معلوم ہوا کہ جمع کا اطلاق دو پر ہو سکتا ہے۔ دلیل (۲) اللہ تعالی کا فرمان ہے فقد صغت قلوبكما، یہاں خطاب حضرت عائشہ اور حضرت حفصہ کو ہے اور یہاں قلوب جمع ہے اس سے حضرت عائشہ اور حضرت حفصہ کا دل مراد ہے تو اس سے دو دل مراد لے سکتے ہیں اب یہاں جمع سے دو فرد مراد لئے جارہے ہیں تو معلوم ہوا کہ جمع کا اطلاق کم از کم دو پر ہوسکتا ہے۔ دلیل (۳) آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا یہ فرمان ہے الاثنان فما فوقهما جماعة تو آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے بھی دو کو جمع شمار کیا ہے۔ دلیل (۴) ماضی کی گردان میں جمع متکلم کا صیغہ فعلنا، یہاں نا ضمیر جمع کی ہے لیکن اس کا اطلاق دو پر بھی ہوتا ہے۔

بعض حضرات کے ادلہ کے جوابات: ولا نزاع في الارث والوصیۃ سے ان چاروں دلیلوں کے جواب ہیں۔ جواب دلیل اول: فان كان له اخوة ' میراث کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور میراث وصیت کے بارے میں بالاتفاق ہے دو بھی جمع میں داخل ہوتے ہیں تو آپ نے بھی اس آیت سے میراث میں یہ ثابت کیا ہے کہ دو جمع میں داخل ہیں اور ہم تمام حالات کی بات کر رہے ہیں یعنی مطلقا بغیر کسی خاص حالت کے جمع کا اطلاق دو پر نہیں ہو سکتا تو آپ کو
The ruling on general words: al-jam' (plural) and what is in its meaning. Here it explains the ruling for all. That jam' (e.g., rijal) and what is in the meaning of jam' (e.g., raht, qawm) applies to at least three individuals, and from three upwards to infinity its application is valid. This application does not mean it has probability of applying to three or more, because that contradicts 'umum (generality). Rather, it means that when this plural is applied to a specific number, it includes all its individuals. For example, if a man says 'my slaves are free' and he has three slaves, it includes all three and all become free; if he has ten, all ten become free. The proof that the minimum of jam' is three is that the Arabic language has consensus that the forms of singular, dual, and plural are distinct from each other, and this distinction can only be if the minimum of plural is three, because below that, one is indicated by singular and two by dual, so the limit of plural starts from three. Regarding the view of some that plural can apply to two: they present four proofs: (1) Quran: 'if he has brothers, his mother gets one-sixth' – brothers (ikhwah) is plural, and the hijab (blocking) effect occurs with two brothers as well, so ikhwah must include two. (2) Quran: 'your hearts have inclined' – hearts (qulub) is plural and refers to two hearts. (3) Hadith: 'two and above are a congregation' – two counted as a congregation. (4) Conjugation: the past tense form fa'alna has plural pronoun na which can apply to two. The refutation: there is no dispute in inheritance and bequest that two are included in plural, but the general linguistic principle is that plural applies to three; these examples are specific contexts, not general.
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage from Altarweeh begins by stating the rule (hukm) regarding general words (alfaz al-umum). It first clarifies that plural (jam') words like 'رجال' (men) and words conveying the meaning of plural like 'رہط' (group) and 'قوم' (people) minimally apply to three individuals. The author emphasizes that this does not mean the plural is ambiguous between three and more; rather, it definitively applies to any specific number from three upward, including all individuals of that number. For example, if someone says 'my slaves are free' and has exactly three or ten slaves, all are freed. The linguistic proof (dalil) for the minimum of three is the clear distinction in Arabic between singular, dual, and plural forms; since singular indicates one and dual two, plural must begin at three, as agreed upon by grammarians. The passage then presents an ikhtilaf: some scholars hold that plural can apply to two, citing four proofs: (1) the inheritance verse where 'اخوة' (brothers) includes two in the ruling of hijab (reducing the mother's share); (2) the verse 'قلوبكما' (your two hearts) using plural 'قلوب' for two; (3) the hadith 'الاثنان فما فوقهما جماعة' (two and above are a congregation); (4) the pronoun 'نا' in past tense conjugations like 'فعلنا' applying to two. The Hanafi response (jawaab) refutes these by noting that there is no dispute in inheritance and bequest that two are included in plural in those specific contexts, but the general linguistic rule remains that plural minimally means three. The examples are limited to their specific fields (inheritance, grammar) and do not change the universal principle.

Key Terms
جمع (jam'): Plural form in Arabic, minimally applying to three individuals in Hanafi usul
عموم (umum): Generality of a term covering all individuals without exclusion
اقل الجمع (aqall al-jam'): The minimum number for plural, which Hanafis hold to be three

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The minimum for plural in general terms is three in Hanafi usul, based on linguistic consensus, and this rule governs the interpretation of general commands except where context specifies otherwise.

The Minimum for Plural (Jam‘): Linguistic Consensus vs. Evidence from Texts
Disputing the minimum number for plural in Arabic and Hanafi response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the minimum number for the plural in Arabic and refute each of the four opposing arguments.

Core Idea
The literal plural requires three; any use for two is context-specific or metaphorical.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, determining whether a term is general (amm) or specific (khass) often hinges on the word's literal meaning. One key dispute is the minimum number for the plural in Arabic. This lesson examines the arguments of those who claim the plural can mean two and the Hanafi response, which defends the linguistic consensus that plural begins at three. Understanding this dispute is crucial for correctly interpreting general commands in the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi school's ruling on the minimum number for the plural in Arabic. Note that they follow the majority (jumhūr) view that the literal plural applies to three or more.
The dual (tathniyya) is a separate grammatical category.
2
Identify the opposing view and its four proofs
List the four proofs presented by those who claim the plural can mean two: (1) Quran 4:11 'ikhwatun' for brothers in inheritance, (2) Quran 66:4 'qulūbukumā' for two hearts, (3) Hadith 'al-ithnāni famā fawqahumā jamā‘atun', (4) the Arabic suffix '-nā' used for both dual and plural.
Note that the opponents are not named but represent a minority view.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to each proof
For each of the four proofs, explain the Hanafi refutation as presented in the text: (1) inheritance verse is a specific context where two are included by agreement, (2) 'qulūb' is metaphorical (majāz) due to dual addition, (3) the hadith is specific to inheritance, prayer, or travel, (4) '-nā' is shared between dual and plural.
The Hanafi responses rely on distinguishing absolute (mutlaq) from context-specific usage.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Explain the practical impact: if a general command uses a plural form, the Hanafi interpreter requires at least three individuals for the ruling to apply absolutely. In specific contexts (like inheritance), two may be included by convention, but this does not change the linguistic rule.
This affects how jurists interpret texts like 'O you who believe' (khitāb) or general commands.

اخوۃ سے مراد کم از کم دو بھائی ہوئے لھذا معلوم ہوا کہ جمع کا اطلاق دو پر ہو سکتا ہے۔ دلیل :(۲): اللہ تعالی کا فرمان ہے فقد صحت قلوبكما ، یہاں خطاب حضرت امتنا عائشہ اور اسی حصہ کو ہے اور یہاں قلوب جمع ہے اس سے حضرت امی عائشہ اور حضرت حفصہ کا دل مراد ہے تو اس سے دو دل مراد لے سکتے ہیں اب یہاں جمع سے دو فرد مراد لیئے جارہے ہیں تو معلوم ہوا کہ جمع کا اطلاق کم از کم دو پر ہوسکتا ہے۔ دلیل (۳) آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ فرمان ہے الاثنان فما فوقهما جماعة" تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بھی دو کو جمع شمار کیا ہے۔ دلیل (۴):۔ ماضی کی گردان میں جمع متکلم کا صیغہ ہے فعلنا ، یہاں 'نا' ضمیر جمع کی ہے لیکن اس کا اطلاق دو پر بھی ہوتا بعض حضرات کے ادلہ کے جوابات: ولا نزاع في الارث والوصیۃ سے ان چاروں دلیلوں کے جواب ہیں۔ جواب دلیل اول: فاذا كان له اخوة ' میراث کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور میراث وصیت کے بارے میں بالاتفاق ہے دو بھی جمع میں داخل ہوتے ہیں تو آپ نے بھی اس آیت سے میراث میں یہ ثابت کیا ہے کہ دو جمع میں داخل ہیں اور ہم تمام حالات کی بات کر رہے ہیں یعنی مطلقا بغیر کسی خاص حالت کے جمع کا اطلاق دو پر نہیں ہو سکتا تو آپ کو ایسی دلیل دینی چاہیے تھی جو مطلق ہو۔ یہ دلیل درست نہیں ہے۔ جواب دلیل ثانی: فقد صنعت قلوبکما پس قلوب سے مجاز آدو دل مراد لیے گئے ہیں اور یہ مجاز دو دل مراد لینے پر قرینہ یہ ہے کہ قلوب کی اضافت تثنیہ کی طرف کی گئی ہے تو دو افراد کے دل بھی دو ہوں گے تو معلوم ہوا یہاں مجازاً تثنیہ مراد ہے۔ اور مجاز ا تو جمع سے ایک فرد بھی مراد لیا جا سکتا ہے لھدایہ کوئی ذلیل نہیں ہے۔ جواب اول دلیل ثالث الانسان فما فوقهما جماعة، والی حدیث میراث اور وصیت کے بارے میں وارد ہوئی ہے اور میراث اور وصیت میں تو دو کے جمع میں داخل ہونے میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ جواب ثانی یا یہ جواب بھی دیا جاسکتا ہے کہ یہ حدیث اس بارے میں وارد ہوئی ہے کہ اگر امام کیساتھ نماز میں دو آدمی ہوں تو امام کے کھڑا ہونے کا طریقہ کیا ہے؟ تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اس بارے میں دو آدمی جماعت کے حکم میں ہیں کہ جو طریقہ جماعت کیساتھ کھڑا ہونے کا ہے وہی دو آدمیوں کے ہوتے ہوئے بھی ہوگا۔ امام ایک صف مقتدیوں سے آگے کھڑا اسے آگے کی ہوگا نہ ایسے جیسے ایک آدمی کے ہوتے ہوئے کھڑا ہوتا ہے یعنی بائیں جانب ایک قدم آگے۔ تو یہ حدیث ایک خاص حالت کے بارے میں وارد ہوئی ہے نہ کہ مطلقاً اور ہم مطلقا کم از کم تین افراد مراد لینے کی بات کر رہے ہیں۔ جواب ثالث:۔ اور یہ جواب بھی دیا جا سکتا ہے کہ یہ حدیث سفر کے بارے میں وارد ہوتی ہے۔ کہ پہلے پہلے جب اسلام کو غلبہ نہیں ہوا تھا، ایک یا دو آدمیوں کو سفر کرنے کی اجازت نہیں تھی آپ کا فرمان ہے ' الواحد شيطان والالنان شيطانان والعلقة ركب لیکن جب اسلام کو غلبہ ہوا تو آپ نے دو کو بھی سفر کرنے کی اجازت دے دی۔ اور یہ فرمایا " الانسان فما فوقهما جماعة ، تو يحدیث خاص سفر کی حالت میں نازل ہوئی ہے نہ کہ مطلقا لھذا اس حدیث سے بھی استدلال کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ اور ہاں یہ تاویلیں ہم نے اس لیئے کی ہیں کہ اگر اس حدیث کو ظا ہر پر محمول کریں تو اس میں اصل لغت کے اجماع کی مخالفت لازم آئے گی۔ جواب دلیل رابع : فعلنا جمع متکلم) سے آپ کا دلیل پکڑنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ نا ضمیر صرف جمع کیلئے وضع نہیں کی گئی بلکہ یہ مشترک ہے منیہ اور جمع دونوں کیلئے وضع کی گئی ہے اس لیئے اس سے جمع بھی مراد لیتے ہیں اور تشنہ بھی مراد لیتے ہیں لھذا یہ دلیل بھی درست نہیں۔ یہ دلیل جب درست ہوتی جب نا اضمیر کی صرف جمع کیلئے وضع ہوتی اور اس سے مراد
Regarding the opinion of some about the plural and their proofs: And according to some, two [is the minimum] because of His saying... From here it is explained that the aforementioned opinion was that of the majority, that the plural applies to at least three persons. Some say that the plural can also apply to two, so according to them the minimum degree of plural is two. And upon that they present four proofs. Proof 1: In the Holy Quran it is said 'fa in kāna lahu ikhwatun fa li-ummihi al-sudus' – if he has brothers, then his mother gets one-sixth. The mother's share is normally one-third, but brothers become a preventer (hājib) and change her share to one-sixth. And this reduction occurs just as with many brothers, so too with two brothers. Now in the verse 'ikhwatun' is a plural form. If the plural only applied to at least three, then for the reduction to occur, three brothers would be necessary, and it would not occur with two. But in fact, reduction does occur with two, so 'ikhwah' means at least two brothers. Hence it is known that the plural can apply to two. Proof 2: Allah's saying 'fa qad ṣaghat qulūbukumā' – here the address is to our mother Aisha and the other [Hafsa], and 'qulūb' is plural, referring to the hearts of Aisha and Hafsa, so two hearts are meant. Thus, from this plural, two individuals are intended, so it is known that the plural can apply to at least two. Proof 3: The Prophet ﷺ said 'al-ithnāni famā fawqahumā jamā'atun' – two and above are a congregation. So the Prophet ﷺ also counted two as plural. Proof 4: In the conjugation of the past tense, the plural first person form is 'fa'alnā'. Here 'nā' is a plural pronoun, but it applies also to two. Responses to the proofs of some people: 'And there is no dispute regarding inheritance and bequest' – from this the responses to all four proofs. Response to proof 1: 'fa in kāna lahu ikhwatun' was revealed regarding inheritance, and it is agreed upon that in inheritance and bequest, two are included in the plural. You have proved from this verse that two are included in the plural in inheritance, but we are speaking about all circumstances – i.e., absolutely, without any specific condition, the plural cannot apply to two. So you should have presented a proof that is absolute. This proof is not valid. Response to proof 2: 'fa qad ṣaghat qulūbukumā' – here 'qulūb' is used metaphorically (majāz) to mean two hearts, and the indication that it is metaphorical is that 'qulūb' is added to a dual, so the hearts of two individuals are two. So it is known that here metaphorically the dual is intended. And metaphorically, it is possible to intend even one individual from a plural, so this is not a proof. First response to proof 3: The hadith 'al-ithnāni famā fawqahumā jamā'atun' was reported regarding inheritance and bequest, and in inheritance and bequest there is no dispute that two are included in the plural. Second response: Or it can be said that this hadith was reported regarding the case when two people are with the imam in prayer, concerning the way the imam stands. The Prophet ﷺ said that in this matter, two people are like a congregation – the way of standing with a congregation is the same for two people. The imam stands ahead of the row, not like when there is one person where he stands slightly forward to the left. So this hadith was reported for a specific situation, not absolutely, and we are speaking about the absolute minimum of three persons. Third response: This response can also be given: that this hadith is about travel. In the early days when Islam had not yet prevailed, one or two persons were not allowed to travel. The Prophet ﷺ said 'al-wāḥidu shayṭān, wa al-ithnāni shayṭānāni, wa al-thalāthatu rakb' – but when Islam prevailed, he allowed two to travel and said 'al-ithnāni famā fawqahumā jamā'atun'. So this hadith was revealed specifically about travel, not absolutely. Therefore, using this hadith as proof is not correct. And we have given these interpretations because if we take the hadith literally, it would contradict the consensus of the Arabic language. Response to proof 4: Your use of 'fa'alnā' (plural first person) as proof is not valid because the pronoun 'nā' was not coined only for the plural, but it is shared between the dual and the plural. For this reason, we use it for both plural and dual. So this proof is also not valid. It would be valid only if 'nā' had been coined for the plural alone.
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilāf) regarding the minimum number for the plural (jam‘) in Arabic, a key issue in uṣūl al-fiqh because many legal rulings turn on whether a term is considered general (ʿāmm) or specific. The Hanafī position, following the majority (jumhūr), holds that the literal plural requires at least three. Some unidentified scholars argue that two suffices, citing four proofs. The author systematically refutes each: (1) The inheritance verse about brothers is specific to inheritance law, where it is agreed that two are included, but this does not prove the absolute linguistic meaning. (2) The word 'qulūb' in the Qur’ān is used metaphorically (majāz), as indicated by its addition to a dual pronoun; metaphor can stretch meanings. (3) The hadith 'al-ithnāni famā fawqahumā jamā‘atun' is interpreted in three ways: it either applies to inheritance, to the imam’s position in prayer, or to travel permits—all specific contexts. Taking it literally would contradict the consensus of Arabic. (4) The pronoun '-nā' is shared between dual and plural, so it does not prove the plural includes two. The Hanafī response defends the linguistic consensus that the plural starts at three, and any usage for two is either convention (ʿurf) or metaphor. This analysis is crucial for determining the scope of ʿāmm and khaṣṣ in legal texts.

Key Terms
جمع (jam‘): Plural in Arabic grammar; in this passage, the minimum number for its literal application.
تثنية (tathniyya): Dual number, specifically referring to two.
مجاز (majāz): Metaphorical or figurative usage of a word, not its literal meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the author rebut the proof from the hadith 'al-ithnāni famā fawqahumā jamā'atun' that the plural includes two?
A) He accepts it as valid proof for the absolute meaning.
B) He says the hadith is weak.
C) He says the hadith is specific to inheritance, prayer, or travel, not absolute.
D) He says it is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The literal plural in Arabic requires three; any apparent use for two is a specific convention or metaphor, not the linguistic rule.

Rule for Specifying the Collective Noun to Three and Singular to One
States the principle for specifying collective and singular nouns

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for specifying collective and singular nouns, and apply it to identify the minimum number after takhsis.

Core Idea
A collective noun can only be specified to three, preserving its original meaning; a singular can be specified to one.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding the limits of takhsis (specification) is crucial for correctly interpreting general commands in the Quran and Sunnah. This lesson explains a fundamental linguistic rule: a collective noun cannot be specified to fewer than three individuals, while a singular noun is specified to one. This rule ensures that general terms retain their primary meaning until clear evidence limits them.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the linguistic basis
Understand that the Arabic plural (jam') linguistically denotes three or more. This is a fixed definition in Hanafi usul.
2
Identify the minimum of the plural
The text states: 'إِنَّ أَقَلَّ الْجَمْعِ ثَلَاثَةٌ' – the least of the plural is three. Therefore, specification cannot reduce it below three.
This is a corollary (ta'qib) from the definition.
3
Distinguish the type of specifier
Specification must be done with an independent word (mustaqill) or a word in its meaning (like rahT and qawm). These are words that themselves indicate a group.
4
Apply to singular nouns
A singular noun can be specified to one. An example is when a plural form is used with a singular intent, like 'لا أتزوج النساء' (I will not marry women), which can be specified to one woman.
5
Relate to Quranic interpretation
The word 'ta'ifah' is treated like a singular, as seen in Ibn Abbas's tafsir of verse 9:122, where a single group is intended.
This shows practical application of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَيَصِحُ تَخْصِيصُ الْجَمْعِ ) تَعْقِيبٌ لِقَوْلِهِ إِنَّ أَقَلَّ الْجَمْعِ ثَلَاثَةٌ ، وَالْمُرَادُ التَّخْصِيصُ بِالْمُسْتَقِلْ ) وَمَا فِي مَعْنَاهُ ) كَالرَّهْطِ، وَالْقَوْمِ ( إلَى الثَّلاثَةِ ، وَالْمُفْرَدِ) بِالجَرِّ عَطَفٌ عَلَى الجَمْعِ أَى الْمُفْرَدُ الْحَقِيقِيُّ ( كَالرَّجُلٍ ) وَمَا فِي مَعْنَاهُ كَالْجَمْعِ الَّذِى يُرَادُ بِهِ الْوَاحِدُ ) نَحْو لَا أَتَزَوَّجُ النِّسَاءَ إِلَى الْوَاحِدِ ) أَى يَصِحُ تَخْصِيصُ الْمُفْرَدِ إلَى الْوَاحِدِ ) وَالطَّائِفَةُ كَالْمُفْرَدِ ) بِهَذَا فَسَّرَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ الله تَعَالَى عَنْهُمَا قَوْله تَعَالَى ( فَلَوْلا نَفَرَ مِنْ كُلِّ فِرْقَةٍ مِنْهُمْ طَائِفَةٌ ) .
ترجمہ: (پس صحیح ہے جمع کی تخصیص) تفریع ہے اس کے قول لان اقل الجمع ثلاثہ کے اور مراد تخصیص سے مستقل کیساتھ ہے اور وہ جو جمع کے معنی میں ہو ) جیسا کہ رھط اور قوم ہے (تین تک اور مفرد ) جر کیسا تھ عطف ہے جمع پر یعنی مفرد حقیقی ) جیسا کہ رجل ہے اور وہ کہ جو مفرد کے معنی میں ہو ) جیسا کہ وہ جمع جس سے مراد واحد ہو (جیسے لا اتزوج النساء ہے ایک تک) یعنی صحیح ہے مفرد کی تخصیص ایک تک ( اور لفظ طائفہ مثل مفرد کے ہے) اور اسی کیسا تھ تفسیر کی ہے حضرت ابن عباس نے اللہ تعالی کے قول فَلَوْلا نَفَرَ مِن كُلِّ فِرْقَةٍ مِّنْهُم طَائِفَةٌ -
So specification of the collective is valid – it is a corollary to his statement that the minimum of the collective is three. And what is meant is specification with an independent [word] and what is in its meaning like 'rahT' and 'qawm' to three. And [specification of] the singular – by jar, an 'atf' on the collective, meaning the real singular like 'rajul' and what is in its meaning like the collective by which the one is intended, such as 'la atazawwaju al-nisa'' [I will not marry women] to one. That is, specification of the singular to one is valid. And the word 'ta'ifah' is like the singular. With this, Ibn Abbas interpreted the saying of Allah Most High: 'Then why did not a company from every faction of them go forth...'
Translation: (So specification of the collective is valid) – a corollary to his statement 'that the minimum of the collective is three', and what is meant by specification is with an independent [word] and what is in its meaning) like 'rahT' and 'qawm' (to three. And [specification of] the singular – by jar, an 'atf' on the collective, meaning the real singular) like 'rajul' (and what is in its meaning like the collective by which the one is intended) such as 'la atazawwaju al-nisa'' [I will not marry women] (to one. That is, specification of the singular to one is valid. And the word 'ta'ifah' is like the singular. And this is how Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, interpreted the saying of Allah Most High: 'Then why did not a company from every faction of them go forth...')
Source pages p. 601

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul al-fiqh rule concerning the valid scope of takhsis (specification) of general terms. The author explains that a collective noun (jama') can be specified only to a minimum of three, because the plural linguistically requires at least three. This is based on the definition that the least of the plural is three. Specification is allowed when using an independent specifying word (mustaqill) or words that carry the meaning of the plural like 'rahT' (group) and 'qawm' (people). Similarly, a singular noun can be specified to one, as in the example 'I will not marry women' (a plural form intended as general) specified to one woman. The word 'ta'ifah' (party/section) is treated like a singular, so it can also be specified to one. The author cites Ibn Abbas's tafsir of the verse (9:122) where 'ta'ifah' means a single group. This rule is crucial in Hanafi usul for determining how general commands and prohibitions can be limited.

Key Terms
تَخْصِيص (takhsis): Specification: limiting a general term to a subset of its individuals.
جَمْع (jam'): A plural noun, which in Arabic is assigned to three or more individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
To what number can a collective noun (jam') be specified according to this Hanafi usul rule?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a collective noun can only be specified to a minimum of three, while a singular noun can be specified to one.

Specifying a General Plural or Singular
Explaining the permissibility of specifying general words down to their minimum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a general plural can be specified down to three and a general singular down to one, and identify the exceptional case of 'ta'ifah'.

Core Idea
A general plural cannot be specified below three; a general singular can be specified to one.

This passage examines the limits of specification (takhsis) for general words. In Hanafi usul, the general plural (al-jam') has a minimum of three, so any specification must leave at least three individuals. The general singular (al-mufrad) can be specified down to one. The word 'ta'ifah' is treated like a singular because it can refer to one person, as shown by Ibn Abbas's tafsir of Quran 9:122.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of general word
Determine whether the word is a general plural (like 'al-rijal', 'al-qawm') or a general singular (like 'al-rajul'). Also note words like 'ta'ifah' that are semantically general but syntactically singular.
The text distinguishes between true plurals and words that function like plurals (e.g., raht, qawm) and true singulars and words that function like singulars (e.g., ta'ifah).
2
Determine the specification minimum
Apply the Hanafi rule: a general plural can be specified down to three individuals (the minimum of plural). A general singular can be specified down to one. For words treated like singulars (ta'ifah), the minimum is also one.
Specification below three for a plural would negate the very meaning of plurality.
3
Analyze the word 'ta'ifah'
Understand that 'ta'ifah' is lexically general (can refer to one or more) but is treated as a singular for specification. The proof comes from Ibn Abbas's tafsir where he interpreted 'ta'ifah' in Quran 9:122 as one person.
This shows that a general word can be specified to a single individual when the context allows.
4
Verify with the dalil
Connect the ruling to the primary evidence: Quran 9:122 and the interpretation of Ibn Abbas. The verse uses 'ta'ifah' generally, but Ibn Abbas specified it to one, validating the permissibility of such specification.
The dalil demonstrates that specification does not contradict the original generality when the lower limit is respected.

Source Text

الترويحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيعِ وَالتَّلويح دو بھی لیے جاتے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔
) فَيَصِحُ تَخْصِيصُ الْجَمْعِ ) تَعْقِيبٌ لِقَوْلِهِ إِنَّ أَقَلَّ الْجَمْعِ ثَلَاثَةٌ ، وَالْمُرَادُ التَّخْصِيصُ بِالْمُسْتَقِلْ ) وَمَا فِي مَعْنَاهُ ) كَالرَّهْطِ، وَالْقَوْمِ ( إلَى الثَّلاثَةِ ، وَالْمُفْرَدِ) بِالجَرٌ عَطَفٌ عَلَى الجَمْعِ أَى الْمُفَرَدُ الْحَقِيقِيُّ ( كَالرَّجُلٍ ) وَمَا فِي مَعْنَاهُ كَالْجَمْعِ الَّذِى يُرَادُ بِهِ الْوَاحِدُ ) نَحْو لَا أَتَزَوَّجُ النِّسَاءَ إِلَى الْوَاحِدِ ) أَى يَصِحُ تَخْصِيصُ الْمُفْرَدِ إلَى الْوَاحِدِ ) وَالطَّائِفَةُ كَالْمُفْرَدِ ) بِهَذَا فَسَّرَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ الله تَعَالَى عَنْهُمَا قَوْله تَعَالَى ( فَلَوْلا نَفَرَ مِنْ كُلِّ فِرْقَةٍ مِنْهُمْ طَائِفَةٌ ) .
ترجمہ:۔ (پس صحیح ہے جمع کی تخصیص) تفریح ہے اس کے قول لان اقل الجمع ثلاثہ کے اور مراد تخصیص سے مستقل کیساتھ ہے اور وہ جو جمع کے معنی میں ہو ) جیسا کہ رهط اور قوم ہے (تین تک اور مفرد ) جر کیسا تھ عطف ہے جمع پر یعنی مفرد حقیقی ) جیسا کہ رجل ہے اور وہ کہ جو مفرد کے معنی میں ہو ) جیسا کہ وہ جمع جس سے مراد واحد ہو (جیسے لا اتزوج النساء ہے ایک تک) یعنی صحیح ہے مفرد کی تخصیص ایک تک ( اور لفظ طائفہ مثل مفرد کے ہے) اور اسی کیسا تھ تفسیر کی ہے حضرت ابن عباس نے اللہ تعالی کے قول فَلَوْلا نَفَرمَن كُلِّ فِرْقَةً مِّنْهُم طَائِفَةٌ -
جمع کی تخصیص تین افراد تک ہو سکتی ہے اس سے کم نہیں
فیصح تخصیص الجمع :۔ جب یہ بیان ہو چکا کہ جمع عام ہے اور اس کا اطلاق تین اور اسے زائد پر ہوتا ہے تواب ماتین تفریع ہو متفرع کرتے ہوئے فرمارہے ہیں کہ اگر جمع میں تخصیص کی جائے اور تخصیص بھی مستقل کے ذریعے ہو یا اس لفظ میں تخصیص کی جائے جو جمع کے معنی میں ہو جیسا کہ قوم اور ربط ہے تو یہ تخصیص تین افراد تک جائز ہے جب جمع یا جو جمع کے معنی میں ہے اس کے تحت تین افراد باقی رہ جائیں گے تو اس کے بعد مزید تخصیص جائز نہیں ہوگی بلکہ تین افراد پر حکم ضرور صادق آئے گا کیونکہ تین افراد سے کم تخصیص عام کو جمع پر دلالت سے نکال دیتا ہے حالانکہ جمع کی اصل وضع کم از کم تین افراد کے لیئے ہے اور اگر عام مفرد ہو جیسے رجل اور جو اس کے معنی میں ہو جیسے النساء اس میں واحد تک تخصیص جائز ہے کیونکہ مفرد کی اصل وضع واحد کے لئے ہے اس لئے تخصیص اس کو اصل وضع پر دلالت سے نہیں نکالتی ۔ والطائفہ کا لمفرو:۔ یہاں سے ماتن نے لفظ طائفہ کے بارے میں فائدہ بیان کیا ہے کہ یہ لفظ حقیقتا مفرد تو نہیں لیکن مفرد
کی طرح ہے تو جس طرح مفرد میں ایک فرد تک تخصیص ہو سکتی ہے اسی طرح لفظ طائفہ میں بھی ایک فرد تک تخصیص ہو سکتی ہے اور اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طائفہ کا لغوی معنی ہے قطعہ آگے عام ہے کہ واحد ہو یا اس سے زیادہ چنانچہ حضرت ابن عباس نے اللہ تعالی کے قول فلولا نفر من كل فرقة منهم طائفة کی تفسیر میں اسی طرح فرمایا ہے کہ طائفہ سے مراد واحد ہے۔
It is valid to specify the plural — a clarification of his statement that the minimum of the plural is three, and the intended meaning is specification with something independent and what is in its meaning, like raht and qawm, down to three. And the singular (in the genitive, coordinated to the plural) i.e., the true singular, like rajul, and what is in its meaning like a plural intended as one, e.g., 'I do not marry women' down to one, i.e., it is valid to specify the singular down to one. And the word ta'ifah is like the singular. With this, Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) interpreted the saying of Allah Almighty: 'So if not a group from every section of them go forth...'
Source pages p. 601

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the general word (عام) in the context of specification (تخصیص). The author states that a general plural can be specified down to three individuals because the minimum of a plural is three. Specification to less than three would negate the very meaning of plurality. Similarly, a general singular can be specified down to one. The word 'ta'ifah' (group) is treated like a singular because it can refer to a single person, as evidenced by Ibn Abbas's tafsir of Quran 9:122. The commentary follows the author's order: first the ruling on plural, then on singular, then on 'ta'ifah'. The proof from Ibn Abbas shows that the general word can be specified to a single individual when the context allows.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam'): A general plural referring to three or more individuals.
المفرد (al-mufrad): A general singular referring to one individual.
الطائفَة (al-ta'ifah): A lexically general word that can refer to one or more, treated as a singular for specification.

Key Takeaway
A general plural cannot be specified below three, while a general singular can be specified to one; the word 'ta'ifah' is like a singular.

The Plural with Definite Article – Indicating Generality
Defining the plural with definite article as a general expression

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a plural with the definite article indicates generality and apply the Hanafi hierarchy of ال to derive a ruling.

Core Idea
Without a covenant, the definite article on a plural defaults to generality, not the essence.

In Hanafi usul, a key expression of generality (عام) is the plural noun with the definite article (al-jam' al-mu'arraf bi al-lam). This lesson unpacks why such a form indicates all individuals of the genus when no specific group (عهد) is intended. The reasoning follows a careful hierarchy of the functions of ال: first covenant, then generality, then definition of nature. The classical proof from the hadith 'الأئمة من قريش' shows how Abu Bakr (ra) used this principle to settle the caliphate debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expression type
Notice that the passage introduces 'الجمع المعرف باللام' as a type of 'عام'. Recognize that a plural with ال is different from a singular with ال because a singular can indicate the essence (ماهية) but a plural cannot.
The plural refers to individuals, not to the essence as such.
2
Learn the hierarchy of the definite article
The passage lists three possible meanings of ال: covenant (عهد), generality (استغراق), and definition of nature (تعريف الطبيعة). It then establishes a hierarchy: covenant is the default, then generality, then definition of nature. Understand why covenant is preferred: because when a specific group is already known (externally or mentally), carrying ال on that certain part is more economical.
The principle is 'al-'ahd huwa al-asl'.
3
Apply the hierarchy to a plural
For a plural with ال, if there is no known covenant (no previous mention or mental presence), it cannot indicate the essence (as plurals denote individuals), so it must default to generality. The passage argues that without a covenant, the plural indicates all individuals of the genus.
This is the core ruling: the plural with ال is عام (general) when not mu'ahhad.
4
Examine the dalil – the hadith of Quraysh
The passage cites the hadith 'الأئمة من قريش' as evidence. Abu Bakr (ra) used it to argue that all leaders must be from Quraysh. The force of the argument relies on the fact that 'الأئمة' is a plural with ال and no covenant was present, so it indicates generality: every imam (leader) is from Quraysh.
This is a practical application of the usul rule.
5
Confirm the derived ruling
From the hadith, we derive that all leaders (in the context of caliphate) must be from Quraysh. This ruling is general and binding unless a specific exception is proven. Note that this is a textual generality (عموم لفظي) that is qat'i in dalala according to Hanafi usul.
The ruling is not just historical; it demonstrates the usul principle in action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا ( أَى مِنْ أَلْفَاظِ الْعَام ) الْجَمْعُ الْمُعَرَّفَ بِاللَّامِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنُ مَعْهُودًا لَّانَّ المُعَرَّفَ لَيْسَ هُوَ الْمَاهِيَّةَ فِى الْجَمْعِ ، وَلَا بَعْضَ الْأَفْرَادِ لِعَدَمِ الْأَوْلَوِيَّةِ فَتَعَيَّنَ الْكُلُّ اعْلَمُ أَنَّ لَامَ الشَّعَرِيفِ إِمَّا لِلْعَهْدِ الْخَارِجِيِّ أَو الذَّهَنِي ، وَإِمَّا لِاسْتِغْرَاقِ الْجِنسِ ، وَإِمَّا لِتَعْرِيفِ الطَّبِيعَةِ لَكِنَّ الْعَهْدَ هُوَ الْأَصْلُ ثُمَّ الِاسْتِغْرَاقُ ثُمَّ تَعْرِيف الطَّبِيعَةِ لِأنّ اللفظ الَّذِي يَدْخُلُ عَلَيْهِ اللَّامُ دَالّ عَلَى الْمَاهِيَّةِ بِدُونِ اللَّامِ فَحَمْلُ اللام عَلَى الْفَائِدَةِ الجَدِيدَةِ أَوْلَى مِنْ حَمْلِهِ عَلَى تَعْرِيفِ الطَّبِيعَةِ ، وَالْفَائِدَةِ الْجَدِيدَةِ أَمَّا تَعْرِيفُ الْعَهْدِ أَوْ اسْتِغْرَاقُ الْجِنْسِ ، وَتَعْرِيفُ الْعَهْدِ أَوْلَى مِنْ الاسْتِغْرَاقِ  ِلأَنَّهُ إِذَا ذُكِرَ بَعْضَ أَفْرَادِ الْجِنْسِ خَارِجًا أَوْ ذِهَنًا فَحَمُلُ اللَّامِ عَلَى ذَلِكَ الْبَعْضِ الْمَذْكُورِ أَوْلَى مِنْ حَمْلِهِ عَلَى جَمِيعِ الْأَفْرَادِ لِأَنَّ الْبَعْضَ مُتَيَقَّنٌ ، وَالكُلَّ مُحْتَمَلٌ فَإِذَا عُلِمَ ذَلِكَ فَفِي الْجَمْعِ الْمُحَلَّى ، بِالْأَلِفِ ، وَاللَّامِ لَا يُمْكِنُ حَمْلُهُ بِطَرِيقِ الْحَقِيقَةِ عَلَى تَعْرِيفِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ لأَنَّ الْجَمْعَ وُضِعَ لِأَفْرَادِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ لَا لِلْمَاهِيَّةِ مِنْ حَيْثُ هِيَ لِكُلِّ يُحْمَلُ عَلَيْهَا بِطَرِيقِ الْمَجَازِ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي فِي هَذِهِ الصَّفْحَةِ ، وَلَا يُمْكِنُ حَمُلُهُ عَلَى الْعَهْدِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ عَهْدٌ فَقَوْلُهُ ، وَلَا بَعْضَ الْأَفْرَادِ لِعَدَمِ الْأوْلَوِيَّةِ إِشَارَةٌ
( إلَى هَذَا فَتَعَيْنَ الاسْتِغْرَاقُ ، وَلِتَمَسُّكِهِمُ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلام ) الأئِمَّةُ مِنْ قُرَيْشٍ ) ( لَمَّا ، وَقَعَ الاخْتِلافُ بَعْدَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ في الخلاقَةِ ، وَقَالَ الأَنصَارُ مِنَّا أَمِيرٌ ، وَمِنكُمْ أَمِيرٌ تَمَسَّكَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ
And among them (i.e., among the expressions of the general) is the plural defined with the lam (definite article) when it is not known by covenant, because the defined is not the essence in the plural, nor a part of the individuals due to lack of priority, so the whole is determined. Know that the lam of definition is either for external or mental covenant, or for generality (istighraq) of the genus, or for definition of the nature. But covenant is the original, then generality, then definition of the nature, because the word that enters upon it the lam indicates the essence without the lam, so carrying the lam on a new benefit is more appropriate than carrying it on definition of the nature. And the new benefit is either definition of covenant or generality of the genus, and definition of covenant is more appropriate than generality, because when some individuals of the genus are mentioned externally or mentally, carrying the lam on that mentioned part is more appropriate than carrying it on all individuals, because the part is certain and the whole is possible. So when that is known, in the plural adorned with alif and lam, it is not possible to carry it via reality on definition of the essence, because the plural is placed for individuals of the essence, not for the essence as such, but it is carried on it via metaphor, as will come on this page. And it is not possible to carry it on covenant when there is no covenant. So his statement 'and not a part of the individuals due to lack of priority' is a reference to this, so generality (istighraq) is determined. And because they adhered to his saying (peace be upon him): 'The leaders are from Quraysh' — when after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) disagreement occurred concerning the caliphate, and the Ansar said, 'From us an amir, and from you an amir,' Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) adhered to this hadith.
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage defines a type of general word (عام): the plural with the definite article (ال) when it is not used for a specific known group (عهد). The author argues that the definite article on a plural cannot indicate the essence (ماهية) as a singular could, nor a specific subset without priority, so it must indicate generality (استغراق) of all individuals. The reasoning follows the hanafi usul hierarchy: the default function of ال is covenant (عهد), then generality, then definition of nature. The proof is the famous hadith 'الأئمة من قريش' (The leaders are from Quraysh) which Abu Bakr used to argue that leadership is restricted to Quraysh, showing that the plural with ال indicates generality (all leaders are from Quraysh).

Key Terms
الجمع المعرف باللام (al-jam' al-mu'arraf bi al-lam): A plural noun with the definite article, which indicates generality when no covenant is present.
العهد (al-'ahd): A known specific group or individual previously mentioned or mentally present.
استغراق الجنس (istighraq al-jins): The definite article indicating all individuals of the genus (generality).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Generality (istighraq)
C) Covenant
D) Indeterminate

Key Takeaway
A plural noun with the definite article, without covenant, is general (عام) and indicates all individuals of the genus.

The Plural with Definite Article as a General Term: Definition and Proof
Definition of plural with definite article as a general term with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a plural with definite article as general or specific based on the presence of 'ahd, and apply the Hanafi hierarchy of lam meanings to derive rulings from scriptural texts.

Core Idea
A plural with alif-lam indicates all individuals unless a prior reference (ahd) restricts it.

In Hanafi usul, understanding when a term is general (amm) is crucial for interpreting the Quran and Sunnah. One key indicator is the plural noun made definite by the definite article alif-lam. But not every such plural is automatically general — its generality depends on the absence of prior reference (ahd). This lesson unpacks the types of lam, their hierarchy, and the proof from the hadith 'al-a'immatau min quraysh' that establishes the default generality of such plurals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the plural with lam
Locate a plural noun prefixed with alif-lam in a text. This is the form under analysis.
Example: 'al-muslimuna' (the Muslims) in an ayah or hadith.
2
Check for prior reference (ahd)
Determine if this plural has been mentioned earlier in the discourse (external or mental). If yes, the lam is for 'ahd and the term is specific to that group.
If 'ahd exists, the plural is not general.
3
Apply the hierarchy of lam
If no 'ahd, see if the lam can be for istighraq (all individuals). The Hanafi order: 'ahd > istighraq > tabi'ah. Since plural is for individuals, it cannot be for tabi'ah; thus istighraq is the default.
This is a rational argument: the essence (tabi'ah) is not indicated by the plural form.
4
Confirm with textual evidence
The hadith 'al-a'immatau min quraysh' was used by Abu Bakr to argue that all leaders must be from Quraysh, and no Companion objected. This shows that the plural with lam without 'ahd is general. Also, the validity of exception (istithna') from such plurals proves generality.
Exception only works from general statements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا (أَى مِنْ أَلْفَاظِ الْعَام) الْجَمْعُ الْمُعَرَّفَ بِاللَّامِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ مَعْهُودًا لَّاَنَّ المُعَرَّفَ لَيْسَ هُوَ الْمَاهِيَّةَ فِى الْجَمْعِ، وَلَا بَعْضَ الْأَفْرَادِ لِعَدَمِ الْأَوْلَوِيَّةِ فَتَعَيَّنَ الْكُلُّ. اعْلَمْ أَنَّ لَامَ التَّعْرِيفِ إِمَّا لِلْعَهْدِ الْخَارِجِيِّ أَوِ الذَّهَنِيِّ، وَإِمَّا لِاسْتِغْرَاقِ الْجِنْسِ، وَإِمَّا لِتَعْرِيفِ الطَّبِيعَةِ لَكِنَّ الْعَهْدَ هُوَ الْأَصْلُ ثُمَّ الِاسْتِغْرَاقُ ثُمَّ تَعْرِيفُ الطَّبِيعَةِ لِأَنَّ اللفظَ الَّذِي يَدْخُلُ عَلَيْهِ اللَّامُ دَالٌّ عَلَى الْمَاهِيَّةِ بِدُونِ اللَّامِ، فَحَمْلُ اللَّامِ عَلَى الْفَائِدَةِ الْجَدِيدَةِ أَوْلَى مِنْ حَمْلِهِ عَلَى تَعْرِيفِ الطَّبِيعَةِ، وَالْفَائِدَةُ الْجَدِيدَةُ أَمَّا تَعْرِيفُ الْعَهْدِ أَوِ اسْتِغْرَاقُ الْجِنْسِ، وَتَعْرِيفُ الْعَهْدِ أَوْلَى مِنَ الِاسْتِغْرَاقِ لِأَنَّهُ إِذَا ذُكِرَ بَعْضُ أَفْرَادِ الْجِنْسِ خَارِجًا أَوْ ذِهَنًا فَحَمْلُ اللَّامِ عَلَى ذَلِكَ الْبَعْضِ الْمَذْكُورِ أَوْلَى مِنْ حَمْلِهِ عَلَى جَمِيعِ الْأَفْرَادِ لِأَنَّ الْبَعْضَ مُتَيَقَّنٌ، وَالْكُلَّ مُحْتَمَلٌ. فَإِذَا عُلِمَ ذَلِكَ فَفِي الْجَمْعِ الْمُحَلَّى بِالْأَلِفِ وَاللَّامِ لَا يُمْكِنُ حَمْلُهُ بِطَرِيقِ الْحَقِيقَةِ عَلَى تَعْرِيفِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ لِأَنَّ الْجَمْعَ وُضِعَ لِأَفْرَادِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ لَا لِلْمَاهِيَّةِ مِنْ حَيْثُ هِيَ، لِكُلِّ يُحْمَلُ عَلَيْهَا بِطَرِيقِ الْمَجَازِ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي فِي هَذِهِ الصَّفْحَةِ، وَلَا يُمْكِنُ حَمْلُهُ عَلَى الْعَهْدِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ عَهْدٌ. فَقَوْلُهُ "وَلَا بَعْضَ الْأَفْرَادِ لِعَدَمِ الْأَوْلَوِيَّةِ" إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى هَذَا فَتَعَيَّنَ الِاسْتِغْرَاقُ. وَلِتَمَسُّكِهِمْ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: (الْأَئِمَّةُ مِنْ قُرَيْشٍ) لَمَّا وَقَعَ الِاخْتِلَافُ بَعْدَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي الْخِلَافَةِ، وَقَالَ الْأَنْصَارُ: مِنَّا أَمِيرٌ وَمِنْكُمْ أَمِيرٌ، تَمَسَّكَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: (الْأَئِمَّةُ مِنْ قُرَيْشٍ) وَلَمْ يُنْكِرْهُ أَحَدٌ. وَلِصِحَّةِ الِاسْتِثْنَاءِ. ترجمہ:۔ (اور ان میں سے) یعنی عام کے الفاظ میں سے (جمع معرف باللام ہے جبکہ نہ ہو وہ الف لام معہود کا۔ کیونکہ معترف نہیں ہے وہ ماہیت جمع میں اور نہ ہی بعض افراد اولویت کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے پس متعین ہو گئے کل افراد) تو جان لے کہ بیشک لام تعریف یا تو ہوگا عہد خارجی کا یا ذہنی کا اور یا جنس کے استغراق کے لیے یا پھر طبعیت کی تعریف کے لیے کیونکہ وہ لفظ کہ داخل ہوتا ہے اس پر لام وہ دلالت کرنے والا ہوتا ہے ماہیت پر بغیر لام کے پس لام کو محمول کرنا فائدہ جدیدہ پر اولیٰ ہے اس کو محمول کرنے سے تعریف طبعیت پر اور فائدہ جدیدہ یا تو عہد کی تعریف ہے یا جنس کا استغراق ہے اور تعریف عہد اولیٰ ہے استغراق سے۔ کیونکہ جب ذکر کیا جائے جنس کے بعض افراد کو خارجی ہوں یا ذہنی ہوں پس لام کو محمول کرنا ان بعض مذکور پر اولیٰ ہوتا ہے اس کو محمول کرنے سے تمام افراد پر کیونکہ بعض افراد متیقن ہیں اور تمام افراد محتمل ہیں پس جب معلوم ہو گئی یہ بات تو جمع معرف باللام نہیں ہے ممکن اس کو محمول کرنا حقیقت کے طریقہ پر تعریف ماہیت پر کیونکہ جمع کو وضع کیا گیا ہے افراد ماہیت کے لیے نہ کہ ماہیت کے لیے اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ ماہیت ہے لیکن محمول کیا جاتا ہے اس ماہیت پر مجاز کے طریق سے جیسا کہ آ رہا ہے اسی محلہ میں اور نہیں ہے ممکن اس کو محمول کرنا عہد پر جبکہ نہ ہو وہ عہد کا پس اس کا قول ولا بعض الافراد لعدم الاولویۃ یہ اشارہ ہے اسی کی طرف پس متعین ہو گیا استغراق۔ (اور وجہ استدلال پکڑنے ان کے آقا کے فرمان الائمۃ من قریش سے) جب واقع ہوا اختلاف رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے بعد خلافت میں اور کہا انصار نے کہ ہم میں سے ایک امیر ہوگا اور تم میں سے ایک امیر ہوگا تو استدلال پکڑا حضرت ابو بکر صدیق نے آقا کے فرمان الائمۃ من قریش سے اور انکار نہیں کیا اس کا کسی ایک نے (اور بوجہ صحیح ہونے استثناء کے) تشریح:- ومنها إلى من الفاظ العام:۔ عام کے الفاظ میں سے ایک جمع ہے لیکن وہ جمع جو معرف باللام ہو۔ اور یہ جمع معرف باللام اس وقت عام بنتا ہے جس وقت وہ پہلے سے معہود نہ یعنی پہلے اس کا تذکرہ نہ ہو چکا ہو۔ اس کی تفصیل پہلے بطور تمہید ایک مقدمہ سمجھیں۔ الف لام میں اول درجہ عہد کا ہے پھر استغراق کا پھر جنس کا مقدمہ:۔ الف لام کی چار قسمیں ہیں۔ جنسی، استغراقی، عہد خارجی، عہد ذہنی۔ اگر الف لام کے مدلول سے مراد اس کی
And among them (i.e., among the terms of the general) is the plural defined by alif-lam when it is not previously known (ma'hud). Because the defined (al-mu'arrif) is neither the essence (mahiyyah) in the plural nor a part of the individuals due to lack of priority, so the whole is determined. Know that the lam of definition is either for external or mental reference ('ahd), or for comprehensive generality of the genus (istighraq al-jins), or for defining the essential nature (ta'rif al-tabi'ah). However, reference ('ahd) is the primary, then comprehensiveness, then definition of nature. Because the word upon which the lam enters indicates the essence without the lam, so carrying the lam upon a new benefit is more appropriate than carrying it upon definition of nature. And the new benefit is either definition of reference or comprehensiveness of the genus, and definition of reference is more appropriate than comprehensiveness because when some individuals of the genus are mentioned externally or mentally, then carrying the lam upon those mentioned individuals is more appropriate than carrying it upon all individuals, because the part is certain and the whole is probable. When this is understood, then in the plural adorned with alif and lam, it is not possible to carry it in the way of reality upon definition of essence, because the plural is placed for individuals of the essence, not for the essence as such; it is carried upon it in the way of metaphor as will come later on this page. And it is not possible to carry it upon reference when there is no reference. So his statement 'and not a part of the individuals due to lack of priority' is an indication of this, so comprehensiveness is determined. And due to their adherence to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The leaders are from Quraysh' when dispute occurred after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) regarding the caliphate, and the Ansar said: 'An amir from us and an amir from you.' Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) adhered to his statement 'the leaders are from Quraysh', and no one denied it. And due to the validity of exception (istithna). Translation: (And among them) i.e., among the terms of the general (is the plural defined by alif-lam when it is not previously known. Because the defined is neither the essence in the plural nor some individuals due to lack of priority, so the whole becomes determined.) Know that the lam of definition is either for external or mental reference, or for comprehensive generality of the genus, or for definition of the essential nature. But reference is the original, then comprehensiveness, then definition of nature. Because the word upon which the lam enters indicates the essence without the lam, so carrying the lam upon a new benefit is more appropriate than carrying it upon definition of nature. And the new benefit is either definition of reference or comprehensiveness of the genus. And definition of reference is more appropriate than comprehensiveness, because when some individuals of the genus are mentioned externally or mentally, then carrying the lam upon those mentioned individuals is more appropriate than carrying it upon all individuals, because the part is certain and the whole is probable. So when this is known, then in the plural adorned with alif-lam, it is not possible to carry it in the way of reality upon definition of essence, because the plural is placed for individuals of the essence, not for the essence as such. But it is carried upon it metaphorically, as will come on this page. And it is not possible to carry it upon reference when there is no reference. So his statement 'and not some individuals due to lack of priority' is an indication of this, so comprehensiveness is determined. (And the reason for their adherence to the saying of their master (peace be upon him) 'the leaders are from Quraysh') When dispute occurred after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) regarding the caliphate, and the Ansar said: 'An amir from us and an amir from you', Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) adhered to the saying of the master 'the leaders are from Quraysh', and no one denied it. (And due to the validity of exception.) Commentary: 'And among them' to 'from the terms of the general': one of them is the plural that is defined by alif-lam. And this plural defined by alif-lam becomes general when it is not previously referred to, i.e., its mention has not occurred before. Its detail: first understand a preface. The alif-lam: the first degree is for reference, then comprehensiveness, then genus. Preface: The alif-lam has four types: generic, comprehensive, external reference, mental reference. If by the intended meaning of alif-lam...
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage defines one of the terms that indicate generality (umum) in Hanafi usul: the plural noun made definite by the definite article alif-lam, provided it is not already known from prior context (ma'hud). The author explains that when such a plural is used without prior reference, it necessarily indicates all individuals of the category, because it cannot be referring to the essence as such (since the plural is for individuals) nor to a part (since there is no priority for any part). The discussion then delves into the types of lam (the definite article): it can be for external or mental reference ('ahd), for comprehensive generality (istighraq al-jins), or for defining the essential nature (ta'rif al-tabi'ah). The author prioritizes reference over comprehensiveness over nature, because reference is certain when the referent is known, and carrying the lam to a known referent is more appropriate than assuming generality. In the absence of any known referent, the lam defaults to comprehensiveness, making the plural general. The author supports this with the well-known hadith 'al-a'immatau min quraysh' (leaders are from Quraysh), which Abu Bakr used as evidence for the caliphate being from Quraysh, and no Companion objected. This hadith demonstrates that the plural 'al-a'immah' (the leaders) with the definite article, without prior reference, indicates all leaders (i.e., every leader must be from Quraysh). Another proof mentioned is the validity of exception (istithna'), which is a sign of generality because exception only applies to general statements. The accompanying Urdu commentary rephrases this in simpler terms for students.

Key Terms
الجمع المعرّف باللام (al-jam‘ al-mu‘arrif bi al-lām): The plural noun that is made definite by the definite article alif-lam; one of the lafaz al-amm.
تعريف العهد (ta‘rīf al-‘ahd): The use of the definite article to refer to a specific known entity, either external or mental.
استغراق الجنس (istighrāq al-jins): The definite article indicating all individuals of the genus, i.e., comprehensive generality.
تعريف الطبيعة (ta‘rīf al-ṭabī‘ah): The definite article indicating the essence or nature of something, not its individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the default ruling for a plural noun with the definite article alif-lam when there is no prior known referent ('ahd)?
A) It refers to the essential nature (tabi'ah).
B) It refers to a specific part of the individuals (ba'd).
C) It indicates comprehensive generality (istighraq) covering all individuals.
D) It is ambiguous and requires further context to determine.

Key Takeaway
The plural with alif-lam defaults to generality (istighraq) unless a prior reference (ahd) restricts it, as proven by the hadith and the validity of exception.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Generality of the Definite Plural (al-Jam' al-Mu'arrif bi al-Lam)
Explaining that al-jam' al-mu'arrif bi al-lam is 'amm when not for 'ahd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the four types of alif lam, apply the Hanafi priority order of interpretation, and derive that the definite plural indicates generality when not preceded by prior reference.

Core Idea
The definite plural defaults to generality because without prior reference, it cannot indicate a specific group or essence.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text explains a core principle: how to interpret the definite article 'al-' when it enters a plural noun. The author classifies alif lam into four types and establishes a priority order: first check for prior reference ('ahd), then universality (istighraq), and finally the generic sense (jins). Applying this to the definite plural, if there is no prior reference, the only valid interpretation is generality, making it a general term ('amm). This rule is demonstrated with the famous hadith 'The leaders are from Quraysh,' which Abu Bakr used as evidence that all leaders must be from Quraysh, and the Companions accepted this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of alif lam
List the four types: jinsiyyah (generic), istighraqiyyah (universal), 'ahd khariji (external prior reference), 'ahd dhihni (mental prior reference). Understand each definition.
This is the foundational classification in Hanafi usul.
2
Apply the principle of new benefit
Recognize that alif lam should add new meaning; if it only indicates the essence (already indicated by the word without alif lam), it is not preferred. Therefore, we first interpret it as prior reference or universality before the generic sense.
This is why 'jins' is the last resort.
3
Determine the priority order
Among the meanings, prior reference ('ahd) is given precedence over universality (istighraq), and universality over the generic sense (jins). This is because 'ahd is certain, istighraq is probable, and jins is metaphorical for the plural.
For the definite plural, the default is istighraq if no 'ahd exists.
4
Apply to the definite plural and the hadith example
The phrase 'al-aimmah (the leaders)' in the hadith 'al-aimmah min Quraysh' is a definite plural. Since there was no prior reference to a specific group, it must be interpreted as universal: all leaders. Abu Bakr used this to argue that leadership must be from Quraysh, and the Companions accepted it, confirming the generality of the definite plural.
This shows practical application of the usul rule.

طریق کیسا تھ جیسا کہ آرہا ہے اسی محلہ میں اور نہیں ہے ممکن اس کو معمول کرنا عہد پر جبکہ نہ ہو وہ عہد کا پس اس کا قول ولا بعض الافراد لعدم الا ولو یہ اشارہ ہے اسی کی طرف پس متعین ہو گیا استغراق ( اور یوجہ استدلال پکڑنے ان کے آقا کے فرمان الایمۃ من قریش امام قریش میں سے ہوں گئے سے) جب واقع ہوا اختلاف رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے بعد خلافت میں اور کہا انصار نے کہ ہم میں سے ایک امیر ہوگا اور تم میں سے ایک امیر ہوگا تو استدلال پکڑ ا حضرت ابو بکر صدیق نے آٹا کے فرمان الائمۃ من قریش سے اور انکار نہیں کیا اس کا کسی ایک نے (اور بوجہ صحیح ہونے استثناء کے ) تشریح:- ومنها الى من الفاظ العام:۔ عام کے الفاظ میں سے ایک جمع ہے لیکن وہ جمع جو معرف باسلام ہو۔ اور یہ جمع معرف بالسلام اس وقت عام بنتا ہے جس وقت وہ پہلے سے معہود نہ یعنی پہلے اس کا تذکرہ نہ ہو چکا ہو۔ اس کی تفصیل پہلے بطور تمہید ایک مقدمہ سمجھیں۔ الف لام میں اول درجہ عہد کا ہے پھر استغراق کا پھر جنس کا مقدمہ:۔ الف لام کی چار قسمیں ہیں۔ جنسی ، استغفراتی ، عہدہ خارجی ، عہد ڈالی۔ اگر الف لام کے مدلول سے مراد اس کی ماہیت ہو افراد مراد نہ ہوں تو وہ جنسی اور طبعی ہے اور اگر افراد مراد ہوں تو پھر دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ تمام افراد مراد ہوں گے یا بعض افراد اگر تمام افراد مراد ہوں تو یہ استغراقی ہے اور اگر بعض افراد مراد ہوں تو وہ خارج میں متعین ہونگے یا نہیں ۔ اگر خارج میں متعین ہوں تو یہ عہد خارجی ہے اور اگر خارج میں متعین نہ ہوں تو عہد دینی ہے۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ ان تمام میں سب سے پہلا درجہ عہد کا ہے پھر استغراق کا ہے اور آخر میں جنس کا ہے۔ جنس کا درجہ سب سے آخر میں اس لیے ہے کہ کوئی بھی لفظ ہو الف لام کے بغیر بھی اپنی ماہیت پر دلالت کرتا ہے تو اگر الف لام کے داخل ہونے کے بعد بھی وہ ماہیت پر دلالت کرے تو کوئی نیا فائدہ حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔ حالانکہ لفظ کو فائدہ جدیدہ پر محمول کرنا بہتر ہوتا ہے۔ اور فائدہ جدیدہ ماہیت مراد لینے کی صورت میں نہیں ہوتا بلکہ عہد یا استغراق کی صورت میں ہوتا ہے۔ اس لے اولاً ہم الف لام کو عہد اور استغراق پر محمول کریں گے اگر نہ ہو سکے تو جنس پر محمول کر لیں گے۔ اور پھر عہد اور استغراق میں سے عہد پر محمول کرنا مقدم اس لیے ہے کہ جب مدخول کے جن افراد کا ذکر پہلے بھی ہو چکا ہو تو ان بعض کو مرا لینا یقینی ہوگا اور تمام افراد کومرا لیتا محمل ہوگا۔ اور حمل کی بجائے یقینی کو مراد لینا بہتر ہوتا ہے اس لیے عہد مقدم ہوگا۔ جمع معرف بالسلام کے عموم پر دلائل جمع معرف بالسلام کے عموم پر دلیل اول:۔ جب جمع معرف السلام کا مدلول پہلے معہود نہیں ہو گا اس وقت اس کو ہم نہ تو عہد پر محمول کر سکتے ہیں اور نہ ہی جنس پر۔ عہد پر اس لیے محمول نہیں کر سکتے کہ وہ پہلے معہود نہیں ہے۔ اوا گر جنس پر محمول کریں تو یہ حقیقت نہیں ہوگا بلکہ مجاز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جمع کو ماہیت کیلئے وضع نہیں کیا گیا۔ اس کے افراد کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے۔ تو ماہیت معنی موضوع لہ نہ ہوا اور نہ حقیقی ہوا تو الف لام کو اس پر محمول کرنا حقیقتا نہ ہوا اس لیے جنس پر بھی محمول نہیں کریں گے ۔ لھذا اس کو استغراق پر ہی محمول کریں گے اور اس وقت اس میں معموم آجائے گا اس لیے ہم نے کہا عام کے الفاظ میں ایک جمع معرف بالسلام ہے۔ جمع معرف باسلام کے عام ہونے کی دو دلیلیں اور بھی ہیں۔ وليل ثانى والتمسكهم بقوله عليه السلام الائمة من قريش - دوسری دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے جب آپ کا وصال ہوا تو انصار و مہاجرین کے درمیان خلافت کے بارے میں مشورہ ہوا تو انصار نے کہا منا امیر ومنکم امیر کہ ایک ہمارا امیر ہوگا اور ایک تمہارا امیر ہوگا لیکن اس کے جواب میں حضرت ابو بکر صدیق نے فرمایا کہ نبی پاک کا فرمان ہے الائمہ من قریش اس حدیث مبارک کو آپ نے اس بات پر دلیل بنایا کہ امیر صرف قریش سے ہی ہوگا اور یہ دلیل تب بن سکتی ہے جب الائمہ
The exposition for the solution of al-Tawdih and al-Talwih: About his statement, peace be upon him, 'The leaders are from Quraysh,' and no one denied it. And for the validity of the exception. Translation: And among them—that is, from the words of the general—the definite plural is when it is not the alif lam of prior reference. Because it does not recognize the essence of the plural, nor some individuals due to lack of preference, so all individuals are determined. Know that the lam of definition is either for external prior reference, or mental prior reference, or for the universality of the genus, or for the definition of the nature. Because the word upon which the lam enters, it indicates the essence without the lam. So carrying the lam upon a new benefit is preferable. Carrying it upon the definition of the nature gives no new benefit, and the new benefit is either the definition of prior reference or the universality of the genus. And the definition of prior reference is preferable over universality. Because when some individuals of the genus are mentioned, whether external or mental, then carrying the lam upon those mentioned is more specific than carrying it upon all individuals, because some individuals are certain and all individuals are probable. So when this is known, the definite plural is not possible to be carried upon the essence in a real way because the plural is placed for individuals of the essence, not for the essence as such. But it is carried upon the essence metaphorically, as will come in this same place. And it is not possible to carry it upon prior reference when there is no prior reference. So his statement 'nor some individuals due to lack of preference' indicates this. So universality is determined. And the cause of their taking evidence from his statement, peace be upon him, 'The leaders are from Quraysh' is that when disagreement occurred after the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, regarding the caliphate, and the Ansar said, 'An emir from us and an emir from you,' Abu Bakr al-Siddiq took evidence from his statement, peace be upon him, 'The leaders are from Quraysh,' and no one denied it. And due to the validity of the exception. Commentary: Among the words of the general is the plural that is definite with alif lam. And this definite plural becomes general when it is not previously specified, i.e., it has not been mentioned before. Its detail: first, understand a premise. The first rank in alif lam is prior reference, then universality, then the genus. Premise: Alif lam has four types: jinsiyyah (generic), istighraqiyyah (universal), 'ahd khariji (external prior reference), 'ahd dhihni (mental prior reference). If by the meaning of alif lam, its essence is intended and not individuals, it is jinsiyyah and tab'iyyah. If individuals are intended, then there are two possibilities: either all individuals are intended or some. If all individuals are intended, it is istighraqiyyah. If some individuals are intended, they are either externally determined or not. If externally determined, it is 'ahd khariji; if not, it is 'ahd dhihni. The second point is that among all these, the first rank is prior reference, then universality, and lastly the genus. The genus is last because any word without alif lam still indicates its essence, so if after the entry of alif lam it still indicates the essence, no new benefit is gained. However, carrying the word upon a new benefit is better. And the new benefit does not occur when the essence is intended, but rather when prior reference or universality is intended. Therefore, we first carry alif lam upon prior reference and universality; if not possible, we carry it upon the genus. And among prior reference and universality, carrying it upon prior reference is given precedence because when some individuals of the noun have been mentioned before, taking those specific ones is certain, while taking all individuals is probable. And taking the certain over the probable is better, so prior reference is given precedence. Evidence for the generality of the definite plural: First evidence: When the meaning of the definite plural is not previously specified, we cannot carry it upon prior reference (because there is no prior reference) nor upon the genus (because that would be metaphorical, since the plural is not placed for the essence but for individuals). So it must be carried upon universality, and thus it becomes general. Therefore, we said one of the words of the general is the definite plural. There are also two other pieces of evidence for the generality of the definite plural. Second evidence: Their taking evidence from his statement, peace be upon him, 'The leaders are from Quraysh.' The summary: When he passed away, the Ansar and Muhajirun consulted about the caliphate, and the Ansar said, 'An emir from us and an emir from you.' In response, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq said that the Prophet's statement is 'The leaders are from Quraysh.' He used this hadith as evidence that the emir must be from Quraysh alone. And this evidence is only valid if 'al-aimmah' (the leaders) is general.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul explanation of the types of alif lam and the status of the definite plural as a general term. The author begins by discussing the famous hadith 'al-aimmah min Quraysh' and how Abu Bakr used it as evidence that all leaders must be from Quraysh, which was accepted by the Companions. This serves as a proof that the definite plural (al-jam' al-mu'arrif bi al-lam) indicates generality ('umum) when it is not restricted by prior reference ('ahd). The author then provides a detailed classification of alif lam: it can be for the generic sense (jinsiyyah), universal inclusion (istighraqiyyah), external prior reference ('ahd khariji), or mental prior reference ('ahd dhihni). The principle is that alif lam should be interpreted to give a new benefit; thus, priority is given to prior reference over universality, and universality over the generic sense, because a word without alif lam already indicates its essence. For the definite plural, if there is no prior reference, it cannot be interpreted as generic (since that would be metaphorical), so it defaults to universality, making it a general term. This is a standard Hanafi position: the definite plural is 'amm unless specified otherwise. The example of the hadith demonstrates that the Companions understood 'al-aimmah' in its general sense, covering all leaders, which is why Abu Bakr's argument held force.

Key Terms
اللام التعریف (al-lām al-ta'rīf): The definite article 'al-' that enters nouns to make them definite. It has four types: jinsiyyah, istighraqiyyah, 'ahd khariji, 'ahd dhihni.
عہد خارجی ('ahd khārijī): External prior reference: when some specific individuals of the noun are known from outside the text.
عہد ذہنی ('ahd dhihnī): Mental prior reference: when the specific individuals are not externally known but are present in the mind due to context.
استغراق (istighrāq): Universality: when alif lam indicates all individuals of the noun.
جنس (jins): The genus or essence: when alif lam indicates the essential nature rather than individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default meaning of al-jam' al-mu'arrif bi al-lam (the definite plural) when it is not preceded by prior reference ('ahd)?
A) It indicates a specific group.
B) It indicates the entire genus (jins).
C) It indicates universality (istighraq).
D) It is ambiguous and context-dependent.

Key Takeaway
The definite plural (al-jam' al-mu'arrif bi al-lam) is a general term ('amm) unless it is restricted by prior reference ('ahd).
