Types of the Definite Article and Their Priority
Classification of lām al-ta'rīf types and their priority order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the meanings of the definite article (al-) according to Hanafi usul and apply the priority rule to interpret Quranic or hadith texts.

Core Idea
The definite article is interpreted first as 'ahd, then istighrāq, finally jins, prioritizing certain over speculative meanings.

The definite article (al-) in Arabic can carry different meanings depending on context. Hanafi usul scholars have carefully classified these meanings and established a priority order for interpretation. This lesson unpacks that classification, from the most specific ('ahd) to the most general (jins), and explains the reasoning behind the hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary split
First, determine whether the definite article refers to the essence (jins) or to individuals. If individuals are not intended, it is jins/tabi'i. If individuals are intended, proceed to the next step.
Jins is the default only if no other meaning fits.
2
Distinguish istighrāq from 'ahd
If individuals are intended, decide whether all individuals (istighrāq) or some individuals ('ahd) are meant. 'Ahd requires the individuals to be known (external or mental).
Istighrāq means all members of the genus; 'ahd means a specific set.
3
Subdivide 'ahd
If 'ahd applies, subdivide into 'ahd khārijī (externally determined, e.g., previously mentioned in speech or physically present) and 'ahd dhihnī (mentally known, e.g., a well-known entity).
Both are under 'ahd; the priority rule treats them together.
4
Understand the priority order
The Hanafi rule: first interpret as 'ahd if plausible; if not, try istighrāq; only if neither works, fall back to jins. The reasoning is that 'ahd gives a certain reference (previous mention), istighrāq gives a new benefit (comprehensiveness), while jins adds no new benefit beyond the noun's basic meaning.
Certainty (yaqīn) is preferred over speculation (dhann).
5
Apply to a text
Practice by taking a Quranic or hadith phrase with the definite article, run it through the hierarchy, and state which interpretation the Hanafi school would adopt.
The context (siyāq) is crucial for determining possibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ماہیت ہو افراد مراد نہ ہوں تو وہ جنسی اور طبعی ہے اور اگر افراد مراد ہوں تو پھر دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ تمام افراد مراد ہوں گے یا بعض افراد اگر تمام افراد مراد ہوں تو یہ استغراقی ہے اور اگر بعض افراد مراد ہوں تو وہ خارج میں متعین ہونگے یا نہیں ۔ اگر خارج میں متعین ہوں تو یہ عہد خارجی ہے اور اگر خارج میں متعین نہ ہوں تو عہد دینی ہے۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ ان تمام میں سب سے پہلا درجہ عہد کا ہے پھر استغراق کا ہے اور آخر میں جنس کا ہے۔ جنس کا درجہ سب سے آخر میں اس لیے ہے کہ کوئی بھی لفظ ہو الف لام کے بغیر بھی اپنی ماہیت پر دلالت کرتا ہے تو اگر الف لام کے داخل ہونے کے بعد بھی وہ ماہیت پر دلالت کرے تو کوئی نیا فائدہ حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔ حالانکہ لفظ کو فائدہ جدیدہ پر محمول کرنا بہتر ہوتا ہے۔ اور فائدہ جدیدہ ماہیت مراد لینے کی صورت میں نہیں ہوتا بلکہ عہد یا استغراق کی صورت میں ہوتا ہے۔ اس لے اولاً ہم الف لام کو عہد اور استغراق پر محمول کریں گے اگر نہ ہو سکے تو جنس پر محمول کر لیں گے۔ اور پھر عہد اور استغراق میں سے عہد پر محمول کرنا مقدم اس لیے ہے کہ جب مدخول کے جن افراد کا ذکر پہلے بھی ہو چکا ہو تو ان بعض کو مرا لینا یقینی ہوگا اور تمام افراد کومرا لیتا محمل ہوگا۔ اور حمل کی بجائے یقینی کو مراد لینا بہتر ہوتا ہے اس لیے عہد مقدم ہوگا۔
If the essence (māhiyya) is intended and individuals are not intended, then it is of the genus (jins) and natural (tabi'i). If individuals are intended, then it does not fall short of two states: either all individuals are intended or some individuals. If all individuals are intended, then it is istighrāq (comprehensiveness). If some individuals are intended, then they are externally determined or not. If externally determined, it is 'ahd khārijī (external covenant), and if not, it is 'ahd dhihnī (mental covenant). The second matter is that among all these, the first rank belongs to 'ahd, then istighrāq, and lastly jins. The rank of jins is last because any word without the definite article (alif lām) also indicates its essence. So if after the entry of the definite article it still indicates the essence, no new benefit is gained. Whereas it is better to carry the word upon a new benefit. And the new benefit is not present in the case of intending the essence but rather in the case of 'ahd or istighrāq. Therefore, we first carry the definite article upon 'ahd and istighrāq; if not possible, then we carry it upon jins. Then, between 'ahd and istighrāq, carrying upon 'ahd is prioritized because when the individuals of the word have been mentioned before, intending some of them is certain, while intending all individuals is speculative. And it is better to take what is certain rather than speculative; therefore 'ahd is prioritized.
Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the types of the definite article (lām al-ta'rīf) in the Hanafi usul tradition. The author explains that when the definite article is attached to a noun, it can convey different meanings: the genus (jins) of the thing, comprehension (istighrāq) of all individuals, or reference to a specific previously-mentioned individual ('ahd). 'Ahd is further divided into external ('ahd khārijī, referring to something physically present or previously mentioned) and mental ('ahd dhihnī, something known in the mind but not mentioned). The priority rule is that if the context allows, one should interpret the definite article as 'ahd first, because it gives a specific, certain reference. If that is not possible (no previous mention), then consider istighrāq (all individuals). Only if neither 'ahd nor istighrāq fits, one falls back to jins (the genus meaning). The reasoning is that every noun already indicates its essence without the definite article, so using the definite article for jins adds no new benefit; whereas 'ahd and istighrāq provide additional information. This hierarchy is a key principle in determining the meaning of definite nouns in the Quran and Hadith.

Key Terms
عہد ('ahd): Reference to a specific, known individual or group of individuals, either externally present or mentally known.
استغراق (istighrāq): Comprehensiveness, meaning all individuals of the genus are intended.
جنس (jins): The essence or genus of a thing, without reference to specific individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification, what is the first interpretation of the definite article (al-) when attached to a noun?
A) Istighrāq (all individuals)
B) Jins (genus)
C) 'Ahd (specific reference)
D) Tabi'ī (natural)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the definite article is interpreted in the order: 'ahd, istighrāq, jins, based on the principle of preferring the most certain meaning.

Three Proofs That the Definite Plural Indicates Generality
The author presents three proofs that the definite plural is general, then explains when it becomes metaphorical for the genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three proofs used by Hanafi usulis to establish that al-jam' al-mu'raf bi al-lām is 'āmm, and identify when it may be interpreted metaphorically as the genus.

Core Idea
The definite plural is general unless context makes literal generality impossible—then it becomes metaphorical for the genus.

The Hanafi school has a distinctive position on the definite plural. While it is fundamentally a word of generality ('āmm), the mashāyikh clarified that it can be used metaphorically for the genus when the literal meaning of 'all individuals' is impossible or impractical. This lesson walks through three proofs that establish its generality, and then examines the exception.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first proof: the absence of 'ahd and jins
When the definite plural is not previously specified and cannot be carried on the genus (because that would be metaphorical), it must indicate istighrāq (all individuals), yielding generality.
2
Analyze the second proof: the hadith 'al-a'immatu min quraysh'
The companions' unanimous acceptance of Abu Bakr's citation shows that 'al-a'immatu' was understood as including all leaders, proving generality.
3
Examine the third proof: validity of exception (istithnā')
The ability to say 'the people came except Zayd' proves 'al-qawmu' is general, because you cannot except from a specific referent.
4
Recognize the Hanafi qualification: metaphorical use for the genus
When istighrāq is impossible (e.g., swearing to marry all women, or distributing zakah to all poor), the definite plural is interpreted metaphorically as the genus, preserving the lam's function.

جمع معرف بالسلام کے عموم پر دلائل جمع معرف بالسلام کے عموم پر دلیل اول:۔ جب جمع معرف السلام کا مدلول پہلے معہود نہیں ہو گا اس وقت اس کو ہم نہ تو عہد پر محمول کر سکتے ہیں اور نہ ہی جنس پر۔ عہد پر اس لیے محمول نہیں کر سکتے کہ وہ پہلے معہود نہیں ہے۔ اوا گر جنس پر محمول کریں تو یہ حقیقت نہیں ہوگا بلکہ مجاز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جمع کو ماہیت کیلئے وضع نہیں کیا گیا۔ اس کے افراد کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے۔ تو ماہیت معنی موضوع لہ نہ ہوا اور نہ حقیقی ہوا تو الف لام کو اس پر محمول کرنا حقیقتا نہ ہوا اس لیے جنس پر بھی محمول نہیں کریں گے ۔ لھذا اس کو استغراق پر ہی محمول کریں گے اور اس وقت اس میں معموم آجائے گا اس لیے ہم نے کہا عام کے الفاظ میں ایک جمع معرف بالسلام ہے۔ جمع معرف باسلام کے عام ہونے کی دو دلیلیں اور بھی ہیں۔ وليل ثانى والتمسكهم بقوله عليه السلام الائمة من قريش - دوسری دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے جب آپ کا وصال ہوا تو انصار و مہاجرین کے درمیان خلافت کے بارے میں مشورہ ہوا تو انصار نے کہا منا امیر ومنکم امیر کہ ایک ہمارا امیر ہوگا اور ایک تمہارا امیر ہوگا لیکن اس کے جواب میں حضرت ابو بکر صدیق نے فرمایا کہ نبی پاک کا فرمان ہے الائمہ من قریش اس حدیث مبارک کو آپ نے اس بات پر دلیل بنایا کہ امیر صرف قریش سے ہی ہوگا اور یہ دلیل تب بن سکتی ہے جب الائمہ (جو جمع معرف باسلام ہے) میں عموم ہو کہ تمام امیر اور خلفاء قریش میں سے ہی ہوں گے ۔ کیونکہ اگر اس میں عموم نہ مانا جائے تو جواب میں کہا جا سکتا تھا کہ کچھ ائمہ قریش کے ہو جائیں اور کچھ امراء ہم میں سے ہو جا ئیں تو بھی آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان پر عمل ہو جائے گا لیکن جواب میں کسی صحابی نے یہ نہیں کہا بلکہ سب نے اس بات کو مان لیا کہ تمام امراء اور خلفاء قریش سے ہی ہوں گے تو معلوم ہوا کہ جمع معرف بالسلام عام ہوتا ہے۔ دلیل ثالث: ولصحه الاستثناء تیسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمع معرف بالام سے استثناء کرنا صحیح ہے مثلا کوئی یہ کہے جاءنی القوم الا زیرا تو درست ہے اور اس استثناء کا درست ہونا ہی اس بات پر دلیل ہے کہ جمع معرف بالسلام عام ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر یہ عام نہ ہو بلکہ خاص ہو اور کسی متعین فرد پر دلالت کرے تو اس سے استثناء کرنا درست نہ ہو ۔ حالانکہ وہ درست ہے لھذا جمع معرف بالسلام عام ہے۔ قَالَ مَشَايِحُنَا هَذَا الْجَمْعُ ( أَى الْجَمْعُ الْمُحَلَّى بِاللَّامِ ) مَجَازَ عَنْ الْجِنْسِ ، وَتَبْطُلُ الْجَمْعِيَّةُ حَتَّى لَوْ حَلَفَ لَا أَتَزَوَّجُ النِّسَاء يَحُنَتْ بِالْوَاحِدَةِ ، وَيُرَادُ الْوَاحِدُ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ) إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاء ) ، وَلَوْ أَوْصَى بِشَيْءٍ لِزَيْدٍ ، وَلِلْفُقَرَاء نُصفَ بَيْنَهُ ، وَبَيْنَهُمْ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ) لَا يَحِلُّ لَكَ النِّسَاءُ مِنْ بَعْدُ ) هَذَا دَلِيلٌ عَلَى أنَّ الْجَمْعَ مَجَازٌ عَنْ الْجِنسِ . ( وَلَأنَّهُ لَمَّا لَمْ يَكُنُ هُنَاكَ مَعُهُودٌ ، وَلَيْسَ لِلاسْتِغْرَاقِ لِعَدَمِ الْفَائِدَةِ يَجِبُ حَمُلُهُ عَلَى تَعْرِيفِ الْجِنسِ ) ، وَإِنَّمَا قَالَ لِعَدَمِ الْفَائِدَةِ أَمَّا فِي قَوْلِهِ لَا أَتَزَوْجُ النِّسَاء فَلانَّ الْيَمِينَ لِلْمَنْعِ ، وَتَزَوُّجُ جَمِيعِ نِسَاء الدُّنْيَا غَيْرُ مُمْكِن فَمَنْعُهُ يَكُونُ لَغُوا ، وَفِي قَوْله تَعَالَى ) إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاء ( لا يُمْكِنُ صَرْفُ الصَّدَقَاتِ إِلَى جَمِيع فُقَرَاء الدُّنْيَا فَلا يَكُونُ الاسْتِعْرَاقَ مُوَادًا فَيَكُونُ لِتَعْرِيفِ الْجِنسِ مَجَازا فَتَكُونُ الْآيَةُ لِبَيَانِ مَصْرِفِ الزَّكَاةِ . ) فَتَبْقَى الْجَمْعِيَّةُ فِيهِ مِنْ وَجُهِ ، وَلَوْ لَمْ يُحْمَلُ عَلَى الْجِنْسِ لَبَطَلَ اللَّامُ أَصْلا) أَى إِذَا كَانَ اللَّامُ لِتَعْرِيفِ الْجِنْسِ ، وَمَعْنَى الْجَمْعِيَّةِ بَاقٍ فِى الْجِنْسِ مِنْ وَجْهِ لِأنَّ
Proofs for the generality of the definite plural. First proof: When the referent of the definite plural is not previously specified ('ahd), then we cannot carry it upon 'ahd nor upon jins. Upon 'ahd because it is not previously specified; upon jins because that would be metaphorical (majāz), not real (haqīqa), because the plural form is not placed for the essence but for its individuals. So we carry it upon istighrāq, and then generality results. Hence we said that the definite plural is among the words of generality. There are two other proofs. Second proof: They clung to his statement (peace be upon him): 'al-a'immatu min quraysh' (the leaders are from Quraysh). When the Prophet passed away, the Ansar and Muhajirun consulted about the caliphate. The Ansar said: 'From us an amir and from you an amir.' In response, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq said that the Prophet said: 'al-a'immatu min quraysh.' He used this hadith as evidence that the amir is only from Quraysh. This proof holds only if 'al-a'immatu' (the definite plural) is general, meaning all leaders and caliphs are from Quraysh. Because if it were not general, it could be responded that some imams are from Quraysh and some from us, and still the Prophet's statement would be fulfilled. But no companion said that; they all accepted that all leaders are from Quraysh. So it is known that the definite plural is general. Third proof: The validity of istithnā' (exception). For example, if someone says 'jā'anī al-qawmu illā zaydan' (the people came except Zayd), this is correct. The correctness of this exception proves that the definite plural is general. Because if it were specific and indicated a particular individual, exception from it would not be correct. Since it is correct, the definite plural is general. Our mashāyikh said: This plural (i.e., the plural adorned with lam) is metaphorical for the genus, and the plurality becomes void. Thus if someone swears 'I will not marry women' he breaks the oath with one woman. And by His statement 'innamā al-sadaqātu li al-fuqarā' (alms are for the poor) the one (singular) is intended. And if someone bequeaths something to Zayd and to the poor, it is divided between him and them because of His statement 'lā yahillu laka al-nisā'u min ba‘d' (women are not lawful for you after this). This is evidence that the plural is metaphorical for the genus. And because when there is no 'ahd and no istighrāq due to lack of benefit, it must be carried upon the definition of genus. He said 'due to lack of benefit': in his statement 'I will not marry women' the oath is for prohibition, and marrying all women of the world is impossible, so its prohibition would be futile. And in His statement 'innamā al-sadaqātu li al-fuqarā' it is impossible to distribute alms to all poor of the world, so istighrāq is not intended, so it is for definition of genus metaphorically. Thus the verse is for explaining the recipients of zakah. So the plurality remains in it from one aspect. And if it were not carried upon genus, the lam would be entirely invalid. That is, when the lam is for definition of genus, the meaning of plurality remains in the genus from one aspect.
Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi justification for why the definite plural (al-jam' al-mu'raf bi al-lām) is considered a word of generality ('āmm). The first proof is based on the interpretive hierarchy: when 'ahd (specific reference) is absent, and carrying upon jins (genus) would be metaphorical because the plural form is not originally placed for the essence, we must carry it upon istighrāq (comprehension of all individuals), producing generality. The second proof is from the incident of Saqifa after the Prophet's death. When the Ansar proposed a divided leadership, Abu Bakr cited the hadith 'al-a'immatu min quraysh'. The companions unanimously understood it to mean all leaders are from Quraysh, not just some. If the definite plural were not general, this argument would not have been convincing. The third proof is the validity of exception (istithnā') from the definite plural. For example, 'al-qawmu' (the people) is general because you can say 'except Zayd'. If it were specific to a particular person, you couldn't exclude anyone. The passage also presents the view of the Hanafi mashāyikh that the definite plural is metaphorically used for the genus when there is no 'ahd or istighrāq possible. They support this with examples: a man swearing not to marry women breaks his oath by marrying one woman (showing the plural is not literal), and the zakāh verse 'innamā al-sadaqātu li al-fuqarā' does not literally mean all poor, but the genus. This understanding preserves the validity of the definite article while acknowledging contextual limitations.

Key Terms
جمع معرف باللام (al-jam' al-mu'raf bi al-lām): A plural noun made definite by the definite article al-.
استغراق (istighrāq): Comprehension of all individuals; the literal meaning of the definite plural.
استثناء (istithnā'): Exception; a grammatical construction using 'illā' that is valid only if the base term is general.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the proofs given for the generality of the definite plural?
A) The validity of exception (istithnā') from it
B) The incident of Saqifa and the hadith 'al-a'immatu min quraysh'
C) The fact that the definite plural cannot be used for 'ahd
D) The unanimous consensus of the Sahaba at the Battle of Badr

Key Takeaway
The definite plural is a word of generality in Hanafi usul, proven by three arguments, but it can be metaphorically used for the genus when literal generality is impossible.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
The Definite Plural: Generality and Metaphorical Interpretation
Proving the general nature of the definite plural via exception and impossibility of full inclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the validity of exception proves the generality of the definite plural and apply the Hanafi rule that when full inclusion is impossible, the definite plural is interpreted as a metaphor for the genus.

Core Idea
The definite plural is general (proved by valid exception), but when full inclusion is impossible, it must be interpreted metaphorically as the genus.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the definite plural (al-jam' al-mu'arrif bi al-lam) is considered a general (amm) term. This lesson examines the key proof for its generality—the validity of exception (istithna')—and then explores the important Hanafi modification: when literal full inclusion is impossible, the plural is understood as a metaphor for the genus (majaz 'an al-jins). This principle has significant practical implications in interpreting Quranic verses and legal oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proof of generality
Read the first part of the passage to see how the validity of exception (istithna') demonstrates that the definite plural is general. For example, 'the people came except Zayd' shows that 'the people' includes all individuals except Zayd; if it were specific, exception would be meaningless.
The proof is linguistic: exception is only meaningful from a general term.
2
Understand the Hanafi modification
The passage then explains that when full inclusion (istighraq) is impossible (e.g., marrying all women), the definite plural is not taken literally but as a metaphor for the genus. This prevents the phrase from becoming nonsensical.
Key phrase: 'لعدم الفائدة' (due to lack of benefit).
3
Apply to the oath example
Consider the oath 'I will not marry women.' Marrying all women is impossible, so 'women' is interpreted as the genus. Thus, marrying one woman breaks the oath because the genus is realized.
This contrasts with a literal reading that would require marrying all women.
4
Apply to Quranic examples
The verse 'إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاء' (zakat is for the poor) cannot mean all poor people worldwide, so 'al-fuqara' is interpreted as the genus, indicating the category of recipients.
Similarly, 'لا يَحِلُّ لَكَ النِّسَاءُ مِنْ بَعْدُ' is interpreted as genus, permitting marrying one woman after the prohibition.
5
Distinguish when full inclusion is possible
The passage notes that if full inclusion is possible, the definite plural is taken literally as general, e.g., 'لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ' (eyes perceive Him not) means no eyes at all perceive Him.
This shows the rule is context-dependent.

( وَلَأنَّهُ لَمَّا لَمْ يَكُنُ هُنَاكَ مَعُهُودٌ ، وَلَيْسَ لِلاسْتِغْرَاقِ لِعَدَمِ الْفَائِدَةِ يَجِبُ حَمُلُهُ عَلَى تَعْرِيفِ الْجِنسِ ) ، وَإِنَّمَا قَالَ لِعَدَمِ الْفَائِدَةِ أَمَّا فِي قَوْلِهِ لَا أَتَزَوْجُ النِّسَاء فَلانَّ الْيَمِينَ لِلْمَنْعِ ، وَتَزَوُّجُ جَمِيعِ نِسَاء الدُّنْيَا غَيْرُ مُمْكِن فَمَنْعُهُ يَكُونُ لَغُوا ، وَفِي قَوْله تَعَالَى ) إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاء ( لا يُمْكِنُ صَرْفُ الصَّدَقَاتِ إِلَى جَمِيع فُقَرَاء الدُّنْيَا فَلا يَكُونُ الاسْتِعْرَاقَ مُوَادًا فَيَكُونُ لِتَعْرِيفِ الْجِنسِ مَجَازا فَتَكُونُ الْآيَةُ لِبَيَانِ مَصْرِفِ الزَّكَاةِ . ) فَتَبْقَى الْجَمْعِيَّةُ فِيهِ مِنْ وَجُهِ ، وَلَوْ لَمْ يُحْمَلُ عَلَى الْجِنْسِ لَبَطَلَ اللَّامُ أَصْلا) أَى إِذَا كَانَ اللَّامُ لِتَعْرِيفِ الْجِنْسِ ، وَمَعْنَى الْجَمْعِيَّةِ بَاقٍ فِى الْجِنْسِ مِنْ وَجْهِ لِأنَّ الْجنسَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ تَضَمُّنَّا فَعَلَى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ حَرْفٌ اللَّامِ مَعْمُولٌ وَمَعْنَى الْجَمْعِيَّةِ بَاقٍ مِنْ وَجُهِ ، وَلَوْ لَمْ يُحْمَلُ عَلَى هَذَا الْمَعْنَى ، وَتَبْقَى الْجَمْعِيَّةُ عَلَى حَالِهَا يَبْطُلُ اللَّامُ بالكلّيّةِ فَحَمُلُهُ عَلَى تَعْرِيفِ الْجِنسِ ، وَإِبْطَالِ الجَمْعِيَّةِ مِنْ وَجه أَوْلَى ، وَهَذَا مَعْنَى كَلَامِ فَخْرِ الْإِسْلامِ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ فِي بَابِ مُوجِبِ الْأَمْرِ فِي مَعْنَى العُمُومِ ، وَالتَّكْرَارٍ لَّانَّا إِذَا أَبْقَيْنَاهُ جَمْعًا لَغَا حَرْفَ الْعَهْدِ أَصَلا إلَى آخِرِهِ فَعَلِمَ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأَبْحَاثِ أَنَّ مَا قَالُوا أَنَّهُ يُحْمَلُ عَلَى الْجِنْسِ مَجَازَامُقَيَّدٌ بِصُورٍ لَا يُمْكِنُ حَمْلُهُ عَلَى الْعَهْدِ ، وَالاسْتِغْرَاقِ حَتَّى لَوْ أَمْكَنَ يُحْمَلُ عَلَيْهِ كَمَا فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى (لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ) فَإِنْ عُلَمَاء تَا قَالُوا إِنَّهُ لِسَلْبِ الْعُمُومِ لَا لِعُمُومِ السَّلْبِ فَجَعَلُوا اللام لاسْتِغْرَاقِ الْجِنْسَ . ) وَالْجَمْعُ الْمُعَرَّفَ بِغَيْرِ اللَّامِ نَحْو عَبِيدِى أَحْرَارٌ عَامٌ أَيْضًا لِصِحَّةِ الِاسْتِثْنَاءِ ، وَاخْتُلِفَ فِى الْجَمْعِ الْمُنْكَرِ ، وَالأَكْثَرُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ غَيْرُ عَامٌ ، وَعِنْدَ الْبَعْضِ عَامٌ لصحة الاسْتِنَاء كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ( لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَنَا ) ، وَالنَّحْوِيُّونَ حَمَلُوا إِلَّا عَلَى غَيْرِ .
Third proof: And because exception is valid. The third proof is that exception from the definite plural is valid. For example, if someone says 'the people came except Zayd,' it is correct. And the validity of this exception is evidence that the definite plural is general. Because if it were not general but specific and indicated a specific individual, then excepting from it would not be correct. Yet it is correct; therefore, the definite plural is general. Our scholars said: This plural (i.e., the plural with the definite article al-) is a metaphor for the genus, and plurality is negated. So if one swears 'I will not marry women,' he breaks the oath by marrying one woman. And by the verse 'Zakat is only for the poor,' the singular is intended. And if one bequeaths something to Zayd and to the poor, it is divided between him and them because of the verse 'It is not lawful for you [to marry other] women after this.' This is proof that the plural is a metaphor for the genus. And because when there is no specific referent and it is not for full inclusion due to lack of benefit, it must be interpreted as defining the genus. He only said 'due to lack of benefit.' As for his statement 'I will not marry women,' the oath is for prohibition, and marrying all the women of the world is impossible, so prohibiting that would be nonsense. And in the verse 'Zakat is only for the poor,' it is not possible to distribute all zakat to all the poor of the world, so full inclusion is not intended. Therefore it is for defining the genus metaphorically, and the verse is for explaining the categories of zakat. Thus, plurality remains in it from one aspect. And if it were not interpreted as genus, the al- (definite article) would become entirely void. That is, when the al- is for defining the genus, the meaning of plurality remains in the genus from one aspect because the genus implies multiplicity by entailment. So in this respect the particle al- is functioning and the meaning of plurality remains from one aspect. And if it were not interpreted in this meaning and plurality is retained, the al- would become completely void. So interpreting it as defining the genus and negating plurality from one aspect is more appropriate. This is the meaning of the statement of Fakhr al-Islam (may Allah have mercy on him) in the chapter on the implication of command regarding generality and repetition. He said: If we keep it as plural, the particle of specificity becomes completely void, etc. So it is understood from these discussions that what they said about it being interpreted as genus metaphorically is restricted to cases where it cannot be interpreted as a specific referent or full inclusion. If possible, it is interpreted accordingly, as in the verse 'Eyes perceive Him not.' The scholars said it is for the negation of generality, not the generality of negation, so they made the al- for the full inclusion of the genus. And the plural defined by other than al- like 'my slaves are free' is also general because of the validity of exception. And there is disagreement about the indefinite plural; the majority hold it is not general, while some consider it general because of the validity of exception, as in the verse 'Had there been besides Allah [other] gods, both would have been ruined.' And the grammarians interpreted 'illa' (except) as other than.
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage from Al-Tarweeh explains the rule that the definite plural (الجمع المعرف باللام) is general (عام) in nature. The third proof presented is the validity of exception (استثناء): one can say 'the people came except Zayd,' which shows the plural 'al-qawm' includes all individuals except the one excluded. If it were not general, exception would be meaningless. The passage then discusses the Hanafi position that when it is impossible to mean all individuals (استغراق), the definite plural is interpreted metaphorically as the genus (جنس). For example, if someone swears 'I will not marry women' (لا أتزوج النساء), it is impossible to marry all women, so the oath is interpreted as meaning the genus 'women'—thus marrying one woman breaks the oath. Similarly, the verse 'إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاء' (Zakat is only for the poor) does not mean all poor people worldwide, but the genus 'poor' as a category for zakat distribution. This metaphorical interpretation is obligatory when there is no specific referent (عهد) and full inclusion is impossible. If full inclusion were possible, the plural is taken as general, as in 'لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ' (Eyes perceive Him not)—here it means no eyes perceive Him at all. The passage also notes that plurals defined by other than 'al-' (e.g., 'عبيدي أحرار' my slaves are free) are also general if exception is valid. There is disagreement about the indefinite plural (الجمع المنكر): the majority consider it not general, but some (like the Hanafis) argue it is general based on the validity of exception in verses like 'لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ'.

Key Terms
الجمع المعرف باللام (al-jam' al-mu'arrif bi al-lam): A plural noun that is made definite by the definite article 'al-' (e.g., النساء, القوم).
استثناء (istithna'): The grammatical device of exception using 'إلا' (except); its validity is a proof of generality.
مجاز عن الجنس (majaz 'an al-jins): A metaphorical usage where the definite plural indicates the genus or category rather than all individual members.
استغراق (istighraq): The sense of full inclusion, i.e., applying to every individual member of the category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in this passage, how is the definite plural interpreted when it is impossible to mean all individuals?
A) It is still considered general (عام) and taken literally.
B) It is interpreted as a metaphor for the genus (مجاز عن الجنس).
C) It becomes meaningless (لغو).
D) It is considered specific (خاص) to a particular individual.

Key Takeaway
The definite plural is general, but when full inclusion is impossible, it is interpreted as a metaphor for the genus to avoid meaninglessness.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Rule of الجمع المعرف باللام: Carried on Genus Metaphorically
Explaining the metaphorical genus interpretation of definite plurals and the indefinite plural dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three possible meanings of الجمع المعرف باللام (covenant, comprehensiveness, genus) and apply the Hanafi rule that when comprehensiveness and covenant are impossible, it is carried metaphorically on the genus; additionally, you will be able to explain the disagreement on whether the indefinite plural is general and state the Hanafi preferred position.

Core Idea
When a definite plural cannot mean all or a specific group, it metaphorically means the genus, making one instance sufficient.

This lesson explores one of the most nuanced rules of Hanafi usul: interpreting the definite plural with 'al' when literal generality is impossible or absurd. We will also touch on a related dispute about the indefinite plural. Understanding these principles is essential for correctly deriving rulings from the Quran and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three possible meanings of 'al' in definite plurals
The passage explains that the definite article 'al' on a plural noun can indicate: (1) a specific known group (عهد), (2) comprehensiveness covering all individuals (استغراق), or (3) the genus or kind (جنس) metaphorically. Start by listing these options and their definitions.
Remember that عهد refers to a previously mentioned or contextually known group.
2
Apply the priority principle
When comprehensiveness or covenant is possible, the plural is interpreted accordingly. Only when both are impossible (e.g., marrying all women is impossible) does the genus reading take over. Use the example of the oath 'لا أتزوج النساء' to see this in action.
The impossibility of comprehensiveness can be practical (can't marry all women) or logical (can't give to all poor).
3
Observe the partial loss of plurality
When carried on the genus, the plural meaning (requiring multiple individuals) is partially abandoned to preserve the function of 'al'. The genus still implies multiplicity implicitly (جنس يدل على الكثرة تضمنا), but a single individual suffices for the ruling.
This is why one woman breaks the oath, one poor person receives zakah, etc.
4
Examine the dispute on the indefinite plural
The passage discusses whether الجمع المنكر (indefinite plural) is general (عام). The Hanafi majority say it is not, because exception (استثناء) is not valid in all cases. Some scholars argue it is general based on the Quranic verse 'لو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله لفسدتا', but grammarians reinterpret 'illa' as 'other than' (غير).
This dispute affects how texts like the verse on gods are interpreted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجنسَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ تَضَمُّنًا فَعَلَى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ حَرْفُ اللَّامِ مَعْمُولٌ وَمَعْنَى الْجَمْعِيَّةِ بَاقٍ مِنْ وَجْهٍ، وَلَوْ لَمْ يُحْمَلْ عَلَى هَذَا الْمَعْنَى، وَتَبْقَى الْجَمْعِيَّةُ عَلَى حَالِهَا يَبْطُلُ اللَّامُ بِالْكُلِّيَّةِ، فَحَمْلُهُ عَلَى تَعْرِيفِ الْجِنْسِ، وَإِبْطَالُ الْجَمْعِيَّةِ مِنْ وَجْهٍ أَوْلَى، وَهَذَا مَعْنَى كَلَامِ فَخْرِ الْإِسْلَامِ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ فِي بَابِ مُوجِبِ الْأَمْرِ فِي مَعْنَى الْعُمُومِ، وَالتَّكْرَارِ لِأَنَّا إِذَا أَبْقَيْنَاهُ جَمْعًا لَغَا حَرْفُ الْعَهْدِ أَصْلًا إِلَى آخِرِهِ، فَعُلِمَ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأَبْحَاثِ أَنَّ مَا قَالُوا أَنَّهُ يُحْمَلُ عَلَى الْجِنْسِ مَجَازًا مُقَيَّدٌ بِصُوَرٍ لَا يُمْكِنُ حَمْلُهُ عَلَى الْعَهْدِ، وَالِاسْتِغْرَاقِ حَتَّى لَوْ أَمْكَنَ يُحْمَلُ عَلَيْهِ كَمَا فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى (لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ) فَإِنَّ عُلَمَاءَنَا قَالُوا إِنَّهُ لِسَلْبِ الْعُمُومِ لَا لِعُمُومِ السَّلْبِ فَجَعَلُوا اللَّامَ لِاسْتِغْرَاقِ الْجِنْسِ.) وَالْجَمْعُ الْمُعَرَّفُ بِغَيْرِ اللَّامِ نَحْوُ عَبِيدي أَحْرَارٌ عَامٌ أَيْضًا لِصِحَّةِ الِاسْتِثْنَاءِ، وَاخْتُلِفَ فِي الْجَمْعِ الْمُنْكَرِ، وَالْأَكْثَرُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ غَيْرُ عَامٍ، وَعِنْدَ الْبَعْضِ عَامٌ لِصِحَّةِ الِاسْتِثْنَاءِ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى (لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَتَا)، وَالنَّحْوِيُّونَ حَمَلُوا إِلَّا عَلَى غَيْرِ.

ترجمہ: کہا ہے ہمارے مشائخ نے کہ یہ جمع یعنی معرف باللام ( مجاز ہے جنس سے اور باطل ہو جاتی ہے جمعیت حتی کہ اگر قسم اٹھائے کہ لا اتزوج النساء تو حانث ہو جائے گا ایک عورت سے نکاح کرنے سے، اور مراد لیا جاتا ہے ایک فقیر اللہ تعالی کے قول انما الصدقات للفقراء سے اور اگر وصیت کی کسی شی کی زید کیلئے اور فقراء کیلئے تو تنصیف کی جائے گی اس شی کی اس زید اور ان فقراء کے درمیان اللہ تعالی کے قول لا حل لک النساء من بعد کی وجہ سے) یہ دلیل ہے اس بات پر کہ بیشک جمع مجاز ہے جنس سے ( اور اس لیے کہ جب نہیں ہے یہاں معہود اور نہیں ہے استغراق کیلئے فائدہ کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تو واجب ہے اس کو محمول کرنا جنس کی تعریف پر) اور جز این نیست کہ کہا لعدم الفائدہ بہر حال اس کے قول لا اتزوج النساء میں پس تحقیق یمین رکنے کے لئے ہے اور دنیا کی تمام عورتوں سے نکاح کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے پس اس کا رکنا لغو ہو گا اور اللہ تعالٰی کے قول انما الصدقات للفقراء میں نہیں ہے ممکن صدقات کو پھیرنا دنیا جہاں کے تمام فقراء کی طرف۔ پس نہیں ہو گا مراد

[PAGE_607 continuation] استغراق تو ہو جائے گا جنس کی تعریف کیلئے مجاز آپس ہوگی آیت زکوۃ کے مصرف کو بیان کرنے کیلئے (پس باقی رہے گی جمعیت اس میں من وجہ اور اگر محمول نہ کیا جائے جنس پر تو البتہ باطل ہو جائے گا لام بالکل) یعنی لام جب جنس کی تعریف کیلئے ہو تو جمعیت کا معنی باقی ہے جنس میں من وجہ کیونکہ جنس دلالت کرتی ہے کثرت پر ضمنا پس اس طریقہ سے حرف لام معمول ہے۔ اور جمعیت کا معنی باقی ہے من وجہ اور اگر نہ محمول کیا جائے اس معنی پر اور باقی رہے جمعیت اپنی حالت پر تو باطل ہو جائے گا۔ لام کلی طور پر پس اس کو محمول کرنا جنس کی تعریف پر اور جمعیت کو من وجہ باطل کرنا اولی ہے اور یہ معنی فخر الاسلام کی کلام کا موجب الامرفی معنی العموم و التكرار کے باب میں لانا اذا بقيناه جمعا لغا حرف العهد الى آخره ( يعنى جب ہم اس کو باقی رکھیں گے تو لغو ہو جائے کا عہد بالکل ) پس معلوم ہو گیا ان بحثوں سے وہ جو انہوں نے کہا کہ بیشک اس لام کو معمول کیا جائے گا جنس پر مجاز آنیہ مقید ہے ایسی صورت کیساتھ نہ ممکن ہو اس کو محمول کرنا عہد استغراق پرحتی کہ اگر ممکن ہو تو محمول کیا جائے گا اس پر جیسا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے قول لا تدرکہ الابصار میں ہے کیونکہ ھمارے علماء نے کہا ہے کہ بیشک وہ سلب عموم کیلئے ہے نہ کہ عموم سلب کیلئے پس انہوں نے بنایا لام کو جنس کے استغراق کیلئے (جمع جو معرفہ ہو بغیر لام کے جیسے عبیدی احراز یہ بھی عام ہے استثناء کے صحیح ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اختلاف کیا گیا ہے جمع منکر میں اور اکثر حضرات اس بات پر ہیں کہ وہ عام نہیں ہے اور بعض حضرات کے نزدیک عام ہے استثناء کے صحیح ہونے کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول ہے لو كان فيهما الهة الا الله لفسدتا اور نحوی محمول کرتے ہیں الا کو غیر پر )
جمع معرف بالسلام سے جنس مراد لیتا مجاز ہے اور اس وقت اس کی جمعیت ٹوٹ جاتی ہے قال مشائخنا هذا الجمع ای الجمع الحلی بالام :۔ یہاں سے مان یہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ ہمارے مشائخ نے اس جمع معرف بالسلام کے بارے میں یہ کہا ہے کہ اس کو مجاز جنس پر بھی محمول کیا جاتا ہے اور اس وقت جمعیت والا معنی ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔ مثلاً اگر کوئی آدمی قسم اٹھاتا ہے کہ " لا اتزوج النساء" یہاں النساء میں جمعیت والا معنی مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ جنسیت والا معنی مراد ہے۔ لھذا حالف اگر ایک عورت کیساتھ نکاح کرے گا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اللہ تعالٰی کا فرن ہے انما الصدقات للفقراء یہاں فقراء پر الف لام جنس کا ہے اور آسمیں جنسیت والے معنی پر عمل کیا جائے گا اس لیے ایک فقیر کو صدقہ دینے سے بھی صدقہ ادا ہو جائے گا (صدقہ سے مراد زکوۃ وغیرہ ہے) اسی طرح اگر آدمی وصیت کرتا ہے کہ اومی المال لزيد واللفقراء تو یہاں فقراء سے کم از کم تین فقیر مراد لینا ضروری نہیں کہ مال کے چار حصے کر کے ایک حصہ زید کو اور باقی تین فقراء کو دیے جائیں۔ بلکہ اس میں جنسیت والا معنی مراد ہو گا اور ایک فقیر کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے مال دو حصوں میں تقسیم کیا جائے گا اور نصف
The genus indicates multiplicity implicitly, so in this way the letter 'lam' is operative and the meaning of collectivity remains in one respect. And if it is not carried on this meaning, and the collectivity remains as is, the 'lam' becomes entirely invalid. So carrying it on the definition of the genus and invalidating the collectivity in one respect is more appropriate. And this is the meaning of the statement of Fakhr al-Islam (may Allah have mercy on him) in the chapter on the requirement of the command regarding generality and repetition: 'When we keep it as a plural, the letter of covenant becomes entirely invalid…' So it is known from these investigations that what they said – that it is carried on the genus metaphorically – is restricted to cases where it is not possible to carry it on the covenant or comprehensiveness, such that if it is possible, it is carried on it as in His statement ( لا تدركه الأبصار ) for our scholars said it is for the negation of generality, not for the generality of negation, so they made the 'lam' for the comprehensiveness of the genus. And the plural defined without 'lam' like 'عبيدي أحرار' is also general because of the validity of exception. And there is disagreement regarding the indefinite plural; the majority hold it is not general, while some hold it is general due to the validity of exception as in His statement ( لو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله لفسدتا ), and the grammarians carry 'illa' on 'other'.
Source pages p. 606

Commentary
This passage is a rule from usul al-fiqh explaining how to interpret a definite plural noun with the definite article 'al' (الجمع المعرف باللام). The author, commenting on Fakhr al-Islam's discussion on the command and generality, states that when a plural noun is prefixed with 'al', if it cannot be interpreted as referring to a specific known group (عهد) or as including all individuals (استغراق), then it is taken metaphorically to indicate the genus (جنس). This means the plural meaning is partially abandoned to preserve the function of 'al'. For example, in an oath like 'لا أتزوج النساء' (I will not marry women), if interpreted as all women, the oath would be impossible to fulfill, so it is interpreted as the genus, meaning he will not marry any woman, and marrying one woman would break the oath. Similarly, Quranic verse 'إنما الصدقات للفقراء' (alms are for the poor) is interpreted for the genus, so giving to one poor person suffices for zakah. In a will giving to 'Zaid and the poor', the poor are interpreted as the genus, so the property is divided into two halves: one for Zaid and one for the poor (any individual poor person). The passage also addresses plural defined without 'al' (e.g., 'عبيدي أحرار' my slaves are free) as general due to valid exception. The indefinite plural is disputed: majority say not general, some say general. The example 'لو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله لفسدتا' is given for the latter, but grammarians treat 'illa' differently. This demonstrates the nuanced Hanafi usul approach to interpreting plurals, prioritizing the function of the definite article over strict plural meaning.

Key Terms
الجمع المعرف باللام (al-jam‘ al-mu‘arraf bi al-lam): A plural noun that is made definite by the prefix 'al' (e.g., النساء, الفقراء).
العهد (al-‘ahd): Referring to a specific known group or individuals previously mentioned or known by context.
الاستغراق (al-istighraq): Comprehensiveness, meaning all individuals of that category without exception.
الجنس (al-jins): The genus or category, indicating the kind or type rather than specific individuals or all members.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage, where the word is used in a sense other than its primary meaning due to a contextual constraint.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man swears, 'لا أتزوج النساء' (I will not marry women). According to the rule explained in this passage, what is the ruling if he later marries one woman?
A) He does not break his oath because 'women' means all women, and marrying one does not fulfill the condition of all.
B) He breaks his oath because 'women' is interpreted as the genus, so marrying any woman is included in the prohibition.
C) He does not break his oath because the plural is indefinite and not general.
D) He breaks his oath only if he marries three women, proving the plural requires multiple.

Key Takeaway
When a definite plural with 'al' cannot indicate all or a specific group, it is interpreted as the genus metaphorically, allowing one instance to suffice.

Interpretation of Definite Plural as Genus
Explaining rule when definite plural is interpreted as genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a definite plural is interpreted as genus and apply the rule to derive the correct legal meaning in Quranic verses and legal documents.

Core Idea
A definite plural is interpreted as genus when covenant and totality are impossible, and the collective sense is partially retained.

In Hanafi usul, the definite plural (al-jam' al-mu'arraf bi al-lam) has three possible meanings: covenant, totality, or genus. The default is covenant, then totality, but when both are impossible, it shifts to genus as a metaphor. This lesson unpacks that rule and its application using classical examples from oaths, charity, wills, and Quranic prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definite plural
Locate the plural noun prefixed with alif-lam in the text. This is the starting point for analysis.
2
Check for covenant (al-‘ahd)
Determine if the plural refers to a group previously mentioned or known from context. If so, interpret as covenant and stop.
If not previously mentioned, covenant is impossible.
3
Check for totality (al-istiqhraq)
Evaluate whether interpreting the plural as including all individuals is feasible. If it leads to impossibility or no benefit (e.g., impossible to perform), reject totality.
Totality is rejected when it creates taklif ma la yutaq (obligation beyond capacity).
4
Interpret as genus (al-jins)
If both covenant and totality are impossible, interpret the plural as genus metaphorically. The lam now defines the genus, and the plural form partially retains its collective sense (min wajh).
The collective sense is partially lost because the term can apply to one or two, but partially retained because both plural form and genus imply abundance.
5
Derive the legal consequence
Apply the genus meaning to the specific case. For example, a single individual suffices to fulfill the command or break the oath.
The lam is given a function; otherwise it would be superfluous.

جمع معرف بالسلام سے جنس مراد لیتا مجاز ہے اور اس وقت اس کی جمعیت ٹوٹ جاتی ہے قال مشائخنا هذا الجمع ای الجمع الحلی بالام :۔ یہاں سے مان یہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ ہمارے مشائخ نے اس جمع معرف بالسلام کے بارے میں یہ کہا ہے کہ اس کو مجاز جنس پر بھی محمول کیا جاتا ہے اور اس وقت جمعیت والا معنی ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔ مثلاً اگر کوئی آدمی قسم اٹھاتا ہے کہ " لا اتزوج النساء" یہاں النساء میں جمعیت والا معنی مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ جنسیت والا معنی مراد ہے۔ لھذا حالف اگر ایک عورت کیساتھ نکاح کرے گا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اللہ تعالٰی کا فرن ہے انما الصدقات للفقراء یہاں فقراء پر الف لام جنس کا ہے اور آسمیں جنسیت والے معنی پر عمل کیا جائے گا اس لیے ایک فقیر کو صدقہ دینے سے بھی صدقہ ادا ہو جائے گا (صدقہ سے مراد زکوۃ وغیرہ ہے) اسی طرح اگر آدمی وصیت کرتا ہے کہ اومی المال لزيد واللفقراء تو یہاں فقراء سے کم از کم تین فقیر مراد لینا ضروری نہیں کہ مال کے چار حصے کر کے ایک حصہ زید کو اور باقی تین فقراء کو دیے جائیں۔ بلکہ اس میں جنسیت والا معنی مراد ہو گا اور ایک فقیر کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے مال دو حصوں میں تقسیم کیا جائے گا اور نصف زید کو نصف کسی فقیر کو دیدیا جائے گا۔
اسی طرح اللہ تعالی کا فرمان ہے "لا تحل لک النساء من بعد" یہاں آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو یہ نہیں کہا گیا ان موجودہ زوجات کے علاوہ دنیا کی تمام اور عورتوں سے نکاح نہیں کر سکتے ایک دو کیساتھ نکاح کر سکتے ہو بلکہ سرے سے کسی عورت سے بھی نکاح کرنے سے منع کیا گیا ہے اور یہ بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ النساء میں الف لام جنس کا ہو۔
تو مذکورہ بالا تمام امثلہ میں جمع معرف بالام کو جنس پر محمول کیا گیا ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہاں اس کو عہد پر محمول نہیں کر سکتے کہ اسی طرح استغراق پر بھی محمول نہیں کر سکتے ۔ عہد پر اس لیے محمول نہیں کر سکتے کہ یہ تمام الفاظ معہود نہیں ہیں یعنی ماقبل میں انکا ذکر نہیں ہوا اور استغراق پر اس لیے محمول نہیں کر سکتے کہ استغراق پر محمول کرنے کا کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ اول مثال لا اتزوج النساء" میں تو اس لئے فائدہ نہیں ہے کہ قسم منع کیلئے ہے یعنی اپنے آپ کو روکنے کیلئے تو اگر النساء میں استغراق ہو مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ حالف اپنے آپ کو دنیا کی تمام عورتوں سے نکاح کرنے سے منع کر رہا ہے حالانکہ یہ تو اس کے بس میں ہی نہیں ہے تو روکنے کا کیا فائدہ تو قسم لغو ہو جائے گی کوئی فائدہ نہیں رہے گا۔ اور دوسری اور تیسری مثال " انما الصدقات للفقراء اور وصیت والی مثال میں اس لیے فائدہ نہیں ہے کہ تمام فقراء کو صدقہ اور مال پہنچا ناممکن نہیں ہے ۔ تو استغراق والے معنی سے ” تکلیف مالا طاق لازم آئے گی۔ اسی طرح آخری مثال لا حل لک النساء میں کہ تمام عورتوں سے نکاح کرنا تو ممکن ہی نہیں ہے تو منع کرنے کا کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ تو جب تمام صورتوں میں الف لام سے نہ عہد مراد لے سکتے ہیں نہ ہی استغراق تو اس کو مجاز ا جنس پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔
جمع معرف بالسلام سے مراد جب جنس ہو تو من وجہ جمعیت باقی رہتی ہے الجمعية فيه من وجہ:۔ یہاں سے تفریح ذکر کر رہے ہیں جب معرف باسلام کو جنس پر محمول کر لیا جائے تو اس میں جمعہ من وجہ ختم ہو جائے گی اور من وجہ باقی رہے گی۔ میں وجہ ختم تو اس لیے ہوگی کہ اس کا اطلاق ایک اور دو پر بھی ہوگا حالانکہ جمع کا اطلاق کم از کم تین پر ہوتا ہے۔ اور من وجہ باقی اس لیے رہے گی کہ جمع کا صیغہ کثرت پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور جنس بھی تضمناً کثرت پر دلالت کرتی ہے۔
فائدہ: ماتن فرماتے ہیں کہ اس جمع معرف باسلام کو جنس پر محمول کر کے جمعیت والا معنی من وجہ ختم اس لیے کیا ہے کہ اگر جمعیت والا معنی کو باقی رکھا جائے تو الف لام باطل ہو جائے گا اس کا کوئی فائدہ نہیں رہے گا ۔ کیونکہ جمعیت والا معنی تو الف لام کے بغیر بھی اس میں موجود تھا تو اگر الف لام کے بعد بھی اس میں صرف جمعیت والا معنی باقی رہے تو الف لام بالکل
The totality will occur, for the definition of genus it is a metaphor, for explaining the verse of zakat's expenditure (so the collective meaning remains in it partially, and if it is not interpreted as genus, then the lam becomes completely invalid). That is, when lam is for definition of genus, the meaning of collectivity remains in the genus partially, because genus indicates abundance implicitly. So in this way the letter lam is operative. And the meaning of collectivity remains partially. And if it is not interpreted on this meaning and the collectivity remains in its state, then the lam becomes completely invalid. So interpreting it as definition of genus and partially invalidating collectivity is preferable. And this meaning is the purport of Fakhr al-Islam's statement in the chapter of 'al-amr fi ma'na al-umum wa al-tikrar': 'When we retain it as collective, the letter of covenant becomes completely void.' So it is known from these discussions what they said: that indeed this lam will be interpreted as genus metaphorically, but it is restricted to such a case where it is not possible to interpret it as covenant or totality, so that if possible, it will be interpreted accordingly, as in the saying of Allah Most High 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' because our scholars said that it is for negation of generality, not for generality of negation. So they based the lam on totality of genus. (A plural that is definite without lam, like 'Ubaidi ihraz? This is also general due to the validity of exception. And disagreement occurred regarding indefinite plural: most scholars hold that it is not general, but some hold it is general due to validity of exception, as in Allah's saying 'Law kana fihima alihatun illa Allahu lafasadata' and grammarians interpret 'illa' as 'ghair'.) 
A plural definite with alif lam when taken to mean genus is a metaphor, and at that time its collectivity is broken. They said: Our mashayikh said regarding this plural (i.e., the plural with lam): it is also interpreted as genus metaphorically, and at that time the meaning of collectivity disappears. For example, if a man swears an oath saying 'La atazawwaj al-nisa'', here 'al-nisa' does not mean collectivity but rather the meaning of genus. Hence if the swearer marries one woman, he will break his oath. Similarly, Allah Most High says 'Innama al-sadaqatu lil fuqara'', here 'al-fuqara' has lam of genus, and the meaning of genus is acted upon, so giving charity to one poor person suffices. Similarly, if a person makes a will saying 'Umi al-mal li Zaydin wa lil fuqara'', then here it is not necessary to take 'al-fuqara' as meaning at least three poor persons such that the wealth is divided into four parts: one part to Zayd and the remaining three to the poor. Rather, the meaning of genus is intended, and considering one poor person, the wealth will be divided into two halves: half to Zayd and half to some poor person. Similarly, Allah's command 'La tahillu laka al-nisa' min ba'd' does not mean that you cannot marry all other women except your current wives; rather, it prohibits marrying any woman at all. And it is possible that 'al-nisa' has lam of genus. So in all the mentioned examples, the definite plural is interpreted as genus, and the reason is that it cannot be interpreted as covenant (because these words are not previously mentioned) nor as totality (because interpreting as totality yields no benefit). In the first example of oath, there is no benefit because the oath is for prohibition (restricting oneself), so if 'al-nisa' means totality, the swearer would be prohibiting himself from marrying all women, which is impossible, so the oath would be pointless. In the second and third examples, there is no benefit because giving charity or wealth to all poor people is impossible, so totality leads to impossibility (taklif ma la yutak). Similarly, in the last example, marrying all women is impossible, so prohibition has no benefit. Hence when in all cases neither covenant nor totality can be intended, it is interpreted as genus metaphorically. When the definite plural is taken as genus, the collectivity remains partially (min wajh). Here they clarify: when the definite plural is interpreted as genus, the collectivity disappears partially and remains partially. It disappears partially because it applies to one or two, whereas plural applies to at least three. And it remains partially because the form of plural indicates abundance, and genus also indicates abundance implicitly. Benefit: The matan says that interpreting the definite plural as genus and partially removing collectivity is done because if collectivity is retained, the lam would become invalid and useless. Because the meaning of collectivity was already present without the lam, so if after adding the lam only collectivity remains, the lam becomes completely invalid.
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage is a rule explanation from a Hanafi usul work. It discusses the interpretation of the definite plural (al-jam' al-mu'arraf bi al-lam). The rule: When the definite plural cannot be interpreted as 'ahd (covenant, referring to a previously known group) or istighraq (totality, all individuals), it is interpreted as jins (genus) as a metaphor (majaz). This is because the primary meanings (aha) are covenant and totality, but if both are impossible, we resort to genus. The passage gives four examples: an oath 'I will not marry women' where taking totality is impossible (since one cannot marry all women), Quranic verse 'alms are for the poor' where giving to all poor is impossible, a will 'my wealth for Zayd and the poor' where totality is impossible, and the verse 'women are not permissible for you after' where marrying all women is impossible. In each, the lam of definition of genus is used. The author explains why covenant is impossible: the words are not previously mentioned. Then explains why istighraq is impossible: it would lead to impossibility (taklif ma la yutak) or no benefit. The passage also notes that when interpreted as genus, the meaning of collectivity (jama'iyya) is partially retained (min wajh): it is lost because the word can apply to one or two (whereas plural normally requires three), but retained because both the plural form and genus imply abundance. A 'benefit' section (fa'ida) clarifies: if we kept the collectivity, the lam would be superfluous, so we interpret as genus to give the lam a function. The author quotes Fakhr al-Islam and mentions the mashayikh's view. This is a detailed usul discussion of how to treat the definite article with plurals when literal meanings fail.

Key Terms
الجمع المعرّف باللام (al-jam' al-mu'arraf bi al-lam): A plural noun prefixed with the definite article alif lam.
العهد (al-'ahd): Reference to a specific previously mentioned or known group.
الاستغراق (al-istiqhraq): Inclusion of all individuals of the category without exception.
الجنس (al-jins): The genus or category as a whole, not specifying number.
الجمعية (al-jama'iyya): The property of indicating plurality (at least three).
من وجه (min wajh): Partially; from one aspect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the oath 'la atazawwaj al-nisa'', why is the definite plural 'al-nisa' interpreted as genus rather than totality?
A) Because the word 'al-nisa' is not previously mentioned.
B) Because taking totality would make the oath impossible to fulfill, leading to no benefit.
C) Because the lam is definite, so it must indicate genus.
D) Because the Qur'an uses it that way.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the definite plural is interpreted as genus when covenant and totality are impossible, preserving the function of the definite article.

Interpreting Definite Plural as Genus in Hanafi Usul
Usul rule: when to interpret definite plural as genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify contexts where the definite plural (جمع معرف باللام) must be interpreted as genus rather than covenant or inclusive totality, and apply the rule to new examples.

Core Idea
Interpret definite plural as genus only when covenant and inclusive totality are impossible.

When you encounter a definite plural in a legal text (e.g., 'the poor' in the zakat verse), it usually refers to all individuals or a specific set. But sometimes that leads to impossibility or futility. Hanafi usul says: in such cases, take the alif lam as indicating the genus — a metaphorical meaning that preserves the essence of the category. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and examples from the source passage.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the three possible meanings of alif lam in a definite plural
The definite article can indicate covenant (عهد: a known set), inclusive totality (استغراق: all individuals), or genus (جنس: the kind). The first two are literal; genus is metaphorical.
Hanafi usul treats عهد and استغراق as primary.
2
Check for impossibility of literal meanings
For each occurrence, ask: Can it refer to a previously mentioned set? If not, can it refer to all individuals without leading to logical or practical impossibility (e.g., impossible obligation, futile oath)?
Impossibility can be due to incapacity or futility.
3
If both literal meanings are impossible, adopt genus
When neither عهد nor استغراق works, default to genus. The alif lam is then metaphorical, indicating the kind rather than all instances.
Plurality is partly retained (multiplicity implied) and partly lost (can apply to one or two).
4
Apply the rule to the examples in the passage
Work through the oath, the poor, the will, and the Prophet's marriages. Confirm why عهد and استغراق fail, and why genus saves the meaning.
Each example illustrates a different type of impossibility.
5
Contrast with cases where literal meaning applies
When literal interpretation is possible (e.g., 'لا تدركه الأبصار'), the definite plural retains its inclusive totality meaning. Genus is only for when the literal fails.
The rule: literal is used unless impossible.

اسی طرح اللہ تعالی کا فرمان ہے "لا تحل لک النساء من بعد" یہاں آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو یہ نہیں کہا گیا ان موجودہ زوجات کے علاوہ دنیا کی تمام اور عورتوں سے نکاح نہیں کر سکتے ایک دو کیساتھ نکاح کر سکتے میں استغراق ہو مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ حالف اپنے آپ کو دنیا کی تمام عورتوں سے نکاح کرنے سے منع کر رہا ہے حالانکہ یہ تو اس کے بس میں ہی نہیں ہے تو روکنے کا کیا فائدہ تو قسم لغو ہو جائے گی کوئی فائدہ نہیں رہے گا۔ اور دوسری اور تیسری مثال " انما الصدقات للفقراء اور وصیت والی مثال میں اس لیے فائدہ نہیں ہے کہ تمام فقراء کو صدقہ اور مال پہنچا ناممکن نہیں ہے ۔ تو استغراق والے معنی سے ” تکلیف مالا طاق لازم آئے گی۔ اسی طرح آخری مثال لا حل لک النساء میں کہ تمام عورتوں سے نکاح کرنا تو ممکن ہی نہیں ہے تو منع کرنے کا کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ تو جب تمام صورتوں میں الف لام سے نہ عہد مراد لے سکتے ہیں نہ ہی استغراق تو اس کو مجاز ا جنس پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ جمع معرف بالسلام سے مراد جب جنس ہو تو من وجہ جمعیت باقی رہتی ہے الجمعية فيه من وجہ:۔ یہاں سے تفریح ذکر کر رہے ہیں جب معرف باسلام کو جنس پر محمول کر لیا جائے تو اس میں جمعہ من وجہ ختم ہو جائے گی اور من وجہ باقی رہے گی۔ میں وجہ ختم تو اس لیے ہوگی کہ اس کا اطلاق ایک اور دو پر بھی ہوگا حالانکہ جمع کا اطلاق کم از کم تین پر ہوتا ہے۔ اور من وجہ باقی اس لیے رہے گی کہ جمع کا صیغہ کثرت پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور جنس بھی تضمناً کثرت پر دلالت کرتی ہے۔ فائدہ: ماتن فرماتے ہیں کہ اس جمع معرف باسلام کو جنس پر محمول کر کے جمعیت والا معنی من وجہ ختم اس لیے کیا ہے کہ اگر جمعیت والا معنی کو باقی رکھا جائے تو الف لام باطل ہو جائے گا اس کا کوئی فائدہ نہیں رہے گا ۔ کیونکہ جمعیت والا معنی تو الف لام کے بغیر بھی اس میں موجود تھا تو اگر الف لام کے بعد بھی اس میں صرف جمعیت والا معنی باقی رہے تو الف لام بالکل باطل ہو جائے گا اس لیے اس کو جنس پر محمول کرنا اولیٰ ہے اسی بات کو امام فخر الاسلام نے عموم کے تکرار کے بارے میں امر کے موجب کی بحث میں ان الفاظ میں بیان کیا ہے کہ اگر ہم جمع کو جمع کے معنی میں باقی رکھیں تو حرف عہد یعنی الف لام باطل ہو جائے گا۔ فعلم من هذه الابحاث:۔ یہاں سے مائن یہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ ان ابحاث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جمع معرف باسلام کو مجازاً جنس پر اس وقت محمول کیا جائے گا جب اس کو عہد یا استغراق پر محمول کرنا ممکن نہ ہو کیونکہ ضابطہ ہے کہ حقیقت کو اس وقت ترک کیا جا سکتا ہے جب حقیقی معنی مراد لینا متعذر ہو۔ اگر عہد یا استغراق پر محمول کرنا ممکن ہو تو پھر اس کو اپنے حقیقی معنی یعنی استغراق وغیرہ پر محمول کیا جائے گا نہ کہ جنس پر جیسے لا تدرکہ الابصار یہاں علماء نے فرمایا ہے کہ یفی سلب عموم کیلئے ہے یعنی عموم کا ہی سلب کیا گیا ہے عموم سلب کیلئے نہیں یعنی نفی کو عام نہیں کیا گیا کہ بعض سے ہو یا تمام سے۔ تو یہاں انہوں نے الف لام کو استغراق پر محمول کیا ہے۔
Similarly, Allah's command: "Women are not lawful for you after this" – here the Prophet is not told that he cannot marry all the women of the world except his current wives, but rather that he is prohibited from marrying any woman at all, and it is possible that the alif lam in "women" is for genus. So in all the aforementioned examples, the definite plural is interpreted as genus, and the reason is that it cannot be interpreted as covenant (عهد) nor as inclusive totality (استغراق). It cannot be interpreted as covenant because these words are not previously mentioned. It cannot be interpreted as inclusive totality because there is no benefit in taking that meaning. In the first example, "I will not marry women" – if it were inclusive totality, it would mean the swearer is prohibiting himself from marrying all women in the world, which is beyond his ability, so the oath would be futile. In the second and third examples (alms are for the poor and the will), taking inclusive totality would lead to an obligation beyond capacity. Similarly, the last example "Women are not lawful for you" – marrying all women is impossible, so prohibition has no benefit. When in all cases neither covenant nor inclusive totality can be intended, it is interpreted metaphorically as genus. When the definite plural is interpreted as genus, the plurality aspect is partly lost and partly retained. Lost because it can apply to one or two, while plural requires at least three; retained because the plural form indicates multiplicity and genus also implicitly indicates multiplicity. Benefit: The author says that by interpreting the definite plural as genus, the meaning of plurality is partially removed so that the alif lam does not become meaningless. If the plurality meaning were retained, the alif lam would be redundant. Imam Fakhr al-Islam expressed this in the discussion of repetition of generality concerning the command. So it is learned from these investigations that the definite plural is metaphorically interpreted as genus only when it is impossible to interpret it as covenant or inclusive totality, because the rule is that the literal meaning is abandoned only when it is impossible to take it. If it is possible to interpret it as covenant or inclusive totality, then it is interpreted in its literal meaning (inclusive totality etc.), not as genus, as in the verse "No vision can grasp Him" – here they interpreted the alif lam as inclusive totality.
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of how to interpret the definite plural (جمع معرف باللام) in Arabic when it appears in legal texts. The Hanafi usul scholars use examples from the Quran and everyday speech to show that the alif lam in a definite plural cannot always be taken as indicating all individuals (استغراق) or a specific set (عهد). When both are impossible due to logical or practical reasons, the alif lam is taken as indicating the genus (جنس), which is a metaphorical use. The passage goes through several examples: an oath, the verse on alms, a will, and the Quranic verse about the Prophet's marriages. In each, interpreting the plural as all individuals leads to impossibility or futility. The author then explains that this interpretation preserves some aspect of plurality (since both plural form and genus imply multiplicity) while removing the strict requirement of three individuals. The فائدة emphasizes that this interpretation saves the alif lam from being redundant, as the plural form alone already indicates multiplicity. Finally, the passage concludes with a rule: the metaphorical interpretation (as genus) is only used when the literal interpretations (عهد or استغراق) are impossible; otherwise, the literal meaning is retained, as in the example "لا تدركہ الابصار" where the alif lam is taken as inclusive totality because the negation of all visions is intended.

Key Terms
جمع معرف باللام (jam‘ mu‘arraf bi al-lām): A plural noun defined with the definite article alif lam.
عهد (‘ahd): Referring to a specific, previously mentioned set of individuals.
استغراق (istighrāq): Inclusive totality, referring to all individuals of the kind.
جنس (jins): Genus, the kind or type, implying the essence without specifying number.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is the definite plural (جمع معرف باللام) interpreted metaphorically as genus?
A) When it is impossible to interpret it as covenant or inclusive totality
B) When it refers to women
C) When the speaker intends a metaphorical meaning
D) Always, because genus is the default

Key Takeaway
The definite plural is interpreted as genus only when both covenant and inclusive totality are impossible; otherwise, the literal meaning is retained.

Definite Plural by Idafa is General
States the ruling on definite plural by idafa being general

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a definite plural without alif lam is general, using the validity of istithna' as a test.

Core Idea
A plural made definite by idafa is general: if you can except one, it covers all.

This lesson clarifies a key Hanafi principle about generality in definite plurals. In Arabic grammar, definiteness can be achieved through the article alif lam or through idafa (construct). The Hanafi school holds that both types are general in meaning, and the evidence lies in the permissibility of making an exception (istithna'). Understanding this helps us interpret legal texts correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the plural form
Locate the plural noun and determine how it is made definite. In 'عبيدي أحرار', 'عبيدي' is a plural noun made definite by idafa (construct) because it is attached to the possessive pronoun 'ي' (my).
2
Distinguish definiteness types
Is it definite by alif lam or by idafa? Here it is by idafa. The Hanafi principle applies to both types, but some may mistakenly think only alif lam indicates generality.
This distinction is crucial for istinbat.
3
Apply the generality rule
State the rule: A definite plural without alif lam (e.g., by idafa) is general (عام). This means it encompasses all individuals of that category unless evidence specifies otherwise.
This is a well-established Hanafi rule.
4
Test with istithna'
Check if exclusion (istithna') is valid. In the example, one can say 'except Zaid' after 'عبيدي أحرار'. If the statement were not general, exclusion would be meaningless. The validity of exclusion confirms generality.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجمع المعرف بغیر السلام :۔ پہلے تو ا جمع کا حکم بیان کیا جو عرف بالسلام ہو اب اس جمع کا حکم بیان فرمارہے ہیں جو معرف تو ہو لیکن معرف با الام نہ ہو معرف بغیر اسلام ہو جیسے عبیدی احرار " یہاں عبیدی جمع ہے اور معرف باضافت ہے معرف بالسلام نہیں ہے۔ تو اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ یہ بھی عام ہوتا ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہی ہے کہ اس سے استثناء کرنا درست ہوتا ہے حالانکہ اگر یہ عام نہ ہوتا تو اس سے استثناء کرنا درست نہ ہوتا۔
And the definite plural without the definite article: Previously, the ruling of the plural that is definite with the alif lam was mentioned. Now, the ruling of the plural that is definite but not with the alif lam is mentioned, such as 'عبيدي أحرار' (my slaves, free). Here 'عبيدي' is a plural and is definite by idafa (construct), not by alif lam. Its ruling is that it is also general, and the reason is that exclusion from it is valid, whereas if it were not general, exclusion would not be valid.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage is a fiqh rule about definiteness in plurals. It clarifies that a plural noun can be made definite not only by the definite article (alif lam) but also by idafa (construct phrase, e.g., 'my slaves'). The author states that such a definite plural (without alif lam) is considered general (عام), meaning it applies to all individuals of that category. The proof offered is that it is permissible to make an exception (استثناء) from such a phrase. In Arabic grammar, exclusion (istithna') is only valid from a general statement; if the statement were not general, exclusion would be meaningless. For example, if one says 'my slaves are free' (عبيدي أحرار), one can make an exception: 'except Zaid'. This shows that the phrase 'my slaves' is understood as referring to all of them, i.e., it is general. This is a standard Hanafi usul principle.

Key Terms
جمع معرف بغير السلام (jam‘ mu‘arraf bi ghayr al-ism): A plural noun that is definite but not by the definite article alif lam, e.g., by idafa (construct).
إضافة (iḍāfa): A grammatical construct where a noun is made definite by being attached to another noun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a plural noun that is definite by idafa (e.g., 'عبيدي')?
A) It is not general because it lacks alif lam.
B) It is general, as evidenced by the validity of exceptional exclusion.
C) It is specific to the context of the speaker.
D) It depends on the intention of the speaker.

Key Takeaway
A definite plural without alif lam (e.g., by idafa) is general in Hanafi usul, proven by the validity of istithna'.

Is Indefinite Plural General? The Hanafi Dispute
Presents the disagreement on whether indefinite plural is general

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi majority position on the generality of indefinite plural and apply the distinction between indefinite singular and plural to interpret legal commands.

Core Idea
An indefinite plural is not general; like the singular, it applies to any instance, not all.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, one of the key distinctions is between definite and indefinite nouns. This passage examines a specific dispute: does the indefinite plural (e.g., رجال) indicate generality (عموم) just like the definite plural? The majority of Hanafi scholars say it does not, and this has practical consequences for how commands and prohibitions are interpreted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State clearly what each side claims about the indefinite plural: is it general (عام) or not?
Majority: not general; minority: general.
2
Analyse the majority proof
Understand the analogy with the indefinite singular: just as 'رجل' applies to any man without implying all, 'رجال' applies to any group without implying all.
Key concept: على سبيل البدلية (substitutive manner).
3
Analyse the minority proof
The minority argues that exclusion (استثناء) from indefinite plural is valid in Arabic, as in the Quranic verse (21:22), suggesting it is general.
The verse is incomplete in the text but serves as evidence.
4
Evaluate the practical implication (ثمرة الخلاف)
If indefinite plural is general, a command like 'أكرم فقراء' would require honoring all poor people; if not, it is sufficient to honor any poor person(s).
5
Relate to the Hanafi school
The majority view is relied upon in Hanafi practice. The minority view is acknowledged but not preferred.
Tarjih: majority due to stronger linguistic analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف في المجمع المنکر :۔ یہاں سے ماتن مجمع منکر کا حکم بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ جمع منکر کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ اکثر حضرات فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ عام نہیں ہوتا اور دلیل یہ دیتے ہیں کہ استعمالات میں رجال کا اطلاق رجل کی طرح ہوتا ہے کہ جس طرح وہ علی سبیل البدلیت تمام افراد پر بولا جاتا ہے اور اس میں استغراق نہیں پایا جاتا اسی طرح رجال کا اطلاق بھی علی سبیل الہدلیت تمام افراد پر ہوتا ہے اس میں بھی استغراق اور شمول نہیں ہوتا اور بعض حضرات فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ عام ہوتا ہے اور اس کی دلیل یہ دیتے ہیں کہ اس سے استثناء کرنا درست ہے۔ جیسا کہ قرآن پاک میں ہے ”لو کان فیهما البتہ الا الله لفسد تا
And there is disagreement regarding the indefinite plural: The author is stating the ruling of the indefinite plural. The majority hold that it is not general, and their proof is that in usage, 'men' (رجال) is applied like 'man' (رجل), i.e., it is applied to all individuals in a substitutive manner without inclusive totality. Similarly, 'men' is applied to all individuals in a substitutive manner without inclusive totality. Some scholars hold that it is general, and their proof is that exclusion from it is valid, as in the Quranic verse: "If there had been in them any gods except Allah, they would have been corrupted" (incomplete).
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage presents a disagreement (ikhtilaf) in Hanafi usul about whether the indefinite plural (جمع منكر, e.g., رجال) is general (عام) or not. The majority opinion is that it is not general. Their reasoning is that the indefinite singular (e.g., رجل) is used to refer to any individual of the kind without implying all; similarly, the indefinite plural (رجال) is used to refer to any group of individuals of that kind without implying all. In other words, it indicates a substitutive sense (بدلية), not totality. A minority argues that it is general because exclusion (استثناء) from it is permissible in Arabic. For example, the Quranic verse (21:22) uses an indefinite plural and then excludes, suggesting generality. The passage provides this brief presentation; the full argument would continue, but the OCR cuts off. This is a classic usul dispute where the majority relies on the nature of indefinite nouns, while the minority relies on the linguistic practice of exception.

Key Terms
جمع منكر (jam‘ munkar): An indefinite plural noun, e.g., رجال (men).
على سبيل البدلية (‘alā sabīl al-badalīyah): In a substitutive manner, meaning it applies to any individual but not all.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the majority opinion regarding the indefinite plural's indication of generality?
A) It is general, like the definite plural
B) It is not general, because it is used substitutively like the singular
C) It is general only if its individuals are countable
D) It is not general because it is indefinite

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority holds that indefinite plural is not general; it functions like indefinite singular in applying substitutively.

Rule for Definite Plural with ال when Used Metaphorically for Genus
States the Hanafi rule for interpreting definite plural nouns.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that the definite plural (جمع معرف باللام) is interpreted literally as ʿahd or istighrāq, and only when both are impossible does it shift metaphorically to genus (jins).

Core Idea
The definite plural is literal first; metaphorical genus is only when literal is impossible.

In this lesson, we explore a key Hanafi usul principle governing the interpretation of definite plural nouns (جمع معرف باللام). The default is to understand them as referring to all individuals (istighrāq) or a specific set (ʿahd). Only when these literal meanings are impossible in context does the interpreter shift to a metaphorical genus reading. The Quranic verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' serves as an example where istighrāq is upheld.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic form
Recognize the definite plural (جمع معرف باللام) in the text. This is the starting point for analysis.
The term 'الأبصار' in the example is a جمع معرف باللام.
2
Check literal possibility
Determine whether the context allows interpreting the term as ʿahd (specific reference) or istighrāq (all-inclusiveness). These are the literal meanings.
If the context does not force a specific reference, istighrāq is the default.
3
Apply the hierarchy
If a literal meaning is possible, maintain it. Only when literal meaning is impossible (mutaʿadhdhir) shift to the metaphorical genus (jins).
The principle: الحقيقة لا تترك إلا عند التعذر.
4
Analyze the example
Examine how the rule applies: In 'لا تدركه الأبصار', scholars took 'الأبصار' as istighrāq (all sights), negating that any sight can comprehend Him. They did not shift to genus because literal meaning was possible.
The negation is of generality (salb al-ʿumūm), not general negation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعلم من هذه الابحاث: يہاں سے مائن يہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ ان ابحاث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جمع معرف باللام کو مجازاً جنس پر اس وقت محمول کیا جائے گا جب اس کو عہد یا استغراق پر محمول کرنا ممکن نہ ہو کیونکہ ضابطہ ہے کہ حقیقت کو اس وقت ترک کیا جا سکتا ہے جب حقیقی معنی مراد لینا متعذر ہو۔ اگر عہد یا استغراق پر محمول کرنا ممکن ہو تو پھر اس کو اپنے حقیقی معنی یعنی استغراق وغیرہ پر محمول کیا جائے گا نہ کہ جنس پر جیسے لا تدركہ الابصار يہاں علماء نے فرمایا ہے کہ يفي سلب عموم کیلئے ہے یعنی عموم کا ہی سلب کیا گیا ہے عموم سلب کیلئے نہیں یعنی نفی کو عام نہیں کیا گیا کہ بعض سے ہو یا تمام سے۔ تو يہاں انہوں نے الف لام کو استغراق پر محمول کیا ہے۔
From these investigations it is learned that the definite plural with ال is metaphorically carried on genus only when it is impossible to carry it on specific reference (ʿahd) or all-inclusiveness (istighrāq). Because the rule is that the literal meaning is only abandoned when the literal meaning is impossible to intend. If it is possible to carry it on ʿahd or istighrāq, then it will be carried on its literal meaning, i.e., istighrāq etc., not on genus, like (the verse) 'لا تدركه الأبصار' – here the scholars have said that it is for negation of generality, meaning that generality alone is negated, not that the negation is made general (i.e., it does not mean negation for some or all). So here they carried the ال on istighrāq.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This is a ruling passage from a Hanafi usul commentary. The author explains that when the definite plural (جمع معرف باللام) is used, its default literal meanings are first ʿahd (specific reference), then istighrāq (all-inclusiveness). Only when both are impossible does it slip to a metaphorical meaning (majāz) of genus (jins). The example given is the Quranic verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' (Vision comprehends Him not), which scholars interpret as negating generality (salb al-ʿumūm) rather than making the negation general. Here the ال on 'الأبصار' is taken as istighrāq, i.e., all sights, not a specific sight. The passage emphasizes that moving from literal to metaphorical is only permissible when the literal is impossible (mutaʿadhdhir).

Key Terms
جمع معرف باللام (jamʿ muʿarraf bi-al-lām): A plural noun defined with the definite article al- (ال)
مجاز (majāz): Metaphorical usage
جنس (jins): Genus; here refers to the metaphorical meaning when the definite plural is taken as indicating the whole kind or species.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is جمع معرف باللام interpreted metaphorically for genus?
A) When it is used in a negative context
B) When literal interpretation as ʿahd or istighrāq is impossible
C) When it is indefinite
D) When it is in a conditional sentence

Key Takeaway
The definite plural is literal (istighrāq/ʿahd) unless impossible; only then is it metaphorical genus.
