Definite Plural Without ال: Generality via Idafa
Expands the ruling on general plurals to include those defined by idafa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that any definite plural, whether with al- or through idafa, is general (amm) so long as exception from it is valid.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a plural noun defined by idafa is general and allows valid exception.

In the previous lesson, we learned that plural nouns defined with the definite article ال are general. Now we extend that principle: any definite plural—whether by ال or by idafa (construct phrase)—is also considered عام. The key evidence is that exception (استثناء) from it is valid, which would be impossible if it were not general.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of definite plural
Look at the example 'عبيدي أحرار'. Recognize that 'عبيدي' is a plural noun made definite by idafa (construct phrase), not by the definite article ال.
The definiteness comes from the annexation to the following noun.
2
Apply the Hanafi criterion for generality
In Hanafi usul, a term is considered general (amm) if valid exception (istithna) can be made from it. Check whether you can say 'عبيدي أحرار except for some' and still have a meaningful statement.
The author explicitly states that exception is valid, proving generality.
3
Conclude the ruling
Since exception is valid from this plural, it is general. Therefore, in legal interpretation, it covers all its individuals unless an exception is specified.
This applies to any definite plural, regardless of the method of definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجمع المعرف بغير اللام :۔ پہلے تو ا جمع کا حکم بیان کیا جو عرف باللام ہو اب اس جمع کا حکم بیان فرمارہے ہیں جو معرف تو ہو لیکن معرف باللام نہ ہو معرف بغير اللام ہو جیسے عبیدی احرار " يہاں عبیدی جمع ہے اور معرف باضافت ہے معرف بالسلام نہیں ہے۔ تو اس کا حکم يہ ہے کہ يہ بھی عام ہوتا ہے اور اس کی وجہ يہی ہے کہ اس سے استثناء کرنا درست ہوتا ہے حالانکہ اگر يہ عام نہ ہوتا تو اس سے استثناء کرنا درست نہ ہوتا۔
And the plural defined without ال: First the ruling of the plural that is defined with ال was explained; now the ruling of the plural that is defined but not with ال, rather defined without ال, like 'عبيدي أحرار' (slaves of freemen). Here 'عبيدي' is plural and defined by idafa (annexation), not defined with ال. Its ruling is that it is also general, and the reason is that exception from it is valid, whereas if it were not general, exception from it would not be valid.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling on general plural nouns. In Hanafi usul, a plural noun that is made definite by any means — not just the definite article ال — is considered عام (general) as long as it allows valid exception (istithnāʾ). The example given is 'عبيدي أحرار' (slaves of freemen), where 'عبيدي' is a plural in the construct state (idāfa). The fact that one can say 'except for some' indicates it is general. This is a core principle in Hanafi legal theory for identifying general terms.

Key Terms
جمع معرف بغير اللام (jamʿ muʿarraf bi-ghayr al-lām): A plural noun made definite by means other than al-, such as idafa (construct phrase)

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Exception (استثناء) from it is valid
C) It is preceded by a negative
D) The majority of scholars say so

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a definite plural is general regardless of the method of definition, as long as valid exception is possible.

Is Indefinite Plural General? The Hanafi Dispute
Presents the ikhtilaf on whether indefinite plural is general, with proofs and rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on whether indefinite plural is a general term, evaluate the Quranic evidence cited by opponents, and apply the rebuttal based on grammatical analysis.

Core Idea
Indefinite plural is not general: it distributes per individual like indefinite singular.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, one of the key disputes is whether an indefinite plural noun (جمع منكر) is a general term (عام) that covers all instances. This dispute directly affects how legal texts are interpreted: if indefinite plural is general, a ruling based on it applies to every member; if not, additional evidence is needed. This lesson unpacks the two positions and the critical rebuttal involving a Qur'anic verse.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the ikhtilaf: some scholars hold indefinite plural is general, others (majority) say it is not. Understand what each position claims about scope.
The majority view is the relied-upon position in Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze the majority's reasoning
Examine the analogy: indefinite plural (رجال) is used distributively like indefinite singular (رجل) – each individual is addressed separately, not the group as a whole.
3
Examine the opponent's evidence
Read the Quranic verse (21:22) and see how they use exception (istithnāʾ) from an indefinite plural to argue generality.
The verse: 'لو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله لفسدتا'.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal
Understand the grammatical counter-argument: the 'إلا' here is not a true exception; 'لا' is in the meaning of 'غير' (other than), so the verse does not prove generality.
This rebuttal relies on Arabic grammar (nahw).
5
Apply the dispute to a legal interpretation
Consider how this ruling affects the interpretation of texts using indefinite plurals, e.g., in inheritance or commercial contracts.
Knowing this helps avoid over-generalisation in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف في الجمع المنكر :۔ يہاں سے ماتن مجمع منکر کا حکم بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ جمع منکر کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ اکثر حضرات فرماتے ہیں کہ يہ عام نہیں ہوتا اور دلیل يہ دیتے ہیں کہ استعمالات میں رجال کا اطلاق رجل کی طرح ہوتا ہے کہ جس طرح وہ علی سبیل البدلیت تمام افراد پر بولا جاتا ہے اور اس میں استغراق نہیں پایا جاتا اسی طرح رجال کا اطلاق بھی علی سبیل البديليت تمام افراد پر ہوتا ہے اس میں بھی استغراق اور شمول نہیں ہوتا اور بعض حضرات فرماتے ہیں کہ يہ عام ہوتا ہے اور اس کی دلیل يہ دیتے ہیں کہ اس سے استثناء کرنا درست ہے۔ جیسا کہ قرآن پاک میں ہے ”لو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله لفسدتا (يہاں آیت مکمل ہونی چاہیے) يہاں آلهة جمع منکر ہے اور اس سے إلا الله کا استثناء کیا گیا ہے۔ اگر آلهة عام نہ ہوتا تو يہ استثناء درست نہ ہوتا ۔ تو معلوم ہوا کہ جمع منکر عام ہوتا ہے لیکن اکثر حضرات جو اس کے عموم کے قائل نہیں وہ جواب دیتے ہیں کہ نحویوں کے نزدیک إلا لله استثناء نہیں ہے بلکہ لا يہاں پر غير کے معنی میں ہے لھذا يہ استدلال درست نہیں ہے۔
And there is difference of opinion about the indefinite plural. Here the author states the ruling on indefinite plural: there is ikhtilāf about it. Most scholars say it is not general, and they give as evidence that in usage, 'رجال' (men) is applied like 'رجل' (a man) — just as the latter is uttered for all individuals on a distributive basis and does not contain inclusiveness, similarly 'رجال' is uttered for all individuals on a distributive basis without inclusiveness or comprehensiveness. And some scholars say it is general, and their evidence is that exception from it is valid, as in the Holy Qur'an: 'لو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله لفسدتا' (If there were in them gods except Allah, they would both be corrupted). Here 'آلهة' is an indefinite plural and exception is made from it with 'إلا الله'. If it were not general, this exception would not be valid. So it is learned that indefinite plural is general. But most scholars who do not hold it to be general respond that according to grammarians, 'إلا الله' here is not an exception; rather, 'لا' here is in the meaning of 'غير' (other than), so this evidence is not valid.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This is a dispute passage from a Hanafi usul work covering a key ikhtilāf: whether the indefinite plural (جمع منكر) is a general term (عام) or not. The majority view (اکثر حضرات) holds it is not general, reasoning that indefinite plurals function distributively like indefinite singulars — they apply individually to each member without implying collective inclusiveness. The minority view relies on the validity of exception (istithnāʾ) from indefinite plurals, citing the Qur'anic verse 21:22 'لو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله' where 'آلهة' is indefinite plural and an exception is made. The majority responds by pointing out that grammarians consider the 'إلا' in this verse not a true exception but 'لا' in the sense of 'غير', thereby refuting the proof. This dispute has practical implications for legal interpretation: if indefinite plural is not general, then a ruling based on it does not cover all individuals unless additional evidence is found.

Key Terms
جمع منكر (jamʿ munkar): An indefinite plural noun (without definite article or idafa)
استغراق (istighrāq): All-inclusiveness, comprehensiveness

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority view in this text, why is indefinite plural not general?
A) It cannot take exception
B) It is used distributively like an indefinite singular
C) It is always definite
D) It is not found in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Indefinite plural is not general in Hanafi usul; its distributive nature and the grammatical rebuttal to the exception argument solidify the majority position.

The Definite Singular with ال as a Form of General
Lists the definite singular with ال as a type of general term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definite singular with ال as a type of general term (عام) and determine its meaning based on the Hanafi hierarchy of ال: ʿahd, istighrāq, taʿrīf al-māhiyya.

Core Idea
The definite article ال is inherently general unless a contextual indicator (qarīna) shows it defines the essence (māhiyya).

In Hanafi usul, the definite singular noun (مفرد محلى باللام) is one of the key forms of general terms (عام). However, its generality depends on the purpose of the definite article ال. This passage establishes a default hierarchy for ال: first for a specific referent (ʿahd), then for all-inclusiveness (istighrāq), and finally for defining the essence (taʿrīf al-māhiyya). Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly interpreting legal texts that use definite singulars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic form
Recognize a مفرد محلى باللام: a singular noun with the definite article ال. Not all such nouns are automatically general; their meaning depends on context.
2
Recall the default hierarchy
The Hanafi rule states that the default use of ال is 1) ʿahd (specific reference), 2) istighrāq (all-inclusiveness), 3) taʿrīf al-māhiyya (definition of essence). The first is not general; the second is general; the third requires a qarīna to become non-general.
Memorize this order: ʿahd > istighrāq > māhiyya.
3
Apply to Quranic examples
In 'إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ' and 'وَالسَّارِقُ', the ال is for istighrāq (general) because there is no previous specific reference and no qarīna for māhiyya. The exceptions in the verses confirm the generality.
The exception clause 'إِلَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا' shows that الْإِنْسَانَ covers all humans initially.
4
Identify the exception for māhiyya
When a qarīna indicates definition of essence (e.g., everyday speech like 'أكلت الخبز'), the ال is not general; it refers to the kind or nature of bread.
The qarīna can be the verb or the context of a specific action.
5
Understand the need for qarīna
The default is generality (istighrāq) after ʿahd is ruled out. To shift to māhiyya, a clear contextual indicator is required. This protects the general application of legal texts.
Without a qarīna, a definite singular in a legal ruling is binding on all instances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا أَى مِنْ الْفَاظِ الْعَامِ الْمُفْرَدُ الْمُحَلَّى بِاللَّامِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنُ لِلْمَعُهُودِ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ( إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَفِي خُسْرٍ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا) وقَوْله تَعَالَى ( وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ) إِلَّا أَنْ تَدُلُّ الْقَرِينَةُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لِتَعْرِيفِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ نَحْوُ أَكَلْتَ الْخُبْزَ ، وَشَرِبُت الْمَاءَ ) ، وَإِنَّمَا يَحْتَاجُ تَعْرِيفُ الْمَاهِيَّةِ إِلَى الْقَرِينَةِ لِمَا ذَكَرُنَا أَنَّ الْأَصْلَ فِى اللَّامِ الْعَهْدُ ثُمَّ الاسْتِغْرَاقُ ثُمَّ تَعْرِيفُ الْمَاهِيَّةِ .
ترجمہ:۔ (اور ان میں سے ) یعنی الفاظ عام میں سے (وہ مفرد ہے جو معرف باللام ہو جب کہ نہ ہو وہ معہود کیلئے جیسا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول ہے إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَفِي خُسْرٍ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا اور اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول ہے السارق و السارقتہ مگر یہ کہ دلالت کرے قرینہ اس بات پر کہ بیشک وہ ماہیت کی تعریف کے لیے ہے جیسے اکلت الخبز اور شربت الماء ) اور جز این نیست کہ احتیاجی ہوتی ہے ماہیت کی تعریف میں قرینہ کی طرف بوجہ اس کے جو ہم نے ذکر کیا کہ لام میں اصل عہد ہے۔ پھر استغراق ہے پھر ماهیت کی تعریف ہے
And among them — i.e., among the words of general — is the singular noun that is defined with the definite article al- (ال) when it is not for a specific referent (ʿahd), like Allah's statement: 'إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَفِي خُسْرٍ' (Indeed, mankind is in loss), except those who believe; and His statement: 'وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ' (The thief, male and female), unless a contextual indicator (qarīna) shows that it is for definition of the essence (taʿrīf al-māhiyya), like 'أكلت الخبز' (I ate bread) and 'شربت الماء' (I drank water). And the definition of the essence only needs a qarīna because of what we mentioned: the default for al- is ʿahd, then istighrāq, then taʿrīf al-māhiyya.
Translation: And among them, i.e., among the words of general, is the singular that is defined with ال when it is not for the specific referent, like Allah's saying 'إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَفِي خُسْرٍ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا' and His saying 'السارق و السارقة' unless a qarīna indicates that it is for definition of the essence, like 'أكلت الخبز' and 'شربت الماء'. And it is not but that the definition of the essence needs a qarīna because of what we mentioned that the default in ال is ʿahd, then istighrāq, then definition of the essence.
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage defines another category of general terms (ألفاظ العام) in Hanafi usul: the definite singular (مفرد محلى باللام). It is general when not used for a specific previously mentioned referent (العهد). The default hierarchy for the definite article ال is: first, ʿahd (specific reference); second, istighrāq (all-inclusiveness); third, taʿrīf al-māhiyya (defining the essence/genus). The last requires a contextual indicator (qarīna) to move from the literal general meaning. Examples: 'إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ' in the Quran is general for all mankind (istighrāq) as indicated by the exception; 'وَالسَّارِقُ' is general for all thieves. But in 'أكلت الخبز' (I ate bread), the qarīna shows it is about the essence (bread in general), not all bread. This principle is crucial for interpreting legal texts that use definite singulars.

Key Terms
مفرد محلى باللام (mufrad muḥallā bi-al-lām): A singular noun defined with the definite article ال, used as a general term when not for ʿahd.
تعريف الماهية (taʿrīf al-māhiyya): Definition of the essence/genus, i.e., using ال to indicate the kind or nature, not all individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default order of meanings of the definite article ال according to this passage?
A) Istighrāq, then ʿahd, then māhiyya
B) ʿAhd, then istighrāq, then māhiyya
C) Māhiyya, then ʿahd, then istighrāq
D) Istighrāq, then māhiyya, then ʿahd

Key Takeaway
The definite singular with ال is a form of general term (عام) unless a contextual indicator diverts it to definition of the essence (taʿrīf al-māhiyya), following the Hanafi hierarchy: ʿahd, then istighrāq, then māhiyya.

The Indefinite in Negative Context as 'Amm
Explaining the indefinite noun in a negative context as a type of 'amm with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an indefinite noun in a negative context as a general term and apply the Hanafi principle that it indicates complete negation (salb kulli).

Core Idea
An indefinite noun in a negative context makes the negation universal, covering all individuals of that kind.

In Hanafi usul, one of the recognized categories of general terms ('amm) is the indefinite noun occurring in the scope of negation. This lesson unpacks that definition, grounding it in a Quranic proof that demonstrates why such a construction yields complete negation (salb kulli). By examining the disbelievers' statement 'ما أنزل الله على بشر من شيء' and Allah's response, we see the logical necessity of interpreting the indefinite in a negative context as universal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Term and Its Context
Locate the indefinite noun (nakirah) in a negative sentence. In the Quranic example, the phrase 'ما أنزل الله على بشر من شيء' contains the indefinite nouns 'بشر' (human) and 'شيء' (thing) after the negation 'ما'.
The indefinite noun must be in the scope of the negation.
2
State the Hanafi Claim
The Hanafi school holds that an indefinite in a negative context indicates complete negation (salb kulli), meaning the negation applies to every individual of that noun without exception.
This is a fundamental principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
3
Analyze the Dalil
The proof is the Qur'anic dialogue: the disbelievers said 'ما أنزل الله على بشر من شيء' and Allah responded 'قل من أنزل الكتاب الذي جاء به موسى'. The response only refutes them if their statement is a universal negative. If it were partial, the particular affirmation would not contradict it.
The wajh al-dalalah is the necessity of the refutation.
4
Derive the Linguistic Principle
From this proof, the usuli principle is derived: an indefinite noun in the scope of negation produces a general term ('amm) that indicates comprehensive negation.
This applies whether the negation is explicit (e.g., 'ما', 'لا') or implied contextually.
5
Apply the Principle
Recognize that any similar construction in the Qur'an or Sunnah should be interpreted as general unless a specific exception (takhsis) is proven. For example, 'لا إله إلا الله' where 'إله' is indefinite in a negative context, meaning 'no deity at all except Allah'.
Practice identifying such constructions in primary texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا النَّكِرَةُ فِى مَوْضِعِ النَّفْيِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ( قُلْ مَنْ أَنْزَلَ الْكِتَابَ الَّذِي جَاءَ بِهِ مُوسَى ) فِي جَوَابِ ( مَا أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ عَلَى بَشَرٍ مِنْ شَيْءٍ ) ( وَجُهُ التَّمَسُّكِ أَنَّهُمْ قَالُوا ) مَا أَنزَلَ اللَّهُ عَلَى بَشَرٍ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَلَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مِثْلُ هَذَا الْكَلَامِ لِلسَّلْبِ الْكُلّى لَمْ يَسْتَقِمُ فِى الرَّدْ عَلَيْهِمُ الْإِيجَابُ الْجُزْنِيُّ ، وَهُوَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ( قُلْ مَنْ أَنْزَلَ الْكِتَابَ الَّذِى جَاءَ بِهِ مُوسَى ) (وَلِكَلِمَةِ التَّوْحِيدِ).
ان میں سے وہ نکرہ ہے جو تحت ابھی ہو جیسے اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول " قل من انزل الكتاب الذي جاء بہ موسیٰ ما انزل اللہ علی بشر من شیء کے جواب میں ) استدلال کا طریق یہ ہے کہ بیشک انہوں نے کہا کہ نہیں نازل کی اللہ نے کسی بشر پر کوئی شے ۔ پس اگر نہ ہو اس کلام کی مثل سلب کلی کیلئے تو نہیں نام ہوگا ان پر رد کرنے میں ایجاب جزئی اور وہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے " قل من انزل الكتاب الذي جاء بہ موسیٰ ( اور کلمہ توحید کی وجہ سے )۔
And among them is the indefinite in the position of negation, due to His saying (Qul man anzala al-kitaba alladhi jaa bihi Musa) in response to (Ma anzala Allahu ala basharin min shay'). The way of holding on (to the proof) is that they said: 'Allah did not send down upon any human any thing at all.' So if this speech were not for complete negation, then the particular affirmation in response to them would not be proper, and that is His saying: 'Say: Who sent down the Book that Moses brought?' and because of the word of Tawhid.
Among them is the indefinite that is under negation, like Allah's statement: 'Say: Who sent down the Book that Moses brought?' in response to 'Allah did not send down upon any human any thing.' The method of argument is that indeed they said: 'Allah did not send down upon any human any thing.' So if this speech were not for complete negation, then the partial affirmation in replying to them would not be proper, and that is Allah's command: 'Say: Who sent down the Book that Moses brought?' and because of the word of Tawhid.
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage defines the second type of general terms: the indefinite noun in the context of negation (al-nakirah fi mawdi' al-nafi). The author provides a Quranic proof from the dialogue of the disbelievers who said 'Ma anzala Allahu ala basharin min shay'' (Allah did not send down anything upon any human), which is a complete negation (salb kulli). The response from Allah is 'Qul man anzala al-kitaba alladhi jaa bihi Musa' (Say: Who sent down the Book that Moses brought?), which is a particular affirmation (ijab juz'i) and only refutes them if the original statement is understood as a universal negative. If their negation were not universal, their statement would not be false because a particular affirmation would not contradict a partial negation. Thus, the indefinite 'min shay'' in the negative context implies absolute negation, making it general. The Urdu summary reiterates this reasoning: the indefinite in a negative sentence serves as a general term for complete negation.

Key Terms
النكرة في موضع النفي (al-nakirah fi mawdi' al-nafi): An indefinite noun appearing in a negative sentence, which makes the negation general over all individuals of that noun.
سلب كلي (salb kulli): Complete negation, meaning the negation applies to every individual of the kind without exception.
إيجاب جزئي (ijab juz'i): Particular affirmation, affirming something for some individuals only.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author conclude that 'ما أنزل الله على بشر من شيء' is a complete negation (salb kulli)?
A) Because the word 'بشر' is indefinite and in a negative context.
B) Because the response 'قل من أنزل الكتاب' would not refute them unless their negation was universal.
C) Because the definite article 'ال' appears in the response.
D) Because the word 'شيء' is indefinite and implies comprehensiveness.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, an indefinite noun in a negative context is a general term that indicates complete negation (salb kulli), as proven by the Quranic dialogical necessity.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Definite Article on a Singular Noun as a General Term
Defining al-mufrad al-muhalla bi al-lam as a type of 'amm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a singular noun with 'al-' is a general term (amm) in Hanafi usul, analyze the Quranic evidence for generality, and recognize when a qarinah shifts the meaning to ta'rif al-mahiyyah.

Core Idea
A singular noun with 'al-' is general by default (istighraq) unless context shows it is for 'ahd or essence.

This passage introduces one of the key categories of general terms (alfaz al-'amm) in Hanafi usul: the singular noun made definite with 'al-'. The author explains that such a noun indicates generality (istighraq) provided it is not used for a previously known referent (ma'hood). He provides Quranic examples to prove that the 'al-' can be general, and then discusses contextual indicators (qarinah) that can change its meaning to definition of the essence (ta'rif al-mahiyyah). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly deriving legal rulings from revealed texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that 'al-mufrad al-muhalla bi al-lam' is one type of general term (amm) in Hanafi usul, distinct from plural forms.
The term is a singular noun with the definite article 'al-'.
2
Check the default ruling
When 'al-' is not for a known entity (ma'hood), the default meaning is comprehensiveness (istighraq) covering all individuals of the kind.
This default is based on the hierarchy: 'ahd > istighraq > mahiyyah.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The exception (istithna') in verses like 'إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَفِي خُسْرٍ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا' proves generality because exception can only be taken from an inclusive term.
The same applies to 'وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ' where the legal ruling presupposes individual thieves.
4
Apply the exception
If a contextual indicator (qarinah) shows that 'al-' is for defining the essence (ta'rif al-mahiyyah), the term is not general, e.g., 'akaltu al-khubza' where eating cannot encompass all bread.
The qarinah overrides the default istighraq, shifting to essence/genus meaning.
5
Order of priority
Memorize the hierarchy: first 'ahd (known), then istighraq (comprehensiveness), then ta'rif al-mahiyyah (essence). A qarinah is required for the last two to deviate from the previous default.
This hierarchy governs the interpretation of 'al-' in legal texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ:۔ (اور ان میں سے ) یعنی الفاظ عام میں سے (وہ مفرد ہے جو معرف با الام ہو جب کہ نہ ہو وہ معہود کیلئے جیسا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول ہے إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَفِي خُسْرٍ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا اور اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول ہے السارق و السارقتہ مگر یہ کہ دلالت کرے قرینہ اس بات پر کہ بیشک وہ ماہیت کی تعریف کے لیے ہے جیسے اکلت الکشمیز اور شربت الماء ) اور جز این نیست کہ احتیاجی ہوتی ہے ماہیت کی تعریف میں قرینہ کی طرف بوجہ اس کے جو ہم نے ذکر کیا کہ لام میں اصل عہد ہے۔ پھر استغراق ہے پھر ماهیت کی تعریف ہے
تشریح : ومنها المفرد اعلی اسلام نام کے الفاظ میں سے ایک لفظ مفرد ہے جو عرف بالالام ہو لیکن اس وقت کہ جب وہ معہود نہ ہو۔ اگر وہ معہود ہوا تو پھر وہ عام نہیں ہو گا اور اس کی تفصیل جمع معرف باسلام میں گزر چکی ہے۔ جیسا کہ قرآن پاک میں ہے " ان الانسان لفی خسر" یہاں انسان مفرد ہے اور اس پر الف لام استغراق کا ہے کیونکہ الا الذین امنوا سے اس سے استثناء کیا گیا ہے اور استثناء بھی درست ہو سکتا ہے جب الف لام استغراق کا ہو۔ ای طرح ارشاد باری تعالیٰ ہے والسارق و السارقہ الآیۃ ۔ یہاں کوئی خاص چور مراد ہے نہیں کیونکہ معہود نہیں ہے اور نہ ہی جنس چور مراد ہے کیونکہ جنس کا ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا بلکہ فرد کا ہاتھ کاٹا جاتا ہے اس لیے یہ لام استغراق کا ہے اور السارق والسارقہ عام ہیں۔ اس لیے ہم نے کہا کہ جب الف لام مفرد پر داخل ہو اور وہ معہود نہ ہو تو وہ استغراق پر محمول ہوگا۔ فائدہ:۔ مصنف نے دو مثالیں دے کر اس طرف اشارہ کیا ہے کہ مفرد پر الف لام تعریف کا حرفی ہوگا ۔ جیسے ان الانسان میں ہے یا اسی ہوگا جیسے السارق والسارقہ میں بمعنی الذی ہے۔ اور الف لام حرف ہو یا اسی عام ہونے میں برابر ہے۔ وجود قرینہ کے وقت مفرد میں الف کے مدلول سے ماہیت مراد ہوتی ہے
الا ان تدل القرینہ: الف لام معہود نہ ہونے کی صورت میں استغراق پر محمول ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر کوئی قرینہ اس بات پر پایا جائے کہ یہاں الف لام کے مدخول سے ماھیت مراد ہے تو پھر ماهیت مراد لے لی جاتی ہے۔ اور پھر بعض دفعہ تو ماهیت من حیث الماهیت مراد ہوتی ہے اور بعض دفعہ اہمیت اپنے افراد میں سے کسی فرد کے ضمن میں مراد ہوتی ہے اول کی مثال الانسان حیوان ناطق ہے۔ یہاں الف لام ماھیت کیلئے ہے اور انسان کی ماہیت من حیث الماهیت حیوان ناطق ہے۔ ثانی کی مثال اکلت الخبز اور شربت المساء ہے یہاں الحمز اور الماء پر الف لام عبد کا نہیں ہے معبود نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور استغراق کا بھی نہیں ہے بلکہ جنس کا ہے اور اس پر قرینہ اکل اور شرب ہیں کہ ایک آدمی دنیا کی تمام روٹیوں کو نہیں کھا سکتا اور نہ ہی دنیا کا تمام پانی پی سکتا ہے تو یہاں اس قرینے کی وجہ سے اس کو جنس پر محمول کیا جائے گا اور یہ جنس کسی نہ کسی فرد کے ضمن میں پائی جائے گی ۔ لھذا اس کلام کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ میں نے روٹی کا کوئی فرد کھایا ہے اور پانی کا کوئی فرد پیا ہے۔
فائدہ:۔ ماحیت کو مراد لینے کے وقت ہم نے قرینے کا ذکر اس لیے کیا کہ یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے کہ الف لام میں اصل عبد ہے اس کے بعد دوسرا درجہ استغراق کا ہے اور اس کے بعد جنس کا درجہ ہے تو جب جنس تیسرے نمبر پر ہے تو یہ خلاف اصل ہوا اور
And among them (i.e., the expressions of generality) is the singular noun adorned with 'al-' when it is not for the known (al-ma'had), like His saying: 'Indeed, mankind is in loss, except those who believe...' and His saying: 'The thief, male and female...' unless the context indicates that it is for the definition of the essence, like 'you ate the bread' and 'you drank the water'. And the definition of the essence indeed needs a contextual indicator because of what we mentioned: that the original use of 'lam' is for the known, then for comprehensiveness, then for definition of the essence. Translation: Among them, i.e., among the expressions of generality, is the singular noun that is made definite with 'al-' when it is not for the known, like Allah's statement: 'Indeed, mankind is in loss, except those who believe...' and Allah's statement: 'The thief, male and female...' unless a contextual indicator shows that it is for the definition of the essence, like 'you ate the bread' and 'you drank the water'. And it is not but that there is a need for the definition of the essence to have a contextual indicator because of what we mentioned: that the original in 'lam' is the known, then comprehensiveness, then definition of the essence. Elucidation: And among them, i.e., from the words of generality, one word is the singular that is made definite with 'al-' but only when it is not for the known. If it is for the known, then it is not general, and its detail has already passed in the discussion of the definite plural. As in the Holy Qur'an: 'Indeed, mankind is in loss.' Here 'mankind' is singular and the 'al' is for comprehensiveness, because 'except those who believe' makes an exception from it, and an exception is valid only when the 'al' is for comprehensiveness. Similarly, Allah's command: 'The thief, male and female...' Here no specific thief is intended because it is not known, nor is the genus of thief intended because the hand of the genus is not cut; rather, the hand of the individual is cut, so this 'al' is for comprehensiveness, and 'al-sariq' and 'al-sariqah' are general. Therefore we said: when 'al' enters a singular noun and it is not for the known, then it is taken as indicating comprehensiveness. Benefit: The author has pointed out with two examples that the 'al' on the singular may be a particle of definition, as in 'inna al-insana', or a relative pronoun, as in 'al-sariq' and 'al-sariqah' meaning 'the one who steals'. And whether 'al' is a particle or a relative pronoun, it is equal in being general. When a context exists, the meaning of the singular with 'al' is intended as the essence. 'Unless a context indicates': When 'al' is not for the known, it is taken as indicating comprehensiveness. Yes, if a context exists that indicates that the intended meaning of the word with 'al' is the essence, then the essence is taken. And sometimes the essence in itself is intended, and sometimes it is intended within the scope of some of its individuals. The first example is 'al-insanu hayawanun natiq' (Man is a rational animal). Here 'al' is for the essence, and the essence of man per se is 'rational animal'. The second example is 'akaltu al-khubza' and 'sharibtu al-ma'a'. Here 'al' on 'al-khubz' and 'al-ma' is not for the known because it is not known, nor for comprehensiveness, but for the genus, and the context of eating and drinking indicates that one person cannot eat all the bread of the world nor drink all the water of the world, so due to this context it is taken as genus, and this genus is found within some individual. Therefore the meaning of this speech is: I ate an individual of bread and drank an individual of water. Benefit: In taking the essence as intended, we mentioned the context because it has preceded that the original in 'al' is the known, then second degree is comprehensiveness, then third is genus; so since genus is third, it is against the original.
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage defines the first of two types of general terms (alfaz al-'amm) covered here: the singular noun made definite with 'al-'. The author states that such a noun is general provided it is not used for a previously known/present entity (ma'hood). Proofs are given from the Qur'an: 'Indeed, mankind is in loss' (Surah al-'Asr) and 'The male thief and the female thief' (Surah al-Ma'idah). In both verses, 'al-' indicates comprehensiveness (istighraq) because the exception (istithna') that follows is only valid if the term includes all individuals. The passage then discusses an exception: if a contextual indicator (qarinah) shows that 'al-' is for defining the essence (ta'rif al-mahiyyah) rather than comprehensiveness, then it is not general. Examples are given: 'akalta al-khubz' (you ate bread) – clearly not all bread, and 'sharibta al-maa' (you drank water) – clearly not all water. The author explains the order of priority for the meaning of 'al-': first is ma'hood (previously known), second is istighraq (comprehensiveness), third is ta'rif al-mahiyyah (definition of essence). The Urdu commentary elaborates with examples and clarifies that 'al-' might be a particle (harf) or a relative pronoun (ism mawsool) but in either case it is general. It also provides a detailed discussion of when essence is intended per se (like 'man is a rational animal') versus when essence is intended within an individual (like eating bread). The benefit (fa'idah) at the end re-emphasizes that the use of genus (jins) is the third rank, contrary to the original, so a qarinah is needed.

Key Terms
المفرد المحلى باللام (al-mufrad al-muhalla bi al-lam): A singular noun that has the definite article 'al-' attached to it.
المعهود (al-ma'hood): The known or previously mentioned entity that the definite article refers to specifically.
الاستغراق (al-istighraq): Comprehensiveness, meaning the term includes all individuals of its kind without exception.
تعريف الماهية (ta'rif al-mahiyyah): Defining the essence or nature of the thing, not the individuals.
القرينة (al-qarinah): A contextual indicator that determines the intended meaning of the definite article.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default meaning of 'al-' on a singular noun according to the author, when there is no qarinah for 'ahd or mahiyyah?
A) It indicates the known (ma'hood).
B) It indicates comprehensiveness (istighraq).
C) It indicates the essence (mahiyyah).
D) It is ambiguous and requires further analysis.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a singular noun with the definite article 'al-' is a general term by default, indicating comprehensiveness (istighraq), unless the context shows it is for a known entity (ma'hood) or for defining the essence (mahiyyah).

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Generality of alif lam on Singular Nouns: Istighraq, 'Ahd, and Jins
Explanation of the generality of the definite article on singular nouns

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three usages of alif lam on singular nouns (ahd, istighraq, jins) and determine which usage applies based on the presence or absence of a qarinah.

Core Idea
A singular noun with alif lam is general unless a contextual clue indicates genus or specific reference.

This passage from a classical usul text explains the interpretive rule for singular nouns defined with 'al'. While the default is generality (istighraq) when no specific referent is known, the presence of a qarinah can indicate that the alif lam means genus (jins) or even a specific individual. Understanding this rule is crucial for correctly deriving rulings from Quranic and Hadith texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the noun and its article
Find the singular noun with alif lam in the text.
The noun may be a common noun like 'insan' or 'sariq'.
2
Determine if ma'hud (specific)
Check if the noun refers to a known specific instance from the context. If yes, it is for 'ahd and not general.
Ahd requires a previous mention or clear contextual identification.
3
Check for a qarinah indicating jins
Look for a contextual clue (qarinah) that makes the istighraq meaning impossible or unlikely. For example, 'akaltu al-khubz' cannot mean eating all bread.
A qarinah can shift the meaning from istighraq to jins (genus) or even 'ahd.
4
Apply the hierarchy of meanings
The default is istighraq. If the noun is not ma'hud and no qarinah indicates jins, it is interpreted as istighraq. If a qarinah points to jins, it is interpreted as jins (referring to an individual within the genus).
The hierarchy: 'ahd > istighraq > jins. Going against the default requires a qarinah.
5
Derive the legal meaning
Based on the identified usage, determine the ruling or implication. For example, 'al-sariq wa al-sariqah' (istighraq) means the ruling applies to all thieves.
The derived ruling must be consistent with the established usage.

مفرد معرف باللام عام ہوتا ہے
تشریح : ومنها المفرد اعلی اسلام نام کے الفاظ میں سے ایک لفظ مفرد ہے جو عرف بالالام ہو لیکن اس وقت کہ جب وہ معہود نہ ہو۔ اگر وہ معہود ہوا تو پھر وہ عام نہیں ہو گا اور اس کی تفصیل جمع معرف باسلام میں گزر چکی ہے۔ جیسا کہ قرآن پاک میں ہے " ان الانسان لفی خسر" یہاں انسان مفرد ہے اور اس پر الف لام استغراق کا ہے کیونکہ الا الذین امنوا سے اس سے استثناء کیا گیا ہے اور استثناء بھی درست ہو سکتا ہے جب الف لام استغراق کا ہو۔ ای طرح ارشاد باری تعالیٰ ہے والسارق و السارقہ الآیۃ ۔ یہاں کوئی خاص چور مراد ہے نہیں کیونکہ معہود نہیں ہے اور نہ ہی جنس چور مراد ہے کیونکہ جنس کا ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا بلکہ فرد کا ہاتھ کاٹا جاتا ہے اس لیے یہ لام استغراق کا ہے اور السارق والسارقہ عام ہیں۔ اس لیے ہم نے کہا کہ جب الف لام مفرد پر داخل ہو اور وہ معہود نہ ہو تو وہ استغراق پر محمول ہوگا۔ فائدہ:۔ مصنف نے دو مثالیں دے کر اس طرف اشارہ کیا ہے کہ مفرد پر الف لام تعریف کا حرفی ہوگا ۔ جیسے ان الانسان میں ہے یا اسی ہوگا جیسے السارق والسارقہ میں بمعنی الذی ہے۔ اور الف لام حرف ہو یا اسی عام ہونے میں برابر ہے۔ وجود قرینہ کے وقت مفرد میں الف کے مدلول سے ماہیت مراد ہوتی ہے
الا ان تدل القرینہ: الف لام معہود نہ ہونے کی صورت میں استغراق پر محمول ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر کوئی قرینہ اس بات پر پایا جائے کہ یہاں الف لام کے مدخول سے ماھیت مراد ہے تو پھر ماهیت مراد لے لی جاتی ہے۔ اور پھر بعض دفعہ تو ماهیت من حیث الماهیت مراد ہوتی ہے اور بعض دفعہ اہمیت اپنے افراد میں سے کسی فرد کے ضمن میں مراد ہوتی ہے اول کی مثال الانسان حیوان ناطق ہے۔ یہاں الف لام ماھیت کیلئے ہے اور انسان کی ماہیت من حیث الماهیت حیوان ناطق ہے۔ ثانی کی مثال اکلت الخبز اور شربت المساء ہے یہاں الحمز اور الماء پر الف لام عبد کا نہیں ہے معبود نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور استغراق کا بھی نہیں ہے بلکہ جنس کا ہے اور اس پر قرینہ اکل اور شرب ہیں کہ ایک آدمی دنیا کی تمام روٹیوں کو نہیں کھا سکتا اور نہ ہی دنیا کا تمام پانی پی سکتا ہے تو یہاں اس قرینے کی وجہ سے اس کو جنس پر محمول کیا جائے گا اور یہ جنس کسی نہ کسی فرد کے ضمن میں پائی جائے گی ۔ لھذا اس کلام کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ میں نے روٹی کا کوئی فرد کھایا ہے اور پانی کا کوئی فرد پیا ہے۔
فائدہ:۔ ماحیت کو مراد لینے کے وقت ہم نے قرینے کا ذکر اس لیے کیا کہ یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے کہ الف لام میں اصل عبد ہے اس کے بعد دوسرا درجہ استغراق کا ہے اور اس کے بعد جنس کا درجہ ہے تو جب جنس تیسرے نمبر پر ہے تو یہ خلاف اصل ہوا اور جو معنی خلاف اصل ہو وہ مجاز ہوتا ہے اور مجازی معنی مراد لینے کیلئے قرینہ کی ضرورت ہوتی ہے۔
A singular noun defined with alif lam is general. Explanation: And among them is the singular noun—it is a singular word from the words of Islam [i.e. Arabic] that is defined with alif lam, but only when it is not specific (ma'hud). If it is specific, then it will not be general, and its detail has passed in the discussion of the plural defined with alif lam. As in the Holy Quran: 'Indeed, mankind is in loss.' Here 'mankind' is singular and the alif lam is for istighraq because an exception is made from it with 'except those who believe'. And exception is valid only when the alif lam is for istighraq. Similarly, the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'The male thief and the female thief...' Here no particular thief is meant because it is not specific, nor is the genus of thief meant because the hand of a genus is not cut; rather, the hand of an individual is cut. Therefore, this lam is for istighraq, and 'the male thief' and 'the female thief' are general. Hence we said: when alif lam enters a singular and it is not specific, it is interpreted as istighraq. Benefit: The author has indicated by giving two examples that the alif lam on a singular is either the particle 'al' as in 'inna al-insana' or it is the relative pronoun meaning 'alladhi' as in 'al-sariq wa al-sariqah'. And whether the alif lam is a particle or a relative pronoun, it is equal in being general. In the presence of a qarinah, from the indicated meaning of the alif lam, the quiddity (mahiyyah) is meant. Except if the qarinah indicates: The alif lam when not specific is interpreted as istighraq. Yes, if a qarinah is found that here from the noun of the alif lam the quiddity is meant, then the quiddity is taken. And sometimes the quiddity in itself is meant, and sometimes it is meant within the context of an individual of its individuals. The example of the first: 'Man is a rational animal.' Here the alif lam is for the quiddity, and the quiddity of man in itself is a rational animal. The example of the second: 'I ate the bread and drank the water.' Here the alif lam on 'the bread' and 'the water' is not for 'ahd because it is not specific, nor for istighraq, but rather for genus. And the qarinah for that is eating and drinking, because a person cannot eat all the bread of the world nor drink all the water of the world. So here, due to the qarinah, it is interpreted as genus, and this genus is found within some individual. Therefore, the meaning of this speech is: I ate some individual of bread and drank some individual of water. Benefit: When taking the quiddity, we mentioned the qarinah because it has previously passed that the primary usage of alif lam is for 'ahd, then the second degree is istighraq, then the degree of genus. So when genus is in third place, it is against the original, and a meaning that is against the original is figurative, and to take a figurative meaning, a qarinah is needed.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the principle that a singular noun with the definite article 'al' indicates generality (istighraq) when it is not used for a specific referent (ma'hud). The author explains using Quranic examples: 'inna al-insana' (mankind) is general because it has an exception, and 'al-sariq wa al-sariqah' (the male thief and female thief) are general because the Islamic ruling of cutting the hand applies to individual thieves, not to the genus. The passage also clarifies that when a contextual indication (qarinah) shows that the alif lam is for genus (jins) rather than istighraq, such as in the examples 'akaltu al-khubz' (I ate the bread) and 'sharibtu al-ma' (I drank the water), the noun is interpreted as genus referring to some individual. The second benefit emphasizes that the default usage of alif lam is for 'ahd (specific reference), then istighraq, then genus, and taking a later meaning requires a qarinah because it is figurative (majaz).

Key Terms
مفرد معرف باللام (mufrad mu'arraf bi al-lam): A singular noun that has the definite article alif lam.
استغراق (istighraq): Generality covering all individuals of the noun.
معہود (ma'hud): Specific referent known from previous context.
قرینہ (qarinah): Contextual indication that determines the intended meaning.
جنس (jins): Genus, meaning the kind or type, not all individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is an example of 'alif lam' for istighraq on a singular noun?
A) اكلت الخبز (I ate the bread)
B) الانسان حیوان ناطق (Man is a rational animal)
C) السارق و السارقہ (The male thief and the female thief)
D) شربت المساء (I drank the water)

Key Takeaway
The default meaning of alif lam on a singular noun is generality (istighraq) unless a qarinah indicates a specific referent (ahd) or genus (jins).

Indefinite Noun Under Negation: Its Generality
Proofs that an indefinite noun under negation is general in Hanafi usul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that an indefinite noun under negation indicates generality, and justify it using the Quranic and tawhid proofs.

Core Idea
An indefinite noun under negation is general — it negates all individuals, not just one.

The Hanafi school holds that an indefinite noun (nakirah) in the scope of a negation particle becomes general, encompassing all individuals of that genus. This principle is foundational for understanding many Quranic and legal texts. This lesson explores two key proofs: one from the Quranic rebuttal of a Jewish claim, and one from the kalimat al-tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic principle
Recognize that an indefinite noun (nakirah) under negation (e.g., 'la', 'ma') is considered general in Hanafi usul. This means it negates all instances, not a specific one.
2
Examine the first proof: Quranic contradiction
Analyze Quran 6:91. The Jews said 'ما أنزل الله على بشر من شيء' (a universal negative). Allah's response 'قل من أنزل الكتاب الذي جاء به موسى' is a particular affirmative. In logic, a particular affirmative is the contradictory of a universal negative. Therefore, the Jewish statement must be universal, proving that 'بشر' and 'شيء' are general.
The use of logical contradiction (tanāquḍ) is key.
3
Analyze the second proof: kalimat al-tawhid
Consider 'لا إله إلا الله'. The indefinite 'إله' is under negation. To negate all false gods, 'إله' must be general; otherwise tawhid would not be fully negated.
This is a practical application in core Islamic creed.
4
Extend to conditional sentences
Note the rule for conditionals: if someone swears 'If I hit a man, then my slave is free', the oath is for prevention (yamin li al-man‘), meaning 'I do not hit a man'. The indefinite 'man' here is general on the side of negation, so he must not hit any man.
This shows the same principle applies in conditional oaths.

نكرة تحت الھی کا عموم
ومنها النكرة موضع ابھي لقولہ تعالٰی :۔ عام کے الفاظ میں سے وہ نکرہ بھی ہے جو تحت الھی واقع ہو کیونکہ نمرہ کی وضع فرد مہم کے لئے ہے اور فرد مہم کی نفی تمام افراد کے انتفاء سے ہو سکتی ہے اور اس نکرہ کے عام ہونے کی ایک دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ قرآن پاک میں ہے ۔ ما انزل اللہ علی بشر من شی یہ یہودیوں نے آپ کی نبوت کا انکار کرتے ہوئے کہا تھا کہ اللہ نے کسی بشر پر کوئی شے نازل نہیں کی۔ اس کے جواب میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرما یا قتل من انزل لكتاب الذي جاء به موسیٰ یہ آیت قضیه موجبه جزئیہ ہے اب ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہودیوں کے قول میں بشر اور شی نکرہ ہیں اور تحت الھی واقع ہیں لھذا یہ عام ہیں اس سے کوئی خاص بشر یا خاص شی سے مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ تمام بشروں اور اشیاء کو عام ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان کے قول کے جواب میں اللہ تعالیٰ کا جو فرمان من انزل الكتاب الذي جاء بہ موسیٰ یہ موجبہ جزئیہ ہے اس کو یہودیوں کے قول کی نقیض بنایا گیا ہے اور یہ بات واضح ہے کہ موجبہ جزیہ سالیہ کلیہ کی نقیض بنتا ہے سالیہ جزئیہ کی نقیض نہیں بنتا تو یہاں اللہ تعالیٰ کا فرمان اسی صورت میں یہودیوں کے قول کا جواب بن سکتا ہے کہ ان کے اس قول کو مالیہ کلیہ مانا جائے اور جب سالہ کلیہ مان لینگے تو آیت میں بشر اورشی کو عام ماننا پڑے گا تبھی تو اس سے سلب کلی حاصل ہوگا۔ اور ان کو عام نہ مانیں تو یہ سالیہ جزیہ بنے گا اور یہ درست نہیں ہے کھذا ثابت ہوا کہ نکمر وتحت ابھی عام ہوتا ہے۔ والكلمة التوحيد : یہ نکرہ تحت اھی کے عام ہونے کی دوسری دلیل ہے کہ کلمہ توحید ہے لا الہ الا للہ۔ اس میں الہ نکرہ ہے تحت ابھی ہے اس لے یہ عام ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر یہ عام نہ ہوتو تمام غیر اللہ کے الہ ہونے کی نفی نہیں ہوگی بلکہ بعض کی نفی ہوگی بعض کی نفی نہیں ہوگی تو تو حید تحقیق نہیں ہو گی حالانکہ اس کلمہ سے مقصودی اللہ کی توحید کو بیان کرنا ہے۔ لھذا ثابت ہوا کہ نکرہ تحت الهی عام ہوتا ہے۔
( وَالنَّكِرَةُ فِي مَوْضِعِ الشَّرْطِ إِذَا كَانَ ) أَى الشَّرْطُ ( مُثْبَتًا عَامًا فِي طَرَفِ النَّفْيْ فَإِنْ قَالَ : إِنْ ضَرَبَت رَجُلًا فَكَذَا مَعْنَاهُ لَا أَضْرِبُ رَجُلا لِأَنَّ الْيَمِينَ لِلْمَنْعِ هُنَا اعْلَمُ أَنَّ الْيَمِينَ إِمَّا لِلْحَمْلِ أَو لِلْمَنْعِ فَفِى قَوْلِهِ إِن ضَرَبَت رَجُلًا فَعَبْدِى حُرٌّ اليَمِينُ لِلْمَنْعِ فَيَكُونُ كَقَوْلِهِ لا أَضَرِبُ رَجُلا فَشَرُطُ الْبِرِّ أَنْ لَا يَضُرِبَ أَحَدًا مِنْ
Generality of the indefinite under negation. And among them is the indefinite noun in the position of negation, due to His saying, the Exalted: 'Allah has not sent down to any human being anything' (Quran 6:91). This is because the indefinite is coined for an indeterminate individual, and the negation of an indeterminate individual necessitates the negation of all individuals. One proof of the generality of the indefinite is that the Holy Quran says: 'They said, "Allah has not sent down to any human being anything."' This the Jews said, denying your prophethood. In response, Allah the Exalted said: 'Say, "Who sent down the Book which Moses brought?"' This verse is a particular affirmative proposition. Now we say that in the statement of the Jews, 'human being' and 'thing' are indefinite and are in the position of negation, so they are general. No specific human being or specific thing is meant; rather they are general over all human beings and things. The proof is that in response to their statement, the command of Allah the Exalted, 'Who sent down the Book which Moses brought?' is a particular affirmative which is made the contradictory of the Jews' statement. And it is clear that a particular affirmative is the contradictory of a universal negative, not of a particular negative. So here, the command of Allah the Exalted can only be a response to their statement if their statement is considered a universal negative. And if we consider it a universal negative, then we must consider 'human being' and 'thing' in the verse as general. Only then will universal negation be obtained. And if we do not consider them general, it would be a particular negative, and that is not correct. Thus it is proven that the indefinite under negation is general. And the word of tawhid: This is the second proof of the generality of the indefinite under negation: the word of tawhid is 'La ilaha illa Allah' (There is no god but Allah). In it, 'god' (ilah) is indefinite under negation, thus it is general. Because if it were not general, the negation of all other than Allah as being gods would not be established; rather, only some would be negated and some not, so tawhid would not be established, whereas the purpose of this phrase is to express the oneness of Allah. Therefore, it is proven that the indefinite under negation is general. And the indefinite in the position of condition, if the condition is affirmative, it is general on the side of negation. If one says: 'If I hit a man, then such and such,' its meaning is 'I do not hit a man', because the oath here is for prevention. Know that the oath is either for motivation or for prevention. In his saying, 'If I hit a man, then my slave is free,' the oath is for prevention, so it is like his saying, 'I do not hit a man.' So the condition for being righteous is that he does not hit anyone from
Source pages p. 612

Commentary
This passage discusses the principle that an indefinite noun (nakirah) in the scope of negation (taht al-nafy) indicates generality. Two proofs are provided: First, the Quranic verse in which the Jews said 'Allah has not sent down to any human being anything' (a universal negative), and Allah's response asking who sent down the Book to Moses is a particular affirmative, which can only be the contradictory of a universal negative, indicating that the indefinite nouns 'a human being' and 'anything' are general. Second, the statement of tawhid 'La ilaha illa Allah' (There is no god but Allah) has the indefinite 'ilah' (god) under negation, and it must be general to negate all false gods. The passage then introduces a similar rule for indefinite nouns in conditional sentences when the oath is for prevention (like 'If I hit a man...' meaning 'I will not hit a man'), indicating that the indefinite is also general on the side of negation. The passage cuts off at the end, but it establishes that the indefinite in the condition is general in the same way.

Key Terms
نکرہ (nakirah): An indefinite noun that does not refer to a specific individual.
تحت النفی (taht al-nafy): In the scope of a negation operator, such as 'la' or 'ma'
سالہ کلیہ (saliyyah kulliyyah): A universal negative proposition (e.g., 'no man is...')
موجبه جزئیہ (mujibah juz'iyyah): A particular affirmative proposition (e.g., 'some man is...')
کلمہ توحید (kalimat al-tawhid): The phrase 'La ilaha illa Allah' (There is no god but Allah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the indefinite noun 'ilah' in 'La ilaha illa Allah' considered general?
A) Because it is a singular noun.
B) Because it is under negation and must negate all gods to establish tawhid.
C) Because it is defined with alif lam.
D) Because it is in a conditional sentence.

Key Takeaway
An indefinite noun under negation is general, as proven by the logical contradiction in Quran 6:91 and the necessity of tawhid.

Generality of Indefinite in Positive Condition and Qualified Indefinite
Explaining generality of indefinite in condition and qualified indefinite

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why in Hanafi usul an indefinite noun in a positive condition becomes general on the negation side, and apply the same reasoning to a qualified indefinite noun to derive generality from the cause.

Core Idea
An indefinite in a positive condition is general on negation; a qualified indefinite is general because the attribute is a general cause.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih explores two related rules concerning generality derived from indefinite nouns. The first deals with indefinite nouns in conditional oaths, and the second with indefinite nouns qualified by a general attribute. Both rules, grounded in Quranic usage, lead to the conclusion that such indefinites indicate generality in Hanafi usul. The passage also addresses an objection that a qualified indefinite should be specific, offering a nuanced response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first rule
Locate the statement about indefinite in a positive condition. Observe how the author explains that when a condition is positive (e.g., 'if I strike a man'), the oath is interpreted as a prohibition, making the indefinite general on the side of negation.
This rule distinguishes between positive and negative conditions.
2
Identify the second rule
Find the phrase 'وكذا النكرة الموصوفة بصفة عامة' and note that it is connected to the first rule by 'وكذا' (likewise). The author gives an example: 'I do not sit except with a learned man' and says it is general.
The key is that the attribute must be general, not specific.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof for the second rule
Examine how the author cites Quranic verses (2:221, 2:263) using indefinite nouns with general attributes (believing slave, kind word) in a context of causation (ta'lil) for a general prohibition. Understand that if the cause were not general, the ruling would not be sound.
This establishes the link between generality of the attribute and generality of the ruling.
4
Study the objection and response
Read the objection: a qualified indefinite is restricted, hence specific. The response: it is specific compared to the absolute but general over all individuals containing that qualification.
This clarifies the dual nature: khass min wajh, 'amm min wajh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التَّرُويْحُ لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيحِ وَالتَّلُويْحِ
الرِّجَالِ فَيَكُونُ لِلسَّلْبِ الْكُلّى فَيَكُونُ عَامَّا فِي طَرَفِ النَّفْيِ ، وَإِنَّمَا قُيْدَ بِقَوْلِهِ إِذَا كَانَ الشَّرْطُ مُثْبَتًا حَتَّى لَوْ كَانَ الشَّرُطُ مَنْفِيًّا لَا يَكُونُ عَامَّا كَقَوْلِهِ إِنْ لَمْ أَضْرِبْ رَجُلًا فَعَبْدِي حُرِّ فَمَعْنَاهُ أَضْرِبُ رَجُلًا فَشَرُطُ الْبِرِّ ضَرْبُ أَحَدٍ مِنْ الرِّجَالِ فَيَكُونُ لِلْإِيجَابِ الْجُزْئِيِّ .
( وَكَذَا النَّكِرَةُ الْمَوْصُوفَةُ بِصِفَةِ عَامَّةٍ ) عِنْدَنَا نَحْو لَا أُجَالِسُ ، إِلَّا رَجُلًا عَالِمًا فَلَهُ أَنْ يُجَالِسَ كُلَّ عَالِمٍ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ) وَلَعَبْدٌ مُؤْمِنٌ خَيْرٌ مِنْ مُشْرِك ) وَقَوْلٌ مَعْرُوفٌ خَيْرٌ مِّنْ صَدَقَةٍ الْآيَةَ ، وَإِنَّمَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى الْعُمُومِ لِأَنَّهُ فِي مَعْرَضِ التَّعْلِيلِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَلَا تَنْكِحُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ حَتَّى يُؤْمِنُوا ، وَهَذَا الْحُكْمُ عَامٌ ، وَلَوْ لَمْ تَكنُ الْعِلَّةُ المَذْكُورَةُ عَامَّةً لَمَا صَحَ التَّعْلِيلُ
وَلَانَّ النِّسْبَةَ إِلَى الْمُشْتَقِّ تَدُلُّ عَلَى عِليَّةِ الْمَأْخَذِ فَكَذَا النِّسْبَةُ إِلَى الْمَوْصُوفِ بِالْمُشْتَقِّ لِأَنَّ قَوْلَهُ لَا أُجَالِسُ إِلَّا عَالِمًا مَعْنَاهُ إِلَّا رَجُلًا عَالِمًا فَيَعُمُ لِعُمُومِ الْعِلَّةِ ، فَإِنَّ قَوْلَهُ لَا أُجَالِسُ إِلَّا عَالِمًا لِعُمُومِ الْعِلَّةِ ، وَمَعْنَاهُ لَا أُجَالِسُ إِلَّا رَجُلا عَالِمًا فَإِنْ أَظْهَرُنَا الْمَوْصُوفَ ، وَهُوَ الرَّجُلُ ، وَنَقُولُ لَا أُجَالِسُ إِلَّا رَجُلا عَالِمًا كَانَ عَامَّا أَيْضًا .
) فَإِن قِيلَ النَّكِرَةُ الْمَوْصُوفَةُ مُقَيَّدَةٌ ، وَالْمُقَيَّدُ مِنْ أَقْسَامِ الْخَاصٌ قُلْنَا هُوَ خَاصٌ مِنْ وَجْهِ ، وَعَامٌ مِنْ وَجْهِ) أَى خَاصٌ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى الْمُطْلَقِ الَّذِي لَا يَكُونُ فِيهِ ذَلِكَ الْقَيْدُ عَامٌ فِي إِفْرَادِ مَا يُوجَدُ فِيهِ ذَلِكَ الْقَيْدُ .
The Tavrih for solving Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih. ... becomes for total negation, so it becomes general on the side of negation. And it is only restricted by his statement: when the condition is positive, such that if the condition were negative it would not be general, like his saying: 'If I do not strike a man, then my slave is free' – its meaning is 'I will strike a man', so the condition for fulfilling the oath is striking one of the men, so it is for particular affirmation. (And likewise the indefinite noun qualified by a general attribute) according to us, like 'I do not sit except with a learned man' – so he may sit with every learned person for His statement: 'And a believing slave is better than a polytheist' and 'a kind word is better than charity' – the verse. And it only indicates generality because it is in the context of causation for His statement: 'Do not marry polytheists until they believe' – and this ruling is general. And if the mentioned cause were not general, the causation would not be sound. And because attribution to the derivative indicates the causality of the basis, so too attribution to the thing qualified by the derivative. For his statement 'I do not sit except with a learned person' means 'except a learned man', so it is general due to the generality of the cause. Indeed his statement 'I do not sit except with a learned person' is for the generality of the cause, and its meaning is 'I do not sit except with a learned man'. If we make explicit the qualified term, which is 'man', and say 'I do not sit except with a learned man', it would also be general. If it is said: 'The qualified indefinite is restricted, and the restricted is among the types of the specific', we say: 'It is specific in one respect and general in another' – meaning specific relative to the absolute that does not contain that restriction, general with respect to all individuals that contain that restriction.
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih discusses two rules about indefinite nouns (nakira) and generality ('umum). First, an indefinite noun in the position of a condition (shart) that is positive (muthbat) becomes general on the side of negation (taraf al-nafy). For example, if one swears 'If I strike a man (rajulan), then such-and-such', the oath is a prohibition, meaning 'I will not strike a man (la adribu rajulan)'. The indefinite 'rajulan' is in the scope of negation, so it becomes general, covering any man. If the condition were negative (e.g., 'If I do not strike a man'), it would be particular because it implies a positive action. Second, an indefinite noun qualified by a general attribute (nakira mawsufa bi sifa 'amma) is considered general (in Hanafi usul). For example, 'I do not sit except with a learned man (illa rajulan 'aliman)' or 'except a learned person (illa 'aliman)' – this allows sitting with any learned person. The proof is Quranic: 'And a believing slave is better than a polytheist' (2:221) and 'a kind word is better than charity' (2:263), which use indefinite nouns with general attributes to indicate generality. This is because these verses are in the context of providing a cause ('illa) for a general ruling: the prohibition of marrying polytheists until they believe. If the cause (the attribute of being a believing slave or a kind word) were not general, the causation would not be sound. Similarly, attributing a ruling to a derivative (like 'alim) indicates that the attribute is the cause, and if the attribute is general, the ruling applies to all individuals possessing it. The passage then addresses an objection: a qualified indefinite is restricted (muqayyad) and thus falls under specific (khass). The response is that it is specific in one respect (compared to the absolute) but general in another (it applies to all individuals having that qualification). For example, 'learned man' is specific compared to 'man' but general over all learned men.

Key Terms
النكرة (al-nakira): An indefinite noun that does not specify a particular individual.
الشرط المثبت (al-shart al-muthbat): A positive condition (not negated) in a conditional oath or statement.
النكرة الموصوفة بصفة عامة (al-nakira al-mawsufa bi sifa 'amma): An indefinite noun qualified by a general attribute (e.g., 'a learned man').
عام (amm): A term that covers all individuals of its category without restriction.
خاص (khass): A term that is specific, not covering all individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul rule in this passage, an indefinite noun qualified by a general attribute (e.g., 'a learned man') is considered:
A) Specific (khass) because the qualification restricts it.
B) General (amm) because the attribute is general and functions as a cause.
C) Mutlaq (absolute) because the indefinite itself is unrestricted.
D) Mujmal (ambiguous) because of the qualification.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, an indefinite noun in a positive condition becomes general on the negation side, and an indefinite qualified by a general attribute is general because the attribute serves as a general cause.

Nakira in Positive Conditional: Generality on the Side of Negation
Rule and explanation of nakira in conditional oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a nakira in a positive conditional becomes general in negation, and distinguish this from a negative conditional where the nakira remains particular.

Core Idea
A nakira in a positive conditional is general in negation; in a negative conditional, it remains particular.

This lesson explores how the Hanafi school interprets indefinite nouns (nakira) when they appear in conditional clauses within oaths. The key insight is that the positivity or negativity of the condition determines whether the nakira has general or particular scope. This principle is essential for determining oath violation in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition type
Look at the conditional sentence and determine whether the condition is stated positively (e.g., 'if I strike a man') or negatively (e.g., 'if I do not strike a man'). This is the first and most critical step.
The condition type directly determines the nature of the oath and the scope of the nakira.
2
Determine the oath nature
In Hanafi usul, a positive condition indicates that the oath is one of refraining (man‘), while a negative condition indicates that the oath is one of urging (ḥathth). This classification comes from the understanding that the condition and consequent together form an oath.
This step relies on the principle that oaths can be either for urging or refraining.
3
Analyze the nakira scope
If the oath is for refraining (positive condition), the nakira becomes general on the side of negation. If the oath is for urging (negative condition), the nakira remains particular.
This is the core ruling: generality in negation applies only when the condition is positive.
4
Apply to examples from the text
Work through the two examples: (1) 'If I strike a man, then such-and-such' – positive condition → general in negation → any strike violates. (2) 'If I do not strike a man, then my slave is free' – negative condition → particular → striking one man fulfills the oath.
Notice how the same nakira ('a man') yields different results based on the condition's positivity.
5
Contrast with other madhhabs
Other schools (e.g., Shafi‘i) generally treat nakira as particular in conditional contexts unless there is contextual evidence for generality. Understanding this difference highlights the uniqueness of the Hanafi position.
This step is important for comparative fiqh and for understanding the basis of the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نکرہ کے موضع شرط میں واقع ہونے کا حکم

تشریح:- والنكرة في موضع الشرط:۔ یہاں سے یہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ نکرہ اگر تحت الشرط واقع ہو اور شرط بھی مثبت ہو تو یہ نکرہ بھی عام ہوتا ہے جانب نفی میں۔ یعنی شرط میں جس شی ء کا اثبات تھا اس کی نفی کی جانب میں یہ نکرہ عام ہو جائے گا مثلا اگر آدمی یہ کہے کہ ان ضربت رجلا فلذا ۔ تو اس کا مطلب ہے لا اضرب رجلا ۔ تو جب یہ لا اضرب رجلا کے معنی میں ہے تو اس میں نکرہ تحت ابھی واقع ہونے کی وجہ سے عام ہوگا اور اس نکرہ میں عام ہونے کی دلیل کیا ہے؟ اس سے پہلے یہ سمجھیں کہ شرط اور جزا یمین کے معنی میں ہوتے ہیں اور یمین کبھی تو ابھارنے کیلئے ہوتی ہے اور کبھی اپنے آپ کو کسی کام سے منع کرنے کیلئے ہوتی ہے۔ اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ شرط اگر مثبت ہو تو یہ یمین منع کیلئے ہوگی اور اگر شرط منفی ہو تو یہ کسی کام کے کرنے پر ابھارنے کیلئے ہوگی۔ اب دلیل سمجھیں کہ ہم نے یہ کہا کہ شرط مثبت ہو اور اس کے تحت نکرہ واقع ہو تو یہ عام ہوتا ہے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جب شرط مثبت ہو تو یہ ایسی یمین ہوتی ہے جو منع کیلئے ہوتی ہے مثلاً ان ضربت رجلا فلذا میں سیمین منع کیلئے ہے جب منع کیلئے ہے تو یہ لا اضرب رجلا کے معنی میں ہے اور اس وقت یہ رجلا تحت ابھی واقع ہونے کی وجہ سے عام ہے اس لیے ان ضربت رجلاً لذا میں بھی رجلا عام ہو گا طرف نفی میں یعنی مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ میں کسی آدمی کو بھی نہیں ماروں گا۔ تو اب اس کے بعد ایک آدمی کو مارنے سے بھی آدمی حانث ہو جائے گا۔

شرط کے لئے مثبت ہونے کی قید کا فائدہ

وانما قید بقولہ اذا کان الشرط منجا :۔ یہاں ہے یہ بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ نمرہ کے عام ہونے کیلئے ہم نے شرط کے مثبت ہونے کی شرط لگائی ہے یہ اس لیے ہے کہ اگر شرط منفی ہوئی ہو تو پھر نکر و عام نہیں ہوگا جیسے ان لم اضرب رجلا فعبدی تر یہاں شرط منفی ہے جس وجہ سے یمین ابھارتے کیلئے ہے تو گویا اس کا معنیٰ ہے اضرب رجلا اور اضرب رجلا میں رجلا عام نہیں ہے۔ لھذا اس شرط میں بھی نکرہ ( رجلا ) عام نہیں ہوگا۔ تو اب اگر وہ آدمی ایک آدمی کو مارے گا تو بری ہو جائے گا اور اس کا غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا یعنی یہ موجہ جزئیہ ہوگا۔
The ruling of the indefinite noun occurring in the position of the condition. Explanation: And the indefinite noun in the position of the condition: From here he is explaining that if the indefinite noun occurs under the condition and the condition is also positive, then this indefinite noun becomes general on the side of negation. That is, in the condition, regarding what was affirmed, on the side of its negation this indefinite noun becomes general. For example, if a man says, 'If I strike a man, then such-and-such [is due].' Its meaning is 'I will not strike a man.' So when it is in the meaning of 'I will not strike a man', then the indefinite noun becomes general due to occurring under [the category of] prohibition. And what is the proof of generality in this indefinite noun? Before that, understand that the condition and consequent are in the meaning of an oath, and an oath is sometimes to urge and sometimes to refrain from an action. And the second thing is that if the condition is positive, then this oath is for prohibition, and if the condition is negative, then it is for urging an action. Now understand the proof: we said that if the condition is positive and the indefinite noun occurs under it, then it becomes general. The reason is that when the condition is positive, this oath is for prohibition. For example, 'If I strike a man, then such-and-such' has an oath of prohibition. When it is for prohibition, it is in the meaning of 'I will not strike a man', and at that time this 'a man' is general due to occurring under [the category of] prohibition. Therefore, in 'If I strike a man, then such-and-such', 'a man' is general on the side of negation, meaning the intent is that I will not strike any man. So after this, if he strikes even one man, he will be considered as having violated the oath. And the benefit of the condition of the condition being positive: And he specified [the ruling] with his saying 'when the condition is positive'. Here he is explaining that for the generality of the indefinite noun we stipulated the condition of the condition being positive. This is because if the condition is negative, then the indefinite noun will not be general. For example, 'If I do not strike a man, then my slave is free.' Here the condition is negative, due to which the oath is for urging. So essentially its meaning is 'I will strike a man', and in 'I will strike a man', 'a man' is not general. Therefore, in this condition also the indefinite noun ('a man') is not general. So now if that man strikes one man, he will be absolved and his slave will not be freed; that is, it will be a particular affirmation.
Source pages p. 614

Commentary
This passage is a rule from usul al-fiqh regarding the generality of an indefinite noun (nakira) when it occurs in the position of a condition (shart) in an oath. The commentator expands on the matn from Al-Tawdih. The key point is that when the condition is positive (e.g., 'if I strike a man'), the oath is understood as a vow of refrain, so the indefinite noun becomes general on the side of negation: it means 'I will not strike any man'. Thus, striking any single man violates the oath. However, if the condition is negative (e.g., 'if I do not strike a man'), the oath is for urging an action, so the indefinite noun remains particular: striking one man fulfills the oath, and only striking that particular man (or men?) is required. The commentator clarifies that the ruling depends on the positivity or negativity of the condition. This is a typical Hanafi usul principle applied in the context of oaths and conditions.

Key Terms
نکرہ (nakira): An indefinite noun (e.g., rajulun 'a man') that is not made definite by al- or idafa.
موضع الشرط (mawdi' al-shart): The syntactic position of the condition in a conditional sentence (e.g., 'if X then Y').
یمین (yamin): An oath, which can be either for urging (ḥathth) or refraining (man').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man swears 'If I do not enter a house, my wife is divorced', then enters one house, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) His wife is divorced because he entered a house.
B) His wife is not divorced because the condition is negative and the nakira remains particular.
C) His wife is divorced only if he enters every house.
D) The oath is invalid because 'house' is indefinite.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on a nakira in a conditional oath depends on the positivity of the condition: positive gives generality in negation, negative leaves it particular.
